The basic data for a company code is straightforward (Figure 2.7). 

- In the same transaction, you can enter **address data**, displayed on official financial statements and other communications (Figure 2.8).

---

### 3. Adjust Global Parameters

The company code **global parameters** include essential assignments and decisions (Figure 2.9).

Key global parameters include:

- **Chart of Accounts:** Operating chart of accounts used by the company code, defining general ledger accounts.
- **Country Chart/Accounts:** Legal country-specific chart of accounts, linked one-to-one with operational chart accounts.
- **Company:** Smallest unit for which individual financial statements are created; a company can have multiple company codes.
- **Credit Control Area:** Area where customer credit is awarded and monitored; linked to credit segments in SAP Credit Management.
- **Fiscal Year Variant:** Defines the number of periods and fiscal year start/end dates.
- **Company Code Is Productive:** Indicator preventing accidental reset of transactional data.
- **Field Status Variant:** Groups several field status groups specifying document entry control.
- **Posting Period Variant:** Groups companies sharing the same period control for open periods.
- **Workflow Variant:** Defines workflow processes for the company code (e.g., parked document approvals).

After maintaining these settings, company code configuration is complete. 

- Changes are generally not advised after posting transactions.
- In test clients, transactional data can be wiped for further changes.

---

## 2.2.3 Company

A **company** generally depicts the **legal entity** according to local commercial law and is used for **intercompany transaction posting**.

- The company's financial statements form the basis for **consolidated financial statements**.
- All company codes assigned to a company must use the same **chart of accounts** and **fiscal year**.
- Typically, a separate company is created and assigned per company code.
- Companies can also be created for company codes outside SAP S/4HANA for external system consolidation.
- Companies are usually assigned a **company ID** in the **business partner master record** for intercompany transactions.
- Managing companies with **general ledger accounts** is an alternative.

### Creating a Company

- Defining a company organizational unit is **optional**.
- For consistent group accounting across several clients, companies must be maintained in each client.
- Company IDs must be consistent across the group and system.
- To create a company, enter:
  - A code (up to six alphanumeric characters)
  - Name
  - Address details
  - Language
  - Currency (Figure 2.10)

### Intercompany Transactions

- For transactions where an affiliate acts as supplier or customer, create the affiliate as a **business partner**.
- Maintain the **Trading Partner** field with the relevant company key (Figure 2.11).

---

## 2.2.4 Profit Center

**Profit centers** are considered master data but function like organizational units in accounting.

- Represent areas of responsibility for **profit calculations**, which have costs and revenues assigned.
- Typically represent organizational units such as:
  - Plants
  - Lines of Business (LoB)
  - Geographical locations
  - Combinations thereof
- Profit centers are assigned to a **standard hierarchy** within a special type of profit center group.

### Managing Profit Center Hierarchies

- Managed using the **Manage Global Accounting Hierarchies** app (Figure 2.12).
- Within the app, create **hierarchy nodes** (text elements) on various levels.
- Assign profit centers to the respective nodes as needed (Figure 2.13).

---

## 2.2.5 Segment

**Segments** are used as a dimension for **reporting purposes**.

- When creating a segment, assign an alphanumeric code (up to 10 characters) and a description (Figure 2.14).
- Organizationally, segments are positioned **one level above profit centers**.
- Multiple profit centers can be assigned to the same segment.

## Segment Reporting

Segment reporting was introduced to fulfill reporting requirements on financial statements for certain accounting principles such as **International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS)** and **US generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP)**.

A user in the **SAP S/4HANA** system won’t generally manually enter the segment during posting because the **segment** will be derived from the **profit center**.

Because the **profit center** is highly integrated with other account assignments in the system, it provides for great derivation flexibility. In combination with **document splitting**, segments are posted on all lines.

---

## 2.2.6 Functional Area

The **functional area** classifies the expenses of an organization by function, such as **administration, sales and distribution, marketing, production, research and development (R&D)**, and so on.

This classification is designed to cover the requirements of **cost of sales accounting**. In contrast, **standard period accounting** categorizes expenses based on their origin (e.g., personnel cost, depreciation, travel expenses).

In either accounting view, the operating results are the same in total.

When defining a **functional area**, you enter a four-character alphanumeric key and the name of the functional area (Figure 2.15).

---

## 2.2.7 Business Area

A **business area** is an organizational unit within accounting that represents a separate area of operations or responsibilities in a business organization.

When defining a **business area**, you enter a four-character alphanumeric key and the name of the business area, as shown in Figure 2.16.

**Business areas** aren’t very flexible account assignment objects and aren’t part of the **SAP Best Practices** for **SAP S/4HANA**. They aren’t discussed further in this book, and further details aren’t in scope for the certification.

---

## 2.3 Integration with Non-Financial Accounting Organizational Units

As shown in Figure 2.17, **financial accounting** integrates with several other functionalities by assigning the **company code** to the relevant organizational units of these functionalities in **SAP S/4HANA Customizing**.

These non-financial accounting organizational units include those for **controlling, logistics,** and **human resources management** (see the schematic client-level diagram in Figure 2.18).

---

## 2.3.1 Integration with Controlling

For the **financial accounting** modules, the most significant assignment is with the **controlling area**.

In **SAP S/4HANA**, especially, the integration between **financial accounting** and **controlling** almost blurs the line of where one starts and the other ends.

On the organizational unit level, the **controlling area** can be assigned to a single company code or multiple company codes.

To assign a company code to a controlling area, the following conditions must be met:

- The **fiscal year variant** must be identical.  
  In **SAP S/4HANA**, it’s not enough for the variants to have the same number of normal periods; the variants must have the exact same code (e.g., **K4**).  
  If you’re dealing with a migration, you always align the fiscal year variant to the one with the most special periods; therefore, if a company code had **K2** and a controlling area **K4**, you would change the assignment of the company code to **K4**.

- The **operating chart of accounts** must be identical.  
  The **P&L general ledger accounts** that are relevant for management accounting (primary cost/revenue general ledger accounts) are used in controlling, where they’re named **primary cost elements**.  
  In addition, the **secondary cost elements**, which are used for allocation between controlling objects, are created as **secondary cost general ledger accounts**.

**Tip:**  
The difference in naming between cost accounts in the general ledger and cost elements in controlling is an artifact of the legacy naming coming from **SAP ERP**, rather than a decision by SAP to confuse you.

It makes sense to use cross-company-code cost accounting when you want to:

- Perform reporting across company codes  
- Use internal allocations across company code boundaries

Through the company code assignment to the controlling area, the company code is also assigned indirectly to the **operating concern**.

The **operating concern** is the organizational unit of **profitability analysis (CO-PA)**.

There are two types of profitability analysis:

- **Costing-based**  
- **Account-based**

The most innovative option in **SAP S/4HANA** and the one most relevant to understand for financial accounting consultants is **account-based CO-PA**.

In this case, the CO-PA characteristics act essentially as additional account assignments for the **P&L accounts** of the general ledger and can be reported on through financial accounting reports.

---

## 2.3.2 Integration with Logistics

You can see many integration points for **logistics modules** in Figure 2.18.

A **plant** is an organizational unit that divides an enterprise according to **production, procurement, maintenance**, and **materials planning**.

At a plant, either materials are produced or goods and services are provided.

The **plant assignment to the company code** is the main requirement for integration of financial accounting with logistics components such as:

- Materials management  
- Sales and distribution  
- Warehouse management  
- Plant maintenance  

Proper functionality of the system is ensured when the plants assigned to a company code are in the same country as the company code.

In logistics assignments, you link a **company code** to a **sales organization**.

A **sales organization** is responsible for selling materials and services.

The assignment establishes a link between the sales and distribution functionality and financial accounting.

A sales organization is assigned to a single company code.

Finally, you can assign a **purchasing organization** to a company code.

The **purchasing organization** is responsible for all purchasing activities of an organization, such as purchase requests and order processing.

The purchasing organization is integrated within the organizational structure as follows:

- **Several company codes**  
  A purchasing organization can be assigned to several company codes—for example, for corporate group-wide purchasing.

- **One company code**  
  A purchasing organization can be assigned to one company code; in this case, you perform company-specific purchasing.

- **No company codes**  
  A purchasing organization can be assigned to no company codes. Because the plant is assigned to a company code in any case, the purchasing organization can be determined by the plant at the time of each procurement transaction.

---

## 2.3.3 Integration with SAP ERP Human Capital Management

The **personnel area** is the highest-level organizational unit in **SAP ERP HCM**.

A personnel area is organized according to aspects of **personnel, time management**, and **payroll**.

You allocate each personnel area to one company code so that when you create a personnel number, the company code is directly assigned to it.

---

## 2.4 Master Records

In the general ledger, the **master records** include **general ledger accounts** and **profit centers**.

**General ledger accounts** record all business transactions that concern the **balance sheet** and **income statement**.

All general ledger accounts are assigned to the company code through the **chart of accounts**.

**Profit centers** are master records that are defined in financial accounting but are integrated into many components, especially management accounting, because profit centers are defined per **controlling area**.

---

## 2.4.1 Chart of Accounts

The **chart of accounts** in an **SAP S/4HANA** system contains a list of **general ledger accounts**, as shown in Figure 2.19.

Basic information for a general ledger account (e.g., the name) is maintained on the **chart of accounts level**.

There are three basic types of charts of accounts:

- **Operational chart of accounts**  
  This required chart of accounts contains the accounts used for transactions and is assigned to the company code in the global parameters.

- **Country or alternative chart of accounts**  
  This optional chart of accounts contains accounts that map one to one to the operational accounts and is usually used to report according to local legal standards.  
  This chart of accounts is used when issuing financial statements to country authorities.  
  This is also assigned to the company code in the global parameters.

- **Group chart of accounts**  
  This optional chart of accounts contains the accounts used on the group level.  
  You can assign many operational accounts to a single group account, but not the other way around.  
  In other words, you generally have fewer accounts in the group chart of accounts than the operational chart of accounts.  
  The group chart of accounts is assigned to the operational chart of accounts, not the company code.  
  When the group chart of accounts is used, each operational account must be assigned to a group account.

---

## 2.4.2 Creating a Chart of Accounts

When you want to create a **chart of accounts**, you can create a new empty chart of accounts or copy an existing one, as shown in Figure 2.20.

The following settings are used when creating a **chart of accounts**:

- **Chart of Accts./Description**  
  This is a four-digit alphanumeric code and a text description.

- **Maint. Language**  
  All accounts must be maintained in the defined maintenance language.  
  By default, other languages are optional, but if you use the same chart of accounts for legal reporting in another language, all accounts should be translated to the local language.

- **Length of G/L Account Number**  
  This is the maximum length allowed for a general ledger account.  
  This setting is further refined in the account group definition.

- **Group Chart of Accts.**  
  Enter the group chart of accounts connected to the operational chart of accounts.

- **Blocked**  
  When active, this checkbox blocks the accounts in the chart of accounts from being assigned to a company code.  
  This won’t affect accounts already assigned before this indicator was set.  
  It’s generally used when you’re still building up the chart of accounts and aren’t sure of the final accounts in it.

---

## 2.4.3 Account Groups

The **account groups** categorize **general ledger accounts** according to their purpose.

All general ledger accounts are assigned to an account group based on how the accounts are used when posted to.

The **account group** of an account determines:

- The fields available for entry in the company code segment of the general ledger account  
- The number range an account can be created in

## Common Account Groups for General Ledger Accounts

The **common account groups** for general ledger accounts include:

- **Fixed asset accounts**
- **Material accounts**
- **Cash accounts**
- **Bank accounts**
- **Customer and vendor general ledger accounts**
- **Miscellaneous general ledger accounts**
- **P&L accounts**

In **Figure 2.21**, you define **account groups** per **chart of accounts 1**. For each account group, you enter a **four-digit code**, a **name**, and a **range of accounts**. Double-clicking on a line opens a screen showing the **seven field groups** available per general ledger account 2.

Drilling down further reveals the **field definition per field group**, where you define the **field status** for each available field. The field groupings are defaulted in the system. The **field status 3** can be adjusted in the following ways:

- **Suppress**  
  The field isn’t shown and can’t be entered on the screen.  
- **Req. Entry**  
  The field must be filled.  
- **Opt. Entry**  
  The field can be filled.  
- **Display**  
  The field is shown on the screen, but the values can’t be changed.

The **Account Currency** and **Field Status Group** fields are always marked as **required**; you cannot create an account without indicating values for these fields.

### Warning

Setting a field to **Suppress** or **Display** doesn’t mean the field has no value. If the field status changes — for example, from **Opt. Entry** to **Suppress** — and the field previously had an entry, this entry remains valid.  

You can also set the field status **per action** (create, change, display). For example, you can set a field as **required** when creating an account and **display** when changing it, meaning the field cannot be changed afterwards.

When conflicting field statuses exist, the system uses the status with the highest priority according to this list (from highest to lowest):

1. **Suppress**
2. **Display**
3. **Required**
4. **Optional**

---

## 2.4.4 Maintaining General Ledger Accounts

General ledger account data is maintained on three levels:

- **General chart of accounts level**
- **Company code level**
- **Controlling area level**

### Chart of Account Maintenance Level

At this level, you enter the **general ledger account number** (can be alphanumeric). You then select the **general ledger account type** from the following five types:

- **Balance sheet account**  
  For any account that isn’t a P&L account.  
- **Primary costs or revenue**  
  For P&L accounts reflecting normal operating costs and revenues; integrated with controlling.  
- **Secondary costs**  
  For accounts used for internal cost allocations in controlling.  
- **Nonoperating expense or income**  
  For P&L accounts reflecting gains/losses from non-core activities (e.g., asset sale profits); not integrated with controlling.  
- **Cash account**  
  New in **SAP S/4HANA 2020**. For this account, you must specify one of the following **general ledger subtypes** (see **G/L Account Subtype** in **Figure 2.22**):  
  - **B** (bank reconciliation account)  
  - **P** (petty cash)  
  - **S** (bank subaccount)

In **Figure 2.23**, an example shows the complete details for the **chart of account segment** of an expense general ledger account. You assign the account to the relevant **account group**, and the system checks if the account number falls within the defined range. Then, you enter a **short and long description** in the maintenance language of the chart of accounts.

If you’ve assigned a **group chart of accounts**, you must also enter the relevant **group account**. Optionally, you can assign a **functional area** for cost of sales accounting and a **trading partner** for consolidation purposes.

### P&L Account Maintenance

If creating a **P&L account**, you indicate the **P&L statement account type** (see **P&L Statmt acct type** column in **Figure 2.24**). This assignment indicates the **retained earning account** the values will be carried forward to at year-end.

You maintain the **retained earning account** per P&L statement account type in **Customizing**. At least one value must be maintained. If only one value exists in Customizing, then for any P&L general ledger account created, the **P&L statement account type** is assigned automatically.

### Company Code Level Maintenance

At the company code level, you enter fields defined by the assigned **account group**. **Figure 2.25** shows some fields maintained at this level, noting that requirements vary by account.

Critical fields on the company code level include:

- **Account Currency**  
  Matching the company code currency allows posting in any currency. A different currency restricts posting to that currency (e.g., foreign currency bank account).  
- **Tax Category**  
  Indicates the tax codes valid for posting to the account. Options include input tax, output tax, specific tax code, allow any tax, or no tax (blank). The **Posting Without Tax Allowed** checkbox permits posting without a tax code, though this is risky and zero-percent tax codes are recommended instead.  
- **Alternative Account Number**  
  Enter the relative account from the local chart of accounts. Selecting an already-used account triggers an error.  
- **Reconciliation Account for Account Type**  
  Reconciliation accounts show general ledger views of subledger accounting systems. For example, postings to vendor account 12345 are also posted automatically to general ledger account 21100000. The general ledger account cannot be posted to directly. Use this field to specify if the account is a **reconciliation account** for assets, customers, vendors, or contract account receivables.  
- **Open Item Management**  
  Activated to track offsetting postings; items are either **open** or **cleared**. The account balance equals the balance of open items. This indicator can be changed only for accounts with zero balance. In **SAP S/4HANA**, open items can be managed per ledger using the **Ledger Group-Specific Clearing** checkbox.  
- **Sort Key**  
  Determines the system proposal for the **Allocation field** on document line items. It can be changed manually. Transferable values include posting date, document number, vendor number, and others. Many sort keys are delivered by default; custom ones can also be created.  
- **Field Status Group**  
  Defines the field status for account assignments during posting (e.g., cost center required, profit center optional). There are many standard-delivered field status groups and the option to define custom groups. Examples include cost accounts, bank accounts (with obligatory value date), material accounts, and revenue accounts.

---

## 2.4.5 Primary Cost and Revenue Accounts and Secondary Cost Accounts

For **primary cost and revenue accounts** and **secondary cost accounts**, controlling data must also be maintained.

- Assignment to the **controlling area** is provided through the company codes assigned to the account.
- You must maintain the **cost element category**.

For **primary cost and revenue accounts**, select whether the account depicts **costs** or **revenues** (cost element categories **1** and **11**).

For **secondary cost accounts**, select the type of internal controlling allocations used, e.g., **assessments**, **settlements**, **internal activity allocations** (see **Figure 2.26**).

There is a single exception for balance sheet accounts integrated into controlling. For statistical reasons, **asset reconciliation** and **material accounts** can also be cost elements:

- For **asset accounts**, general ledger accounts must be **reconciliation accounts** included in relevant account determinations for asset accounting.
- For **material accounts**, they must be assigned to the **materials management account determination**.

You can then select the indicator to apply the account assignments **statistically** (see **Figure 2.27** for the asset reconciliation account **Machinery & Equipment**).

---

## 2.4.6 Profit Centers

In the **SAP ERP system** with classic general ledger accounting, **profit centers** were purely controlling objects in a separate submodule.

With the introduction of the **new general ledger**, the profit center became more important in **financial accounting** because it is the object used to fulfill requirements for **segment reporting**.

The profit center was designated for this role because it is an **account assignment** already integrated into most other system components.

### Derivation of Profit Centers and Segments

**Figure 2.28** shows ways the **profit center** is derived during posting. Some options allow for direct assignment of the **segment**. Segments should ideally be derived by the profit center, though alternative assignment methods exist for cases where automatic derivation is not possible.

### Profit Center Hierarchy

First, design the **profit center hierarchy**. All profit centers in the client are assigned to a **profit center hierarchy**, which is assigned to the **controlling area** in **Customizing** (see **Figure 2.29**).

This means all company codes assigned to the controlling area can potentially post to the profit center.

In the second step, **assign profit centers** to the hierarchy. The hierarchy can be:

- **Flat**
- **Structured**

Structuring the hierarchy into **groups and subgroups** facilitates selection during **reporting**, **planning**, and other processes. **Figure 2.30** shows a hierarchy structured into groups.

## Profit Center Creation and Assignment

When you create a **profit center**, you select the **controlling area** and then assign the **company codes** the profit center is valid for, as shown in **Figure 2.31**. You must assign the profit center to the **hierarchy** by indicating the **profit center group** it belongs to. You also maintain the relevant **segment** to be derived from the profit center.

After entering the data, you **activate the profit center** and can then enter it during posting and assign it to other objects such as:

- Profit Center Segment  
- Production Order  
- Sales Order  
- Material  
- Fixed Asset  
- Cost Center  
- Internal Order  
- Project  
- Document  
- Substitution  
- Manual Entry  
- During Posting  
- General Ledger  
- Account Default  
- Account Assignment  
- General Ledger Document Entry  
- BAdI (ABAP Code)  
- Document Splitting  
- Constant  
- Field Assignment  

*© 2024 by Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)*

---

## 2.5 Global Financial Accounting Configuration

In this section, we look at **configuration options** that define system behavior and available functionalities in **financial accounting**. Topics covered include:

- **Parallel accounting**  
- Managing the **fiscal years**  
- Handling **currencies**  
- **Journal entries**  
- **Tax handling**  
- Explanation of **tolerance groups**

---

### 2.5.1 Parallel Accounting

**Parallel accounting**, also known as **parallel valuation**, is increasingly important for companies, especially **multinationals** and their subsidiaries. Reporting only local accounting principles is no longer sufficient in an increasingly global environment, even for nonconsolidated individual company codes.

#### Figure 2.32: Example of Parallel Accounting

For simplicity, two accounting principles are assumed, but this logic extends to more. Key points:

1. The **standard general ledger posting** posts the same amounts to the same accounts across all accounting principles. In **SAP S/4HANA**, a **single document** updates all areas.  
2. If different values are required for the same scenario across accounting principles, the recommended approach is to **post separate documents** for each accounting principle.  
3. For postings specific to certain accounting principles only, separate documents update only the **target accounting principles** without affecting others.

There are two basic approaches for mapping parallel accounting in **SAP S/4HANA**:

- **Ledger approach**  
- **Accounts approach**

The **ledger approach** is preferred for new customers. Customers converting from SAP ERP who were using the accounts approach can continue with it.

**Warning:**  
Currently, there is no way to move from the **accounts approach** to the **ledger approach** within an SAP S/4HANA system. Customers should implement the ledger approach in SAP ERP before converting or perform a new installation instead of a direct conversion.

Every SAP S/4HANA client has exactly one **leading ledger**. The standard predefined leading ledger for a client is **0L**, and all company codes in the client are assigned to this ledger. Additional standard ledgers can be defined as two-digit alphanumeric keys for other accounting principles.

Adding standard ledgers to a productive system requires a project and the use of the **Subsequent Implementation of a Further Accounting Principle Customizing** function. In nonproductive/new systems, defining a new standard ledger is straightforward via Customizing in Financial Accounting Global Settings (New).

---

### 2.5.2 Configuring Ledgers

**Figure 2.33** shows ledger settings at the client level, where you define:

- **Ledger code**  
- **Ledger name**  
- Whether a ledger is the **leading ledger**  
- **Ledger type** (standard or extension)  
- **Extension ledger type** (explained in the upcoming subsection)  
- **Underlying ledger** (for extension ledgers)  
- **Valuation view** (controls currency types assignable to company code/ledger)  
- **Subtype of valuation view** (used for transfer prices, detailed beyond this scope)  
- Whether **manual postings** are allowed or if the ledger is only for automatic postings  
- **Accounting principle** for the ledger if assigned at client level  

After creating the **client-level ledger settings**, define settings **per company code** as shown in **Figure 2.34**:

- **Fiscal Year Variant:** For nonleading standard ledgers; must match company code for the leading ledger.  
- **Posting Period Variant:** Enables independent period opening and closing for each ledger.  
- **Accounting Principle:** For the ledger in the company code (accounts approach only).  
- **Functional Currency:** Additional valuation currency beside local and group currency.  
- **Currency Type:** Currency types updated for the ledger, supporting up to 10 currency types per ledger.  
- **Parallel Accounting Using G/L Accounts:** Assigns multiple accounting principles to a ledger (accounts approach).  

---

### 2.5.3 Deactivating Ledgers

If a ledger activated for a company code is no longer valid, you can **deactivate the ledger** for that company code effective from a specified year. Rules for deactivation:

- Documents posted before or during the fiscal year remain on the ledger.  
- Documents posted after the specified fiscal year are no longer posted to the ledger.  
- Existing posting data remains for reporting, but data may be incomplete if deactivated mid-year.

**Warning:**  
Ledger deactivation is irreversible. To reactivate, you must define a new ledger and assign it as needed.

---

### 2.5.4 Ledger Group Definition

When a ledger is created, the system generates a **ledger group** named the same as the ledger. You can only change the group's name but cannot add more ledgers to this auto-generated group.

You can define **custom ledger groups** in Customizing with a four-character alphanumeric code and description (see **Figure 2.36**). These groups can include multiple ledgers and allow functions to operate on several ledgers simultaneously.

During posting, if the ledger group is left blank, the system processes **all standard ledgers**.

Each ledger group requires a **representative ledger**, which determines the posting period and its open/closed status during posting (see **Figure 2.37**). When the **leading ledger** is in the group, it must be set as the representative ledger.

**Warning:**  
During posting, all ledgers in a group are updated as long as the representative ledger’s posting period is open, even if other ledgers’ periods are closed.

---

### 2.5.5 Extension Ledgers

**Extension ledgers** in **SAP S/4HANA** add flexibility to posting and reporting in the general ledger. Previously, in SAP ERP, **Financial Accounting** and **Management Accounting** were separate with different tables, allowing independent postings and allocations.

With the **Universal Journal**, this separation no longer exists, so extension ledgers restore independence.

An **extension ledger** is an **add-on delta-logic ledger** assigned on top of an **underlying ledger** (which can be a standard or another extension ledger). You can post to extension ledgers without changing the underlying ledger’s values; the extension ledger reports a summary of the underlying and its own postings.

Data footprint is small since extension ledgers do not duplicate Universal Journal line items but keep their own separate lines.

## Extension Ledgers in SAP S/4HANA

In the **Customizing activity** where you define additional ledgers, you can select the **extension ledger type**. You then need to define the underlying ledger.

When you define an **extension ledger**, the system assigns it to a **ledger group** with the same name as the extension ledger. An extension ledger can’t be added to ledger groups manually, so only the group created automatically can include the extension ledger.

An extension ledger can be created at any time and doesn’t require migration or other data-related activities to be performed due to its **delta nature**.

### Extension Ledger Use Cases

Extension ledgers go beyond management accounting and can be used in **SAP S/4HANA systems** migrated or converted from SAP ERP systems that didn’t make use of multiple ledgers (classic general ledger systems or single ledger new general ledger configurations).

Common use cases include:

- Post into a closed period without changing legal reports.
- Perform manual allocations for management accounting.
- Perform postings to different accounts for consolidation.
- Post non-invoiced contracts as revenue to simulate numbers.
- Other scenarios covering specific business needs of accounting.

### Extension Ledger Types

There are **three extension ledger types** you can select depending on the use case:

- **Standard journal entries**  
  Similar to journal entries entered for any standard ledger, these are saved with document numbers. They can’t be directly deleted but must be reversed when required.

- **S - Line items with technical numbers / deletion possible**  
  Used for simulation purposes (e.g., simulating exchange rate differences). Journal entries are saved using technical numbers and can be deleted directly.

- **P - Line items with technical numbers / no deletion possible**  
  Supports journal entries for predictions and commitments. Predictive accounting reports sales order expected future revenues for analysis. Commitments track expenditures against budget. Entries are saved using technical numbers (no document numbers) and must be reversed when required.

> **Tip:**  
> These use cases are traditionally handled in management accounting. Adding these scenarios to the **Universal Journal** blurs the lines between management and financial accounting architecturally.

---

## 2.5.6 Accounts Approach

In the **accounts approach** to parallel valuation, you use a **single ledger** to map multiple accounting principles via separate sets of **general ledger accounts**.

- Differences in valuation (e.g., accruals, fixed assets, currency exchange) are handled by creating a closed system of accounts per accounting principle.
- This approach avoids doubling the total accounts in the chart of accounts.
- For manual transactions, post using accounting principle-specific accounts.
- For automatic transactions, maintain separate accounts in relevant account determinations per accounting principle.

Multiple ledgers can be assigned to a ledger with the **Parallel Accounting Using G/L Accounts** checkbox set.

Although typically handled in a single ledger (almost always the leading ledger), separate **ledger groups** per accounting principle are still maintained in SAP S/4HANA. Each ledger group has the same ledger assigned.

In new SAP S/4HANA systems, the **ledger approach** is recommended for parallel valuation. The accounts approach is reserved for systems converted from SAP ERP without the ledger approach.

---

## 2.5.7 Accounting Principles

**Accounting principles** are defined in **Customizing** with:

- A four-character alphanumeric code
- A description

The accounting principle object contains no direct rules or Customizing definitions.

Each accounting principle is assigned to a **ledger group**. Generally, there is a one-to-one assignment between ledger groups and accounting principles because every principle corresponds to specific legal or other requirements.

### Exception: Accounts Approach

When using the accounts approach to parallel valuation:

- The **Parallel Accounting Using G/L Accounts** indicator is checked.
- The same ledger group can be assigned to two separate accounting principles.
- Ledger groups containing an extension ledger can also be assigned to accounting principles.

---

## 2.5.8 Fiscal Year Variant

The **fiscal year variant** defines:

- Start and end dates of a fiscal year
- Division of the year into periods

It is assigned to the relevant **company codes** (and controlling areas). Variants are usually based on legal or company accounting requirements.

SAP S/4HANA delivers many **standard fiscal year variants** and allows creation of custom variants to fulfill any business case.

### Types of Fiscal Year Variants

- **Year-independent**: The fiscal year starts and ends on the same dates each year with the same number of periods.
- **Year-specific**: Defines different settings per year, e.g., for special needs like liquidation or acquisition. Often a shortened fiscal year with nonstandard start/end dates.

### Key Details

- Fiscal years based on the calendar year (January to December, 12 periods) are simplest and do not require period definitions.
- If fiscal year differs from calendar year, a **year shift** is defined in the period setup.
- Fiscal years can have more or fewer than 12 periods (e.g., one period per trimester).
- Period lengths can vary.
- **Special periods** are used during closing to allow postings after the fiscal year ends but before new year periods open.
- Up to **four special periods** are supported.
- Special periods can be opened or closed independently from normal periods.

---

## 2.5.9 Integration of Controlling with the General Ledger

In **SAP S/4HANA**, integration between **controlling** and **general ledger** is mandatory.

- Both share the same line-item table.
- Any posting in controlling also posts in the general ledger.
- Includes internal controlling postings using **secondary cost elements** defined as secondary cost general ledger accounts.
- Controlling account assignments from overhead cost controlling to profitability analysis update on the same line items, enabling unified reporting.

### Additional Points

- Controlling postings require a **document type**, often defined separately for controlling.
- Each controlling business transaction maps to a document type; all can be mapped to the same document type.
- For manual controlling transactions, users can enter document type and ledger group.
- For automated transactions, system uses document type and ledger group assignments as configured in Customizing.

---

## 2.5.10 Currencies

SAP S/4HANA is preconfigured with most world currencies assigned to **currency keys** per their **ISO codes**.

- You can set a **validity date** for a currency to prevent posting when the currency is obsolete.
- The system uses **exchange rate types** to handle different exchange rate ratios for various business cases such as legal valuation, internal/group valuation, and planning.
- Exchange rate types are assigned to currency types in Customizing.

### Exchange Rate Maintenance

- Translation ratios (how many units of one currency equal a unit of another) must be maintained periodically, often daily.
- Reports can upload exchange rate files or read real-time exchange rate feeds.
- To reduce complexity with hundreds of currency pairs, a **base currency** can be defined.
- Other currency exchange rates are derived from the base currency rates.

#### Example:

- EUR defined as base currency.
- Maintained rates:  
  - 1 EUR = 0.9 GBP  
  - 1 EUR = 1.1 USD  
- System deduces rate between GBP and USD automatically.

## Global Financial Accounting Configuration Section 2.5

### Exchange Rate Maintenance

If you maintain a specific **manual rate** for a combination of currencies, the system will use that; during posting, you can override the proposed values of **translation** and enter a manual translation rate.

You might come across the terms **direct quotation** or **indirect quotation**. These terms define how the **currency translation rate** is maintained:  

- With **direct quotation**, one unit of the **foreign currency** is translated to the **local currency**. For example, with **EUR** as the local currency, $1 buys €0.9.
- With **indirect quotation**, it’s the opposite: €1 buys $1.11.  

You define the standard entry as direct or indirect per currency pair.

The **SAP S/4HANA system** allows for currency maintenance using **worklists**, which are assigned to separate users for when a maintenance task is shared between employees. Using worklists allows multiple users to work on exchange rates at the same time (as long as they’re working on different worklists) and allows for better **authorization control** because specific worklists with specific currencies can be assigned to a user.

The system uses **currency types** to record different value amounts in the line-item tables. All **company codes** record values in the **company code currency**, defined based on legal requirements (the local currency where the company operates). In addition, the system records the **document currency** as well because this is required for auditing and legal reasons.

The fixed currency type assignment per company code includes:  
- **Global currency**: assigned to the controlling area  
- Additionally, up to eight currencies per ledger can be assigned, which the system can update and record during transaction processing.

#### Preconfigured Currency Types in SAP S/4HANA (Figure 2.48)

- **00**: Document Currency  
- **10**: Company Code Currency  
- **20**: Controlling Area Currency  
- **30**: Group Currency  
- **40**: Hard Currency  
- **50**: Index-Based Currency  
- **60**: Global Company Currency  
- **70**: Controlling Object Currency  

You can enhance these with your own types (e.g., **Z0** as a custom currency).

---

### 2.5.11 Document Types and Number Ranges

In **financial accounting**, the **document type** is used to group and categorize business transactions. The document type is entered in the document header and controls which accounts can be posted to.

The document type also defines the **number** the document is assigned when posting (or parking). **SAP S/4HANA** comes with predefined document types for most common business scenarios. You can define your own document types in **Customizing** as needed.

- Document types are defined on the **client level** and can be used directly when posting to all company codes, provided the **document number range** assigned to the document type is defined for the company code.
- A new document type is a **two-digit alphanumeric code** with a description.
- It is common to copy an existing document type covering a similar business case.

#### Important Document Type Settings (Figure 2.49)

- **Number range**: Defines numbers assigned to documents posting using the document type.
- **Reverse Document Type**: When reversing a document, the system uses this type for the reversal. If blank, it uses the original type.
- **Authorization Group**: Limits users able to post using the document type through role assignment.
- **Account types allowed**: Specifies which account types can use this document type, helping limit erroneous postings.
- **BI Only**: Allows limiting posting with the document type through batch processes (e.g., Excel uploads).
- **Exchange Rate Type for FC Documents**: Sets default exchange rate type proposed on document type selection; can be changed manually during posting.
- **Reference Number**: Document header text required during entry, can be marked as mandatory to remind users.
- **Net Document Type**: Used for vendor invoices; cash discounts are directly posted to discount accounts at invoice posting.
- **Cust/vend Check**: Ensures only a single customer or vendor is posted to in a document.
- **Negative Postings Permitted**: Allows reversal postings (explained later).
- **Inter-Company**: Allows posting cross-company-code documents with this document type.
- **Enter Trading Partner**: Allows manual entry of the partner company, often used with the Inter-Company checkbox.

---

### 2.5.12 Posting Keys

The **posting key** defines the **account type** of a line item and whether the line is a **debit** or **credit posting**.  

In SAP S/4HANA, the two-digit posting key is often a “hidden” attribute. Users select **debit** or **credit**, and the system automatically assigns the posting key based on the application. For example, in general ledger accounting:  
- **40**: Debit  
- **50**: Credit  

Posting keys are defined at the **client level**. It is recommended to use SAP-delivered posting keys which cover most business scenarios.

Other posting key definitions include:  
- Whether the posting key is relevant for **sales**  
- Whether it's used for **special general ledger transactions** for customers/vendors  
- Whether it is used for **payment transactions**  
- The reversal posting key for reversals.

Each posting key also defines the **field status**, although this is usually controlled by the **general ledger account field status group**. The field status options in order of priority are:  

1. **Suppress**  
2. **Display**  
3. **Required Entry (Req. Entry)**  
4. **Optional Entry (Opt. Entry)**  

#### Field Status Examples

- If a field is **required** at the account field status level but **hidden** in the posting key (or vice versa), an **error message** occurs during posting.
- If a field is **display only** at the account field status level but **hidden** in the posting key, the field remains hidden but is posted automatically if filled.

*Tip:* Usually, fields are set as optional in the posting key field status, and control occurs via the account field status group.

Certain fields’ status depends on other configuration, e.g.,  
- The **tax code** field is ready for input only if the account is marked as tax relevant.  
- **Profit center** and **segment** fields become required as specified in **document splitting**.

#### Posting Key Ranges and Account Types (Table 2.1)

| Debit Range | Credit Range | Account Type                                  |
|-------------|--------------|-----------------------------------------------|
| 01–09       | 11–19        | Customer                                      |
| 21–29       | 31–39        | Vendor/Supplier                               |
| 40          | 50           | General Ledger                                |
| 80–86       | 90–96        | General Ledger (Materials Management integration) |
| 70          | 75           | Asset                                         |
| 89          | 99           | Material                                      |

---

### 2.5.13 Tolerance Groups

Businesses apply rules for the **amounts** each employee is authorized to handle in various posting transactions.

The basic setting for accounts in **financial accounting** with SAP S/4HANA is the **tolerance group** (Figure 2.52).

The **tolerance group assigned to a user** defines four basic, **amount-related posting limits**:  

- **Maximum amount per document** (includes all debit and credit items)  
- **Maximum amount per open item** (does not apply to automatically created line items)  
- **Maximum cash discount percentage per line item**  
- **Maximum permitted payment differences allowed**, with separate amounts for **overpayments** and **underpayments**  

Tolerance amounts can be set differently for each company code.  

A **blank tolerance group** with common limits exists for all accounting employees and is assigned by default. Specific tolerance groups must be assigned manually to differentiate **user limits**.  

Only one tolerance group can be assigned to a user, which applies to all company codes the user can post in.

---

### 2.5.14 Tax Handling

**Taxes** are complex and vary by country legislation.

SAP S/4HANA performs the following tax-related functions:  

- **Calculates tax amounts** based on preconfigured rules  
- **Updates tax accounts** with calculated values  
- **Posts adjustments** to tax amounts for discounts and deductions  
- Outputs **required tax reporting forms** for tax authorities  

SAP S/4HANA handles the following tax types during posting:  

- **Value-added tax (VAT) or goods and services tax (GST)**  
  - This is an **indirect tax** imposed at every stage of production or service.  
  - Commonly levied on all incoming and outgoing invoices.  
  - Applied in most countries, including all **EU countries**.

## Sales Tax

**Sales tax** is the **percentage of revenue** imposed on the **retail sale of goods**.

## Withholding Tax

**Withholding tax** is commonly a tax the company **deducts from a payment to a person** and pays to the government directly. It acts as a **tax credit** for the person because the tax wasn’t paid to them directly.

- Other types of withholding tax include taxes levied on **income from securities**.

## Other Types of Tax

Legislations vary globally, and **SAP’s global software** must support all **local requirements**. **SAP S/4HANA** is often used with **external specialized tax software**, especially in areas with complex regulations or multiple jurisdiction combinations, such as the **United States**.

**SAP S/4HANA** comes with **preconfigured tax procedures** for every country (see Figure 2.53). Users can copy and modify these as required.

The settings maintained in the **tax procedure** (see Figure 2.54) define the **sequence of calculations** for the condition types (**tax types**).

- The **Account Key** is important for maintaining **account determination** so the system knows which accounts need posting.

---

### Legal Regulations for Tax Base Amount

Countries or jurisdictions define whether the **base tax amount** is either:

- **Net amount**: Tax is calculated on the posted amount **minus relevant discounts**.
- **Gross amount**: Tax is calculated on the **full amount regardless of discounts**. Adjustments occur in a second step.

---

### Tax Codes

During **document posting**, you enter a **tax code** on a line item to specify the **tax percentage**, **valid tax type**, and **account**. The tax code is a **two-character alphanumeric key**.

- Tax codes are defined at the **client level**, either by **country** or a combination of **country and jurisdiction code**.
- To create a tax code, use **Transaction FTXP** and copy an existing similar tax code.
- The system comes with **predefined tax codes** for many countries.

When defining tax codes, enter the valid **tax percentage rate** for specific tax types.

- When a new tax percentage is introduced, create a **new tax code** instead of changing an existing one.
- This preserves **historical accuracy** and manages the **percentage transition period**.

---

### Time-Dependent Tax (TDT) Calculation

Starting from **SAP S/4HANA Cloud 2008** (and planned for on-premise SAP S/4HANA 2021), you can select a **date range** for the validity of a specific tax percentage.

- When **TDT** is active, maintain **tax codes, rates, and properties** for specified time periods.
- This flexibility allows adjustments to **law changes** or **temporary tax relief** without creating new tax codes.

**Tip:**  
To avoid confusion, remove the **rate** from the description when maintaining tax codes for multiple validity periods. For example, instead of “I1 – 10% Input Tax Domestic”, use “I1 – Standard Input Tax Domestic”.

---

### Tax Account Determination

Selecting the **Tax accounts** button shows a window displaying the **tax account**.

- If the **account key** defined in the tax type allows only one account, the system sets it automatically.
- Otherwise, select the correct account from those allowed by account determination (see Figure 2.55).

---

### Posting Tax Accounts

The **tax type** defines whether the tax is posted into:

- A **separate line** (most common), or
- The tax amount is distributed to relevant **revenue or expense accounts** (e.g., certain nondeductible taxes).

### Tax Categories on General Ledger Accounts

General ledger accounts posted with tax must be marked as **input** or **output** tax accounts.

| Tax Category Field | Description                   |
|--------------------|-------------------------------|
| **Blank**          | Not tax-relevant              |
| **>**              | Output tax account            |
| **<**              | Input tax account             |
| **+**              | Relevant for output tax       |
| **-**              | Relevant for input tax        |
| **\***             | Relevant for all kinds of tax |
| **##**             | Specific tax code only        |

*(Table 2.2 Tax Categories on General Ledger Accounts)*

---

## 2.5.15 Analyzing Document Splitting

When posting a document to the **general ledger**, you enter data in the **header segment** with information valid for the whole document, then build up the **line items**.

- Different information is entered in each line item depending on the **account type** and **system configuration**.
- For example, a **cost center** would be entered for an **expense line**, but not for a **vendor or tax line**.

Because the **profit center** is derived from **controlling account assignments** (like the cost center), it is easy to assign **profit center** and **segment** on the **P&L level**.

However, for lines posted to **balance sheet accounts**, manual assignment of a **profit center** isn’t always simple or possible.

---

### Document Splitting Purpose

**Document splitting** allows the system to use amounts from lines where the profit center is entered or derived as **splitting rules** to assign the profit center proportionally to other lines.

---

### Example: Document Splitting

| Line Number | General Ledger Account | Description | Debit/Credit | Amount | Cost Center | Profit Center | Segment |
|-------------|-----------------------|-------------|--------------|--------|-------------|---------------|---------|
| 1           | Vendor C              |             |              | 1100   |             |               |         |
| 2           | Expense A             |             | Debit (D)    | 400    | CCA         | PCA           | SA      |
| 3           | Expense B             |             | Debit (D)    | 600    | CCB         | PCB           | SB      |
| 4           | Tax D                 |             |              | 100    |             |               |         |

*(Table 2.3 Invoice Document: Entry View)*

Without document splitting, vendor and tax lines remain unassigned for profit center and segment.

Activating document splitting adds lines splitting amounts proportionally:

| Line Number | General Ledger Account | Description | Debit/Credit | Amount | Cost Center | Profit Center | Segment |
|-------------|-----------------------|-------------|--------------|--------|-------------|---------------|---------|
| 1           | Vendor C              |             |              | 440    |             | PCA           | SA      |
| 2           | Vendor C              |             |              | 660    |             | PCB           | SB      |
| 3           | Expense A             |             | Debit (D)    | 400    | CCA         | PCA           | SA      |
| 4           | Expense B             |             | Debit (D)    | 600    | CCB         | PCB           | SB      |
| 5           | Tax D                 |             | Debit (D)    | 40     |             | PCA           | SA      |
| 6           | Tax D                 |             | Debit (D)    | 60     |             | PCB           | SB      |

*(Table 2.4 Invoice Document: General Ledger View)*

---

**The four lines** of Table 2.3 represent the **entry view** of the document, while Table 2.4 reflects the **general ledger view** with all splitting details.

---

### Tip

- The **general ledger view** is posted with all line items in the **Universal Journal table**.
- Assigning company codes to additional **standard ledgers** multiplies the number of line items.
- The six-digit **line-item field** allows up to **999,999 lines per document**.

---

### Document Splitting Activation

- Activated at the **client level** in Customizing for **general ledger accounting** (see Figure 2.56).
- Can be activated with a simple switch in a **greenfield system** (no postings).
- For existing systems, activating document splitting requires a project and implementation of **Customizing for Subsequent Implementation of Document Splitting**.
- Does **not require system downtime** but needs **good preparation**.

---

### Basic Settings When Activating Document Splitting

- **Document Splitting/Method**: Controls all splitting rules for business transactions; default SAP settings generally suffice.
- **Inheritance**: Transfers account assignments to lines when the assignment combination is unique within a document.
  - Example: If an invoice has only one expense line, profit center and segment transfer to vendor and tax lines.
  - With multiple account assignment combinations, inheritance is not used.
- **Standard A/C Assgnmt/Constant**: Defines default account assignments (e.g., default profit center and segment) for line items where correct assignments can’t be entered or derived at posting.
  - Example: Cash payment received from a customer before invoicing.

---

### Company Code Specific Settings

- Splitting affects **all company codes by default**.
- You can **deactivate splitting** for specific company codes by selecting the **Inactive indicator** (see Figure 2.57).
- Deactivating splitting on productive systems is generally **not recommended**, as it may cause **inconsistencies** and reduce reporting details.

---

## 2.5.16 Document Splitting Characteristics

In Customizing, select which **account assignments** are used as **splitting characteristics**.

- Fields can be based on **general ledger scenarios** (e.g., Profit Center, Segment) or **custom fields** added via **coding block extensibility**.
- Account assignments can be defined as **zero-balance splitting characteristics** to ensure documents balance per assignment.
- For each field, you can mark it as **mandatory**. All line items must have this field filled.
- If a mandatory field cannot be entered or derived during posting, the system raises an **error**.

---

![Figure 2.53 Tax Procedure List](image1)

![Figure 2.54 Tax Procedure Details](image2)

![Figure 2.55 Manage Tax Codes](image3)

![Figure 2.56 Document Splitting Activation](image4)

![Figure 2.57 Deactivate Document Splitting for Company Code](image5)

![Figure 2.58 Document Splitting Characteristics](image6)

## Document Splitting in General Ledger Accounting

You would select both the **Zero Balance** and **Mandatory Field** checkboxes if a field is required to report on the balance sheet level for the relevant account assignment, as is the case for the **Segment** field when it’s used for segment reporting.

Different business transactions and accounts can be handled differently by the system regarding document splitting. You configure the grouping of accounts and the mapping of these to item categories in **Customizing**. Most accounts are mapped with a specific type automatically by the system, but you need to assign the category manually for **revenue accounts**, **expense accounts**, **bank account/cash accounts**, and **balance sheet accounts**. 

You also assign **document types** to business transactions and can further specify business transaction variants to refine the splitting rules.

### Figure 2.59: General Ledger Account and Document Type Splitting Definition

---

## 2.5.17 Document Splitting Steps

There are three steps in document splitting:

1. **Passive document split**  
   This includes all splitting that you can’t configure and that happens automatically. The most typical example here is a payment for an invoice.

   For example, a payment made to clear the invoice will have the line in the entry view as shown in Table 2.5. The system would produce the lines in the general ledger view as shown in Table 2.6.

   | Line Number | General Ledger Account | Description | Debit/Credit | Amount | Profit Center | Segment |
   |-------------|-----------------------|-------------|--------------|--------|---------------|---------|
   | 1           | Bank Account          | C           | 1100         | N/A    | N/A           | N/A     |
   | 2           | Vendor                | D           | 1100         | N/A    | N/A           | N/A     |

   **Table 2.5** Payment Entry: Document View

   | Line Number | General Ledger Account | Description | Debit/Credit | Amount | Profit Center | Segment |
   |-------------|-----------------------|-------------|--------------|--------|---------------|---------|
   | 1           | Bank Account          | C           | 440          | PCA    | SA            |         |
   | 2           | Bank Account          | C           | 660          | PCB    | SB            |         |
   | 3           | Vendor                | D           | 440          | PCA    | SA            |         |
   | 4           | Vendor                | D           | 660          | PCB    | SB            |         |

   **Table 2.6** Payment Entry: General Ledger View

2. **Active document split**  
   This is the “normal” document rule-based splitting process that you customize and the system splits based on predefined rules. An example of active document splitting was shown earlier in Table 2.4.

3. **Zero-balance clearing line formation**  
   In this step, the system generates the lines required to ensure that the document balances for each account assignment specified as a **zero-balance splitting characteristic**. This is commonly required for **transfer postings** where you post between profit centers and segments.

   For example, in the entry view, you have two simple lines reposting the same expense line to two different profit centers (and subsequently two different segments). If the system is set up with both profit center and segment defined as zero-balance characteristics, the system would post the line in the general ledger view as shown in Table 2.8.

   | Line Number | General Ledger Account | Description | Debit/Credit | Amount | Profit Center | Segment |
   |-------------|-----------------------|-------------|--------------|--------|---------------|---------|
   | 1           | Expense 1             | C           | 1000         | PCA    | SA            |         |
   | 2           | Expense 1             | D           | 1000         | PCB    | SB            |         |

   **Table 2.7** Transfer between Profit Centers: Entry View

   | Line Number | General Ledger Account | Description | Debit/Credit | Amount | Profit Center | Segment |
   |-------------|-----------------------|-------------|--------------|--------|---------------|---------|
   | 1           | Expense 1             | C           | 1000         | PCA    | SA            |         |
   | 2           | Clearing 1            | D           | 1000         | PCA    | SA            |         |
   | 3           | Expense 1             | D           | 1000         | PCB    | SB            |         |
   | 4           | Clearing 1            | C           | 1000         | PCB    | SB            |         |

   **Table 2.8** Transfer Between Profit Centers: General Ledger View

Adding the two clearing lines enables the document to be posted with **zero balance** for all account assignments. For every document that generates clearing lines, the clearing account will always balance to zero.

---

## 2.6 Business Transactions in the General Ledger

The daily business transaction management for general ledger accounting includes **posting**, **changing**, and **reversing general ledger document entries**. Additionally, it covers **cross-company-code transaction posting** and **document clearing** for open-item-managed general ledger accounts.

### 2.6.1 Posting General Ledger Documents

When entering a document, you first enter the details that concern the **header** of the document and then build up the various **line items** you’ll post to. The header details are valid for the complete document.

The system checks that all required header details are entered before you can proceed with entering data in the line items.

In **SAP S/4HANA**, the main application for entering general ledger documents is **Post General Journal Entries**.

---

### Document Header Fields (Figure 2.60)

- **Journal Entry Date**  
   Usually the date on any document that prompted the entry (e.g., invoice date). If no specific document, it is often the same as the posting date.

- **Posting Date**  
   The date the system uses to update the database. Defines the posting period and fiscal year.

- **Journal Entry Type**  
   Refers to the **document type** as analyzed in the document types and number ranges subsection.

- **Company Code**  
   Defaulted for all lines but can be changed on individual lines for cross-company documents.

- **Transaction Currency**  
   Currency used for the posting; translated into company code currency and others.

- **Ledger Group**  
   Defines the ledger group for posting (important in parallel accounting). Leaving blank posts to all ledgers.

- **Reference**  
   Reference number or identification of the originating document (e.g., invoice number).

- **Header Text**  
   Notes the business reason behind posting the document (limited to 25 characters).

- **Exchange Rate**  
   Defaulted to the rate valid on translation date, but can be updated manually. System enforces max rate deviation.

- **Translation Date**  
   Date used to define the exchange rate. Defaults to journal entry date if not manually entered.

---

### Additional Header Information

The system saves more data than manually input, including:

- Entry date and time
- User who made the entry
- Business process (e.g., accounting posting, purchasing invoice verification)
- Document number updated upon parking or posting

---

### Line Item Basics

Each **line item** requires an **account** and a **posting key**. In some cases, the posting key is replaced by fields to indicate debit or credit amounts (e.g., Transaction FB50).

- Debit default posting key: **40**
- Credit default posting key: **50**

It's important to be familiar with posting keys, especially when they must be entered manually.

---

### Line Item Data Entry (Figure 2.61)

After entering the account and posting key, the system displays the fields available for entry based on **field status definitions**.

- In the expense line example, **controlling-relevant fields** are ready for entry.
- **Cost Center** may be manually entered.
- **Profit Center**, **Segment**, and **Functional Area** can be derived automatically.
- For tax-related accounts, entering a **Tax Code** is required.
- The system can calculate tax automatically and supports **net entries** where the entered amount excludes tax.
- **Item Text** is an optional short note.
- **Assignment field** is auto-filled based on the sort key, generally from the header reference but can be overridden.

---

### Bank Account Posting (Figure 2.62)

Example account assignments for a **bank account** posting include fields like:

- **Value Date**  
  Important for cash/bank postings; indicates the date of the cash transaction. It can be set automatically or overridden manually.

- **House Bank**  
- **House Bank Account**

At this stage, **document splitting** isn’t yet applied, so splitting characteristic fields like **Profit Center** and **Segment** are not filled.

---

### Document Simulation and Posting

Before posting, you can **simulate the document** to:

- Check the entry view
- Allow the system to perform check routines
- Get warnings or error messages
- Simulate the general ledger view to verify document splitting

After verification, post the document. You may encounter errors during posting such as missing **document number ranges**.

- Document numbers are assigned only when you post or park the document.
- External document range assignments require entering the document number during header input.

---

### Important Tips and Warnings

- **Extension ledgers** are only posted to when their **ledger group** is explicitly entered but inherit values from underlying ledgers.
- After posting a document, changes are minimal. Mistakes require **reversing and reposting** the document.
- On rare occasions, if an external document range is assigned, enter the document number when inputting header information.

## 2.6.2 Changing Documents

There are two separate areas in which changes are allowed for a **document**: the **document header** and the **line item** (Figure 2.63). You configure rules for changing documents either for all company codes or individually, and the individual rule takes precedence over the global rule.

For the **document header** in Figure 2.63 1, you can define that the fields **reference** and **document header text** can be changed after a document is posted. You can indicate that changes are only allowed so long as the period remains open or leave it so that the fields can change at any time.

For the **line items** in Figure 2.63 2, in addition to the specification per company code, you can set different rules according to the **account type** and the **transaction type**. For processing changes to the line item, more fields are available to set as changeable: the **line-item text**, **assignment**, **payment terms**, and **payment method**.  
In addition, you have more control over when a document field might be changed under the **Stipulations for changing** area 3.

**Figure 2.63 Rules for Changing the Document Header and Line Items**

Every time you make changes to a document (header or line item), the change is **logged by the system**. You can always view the full **history of changes** to a document, including information for the following:

- **When** a change was made (**date, time**)
- **Who** made the change
- **What** was changed for which field (**old value, new value**)

Any line-item field that would alter the **financial accounting integrity** of the document can’t be changed. Fields such as **Posting Key**, **Account**, **Amount**, **Tax Code**, **Profit Center**, and **Segment**, as well as **controlling assignment fields** (e.g., **Cost Center**), are all restricted from being changed.  
To change such fundamental characteristics of a document, the usual course of action is to **reverse and repost** if it’s a controlling account.

---

## 2.6.3 Reversing Documents

**Financial accounting document reversal** in SAP S/4HANA is usually performed in the **Manage Journal Entries** app. You enter search criteria for the document or documents you want to reverse, select the ones to reverse from the list, and reverse them individually or in groups (Figure 2.64).  

**Figure 2.64 Reversal Posting**

When reversing multiple documents, you enter the same reversal criteria for all, so you must make sure the reversal data is correct for all. To reverse documents, you enter the following data:

- **Reversal Reason**  
  Define reversal settings for the document and indicate why the reversal is performed.

- **Posting Date**  
  Enter the date the system will use to post the reversal. When posting in the same period as the original document, you usually enter the same posting date. When posting a reversal for a document in a closed period, you generally enter the current date. The **Period** field will be updated from the period indicated in the posting date.

- **(Optional) Tax Reporting Date**  
  Define whether the tax reporting date is maintained when posting a document in the global settings for the company code. When defined, you can enter a date when reversing the document.

- **(Optional) Check Void Reason**  
  Define a void reason for reversing a manual check posting. Relevant only when reversing a payment document issued by check.

- **(Optional) Process Intercompany Transactions Completely**  
  Use to reverse all journal entries posted with the intercompany transaction even if you didn’t explicitly select all relevant entries.

When a document has been **cleared**, you’re not allowed to reverse it directly. The system raises an error informing you that the document has been cleared. You must first **reset the clearing**, and only then can you reverse the document.

In SAP S/4HANA **Customizing**, you configure the **allowed reversal reasons** (Figure 2.65 1) and define whether **negative postings** are allowed for a company code (Figure 2.65 2). A company code that doesn’t allow negative postings can’t use reversal reasons configured to use negative posting.

**Figure 2.65 Document Reversal Configuration**

You can define as many **reversal reasons** as required for reporting and control purposes. There are only two settings for the reversal reason controls:

- **Neg. Pstg (negative posting)**  
  A normal reversal debits the credit line items and credits the debit line items of the original document. A **negative posting** reduces the transaction figures by posting negative amounts on the same debit/credit side as the original posting. This restores the account debit/credit figures to their status before the original posting. Negative postings aren’t always allowed.

- **Alt.Pos.Dt (alternative posting date)**  
  Allows posting the reversal to a date different from the original document’s posting date. Usually marked for reversals in **closed periods**.

---

## 2.6.4 Cross-Company-Code Postings

When entering a simple **cross-company-code** transaction, you enter the **company code** the line refers to in each line, as shown in Figure 2.66. The system generates two documents, one for each company code.

To balance the document per company code, the system generates a line using a **preconfigured clearing account** for the posting document in each company code. The system writes a common **cross-company-code document number** to group the relevant documents together for reporting.

**Figure 2.66 Entering Cross-Company-Code Postings**

In Customizing, you define the clearing account for each pair of company codes where cross-company-code transactions are valid, as shown in Figure 2.67 1.

**Figure 2.67 Configure Cross-Company-Code Postings**

For each company code, you determine a **posting key** and **account** on the receivables and payables sides 2. The clearing account doesn’t have to be a general ledger account; you can also define **customer** and **vendor posting keys and accounts**.

---

## 2.6.5 Financial Document Clearing

When you post a transaction to an account that is **open-item managed**, the transaction is incomplete until the item is cleared. To clear an open item, you post a **clearing document** that balances the open item or group of open items to zero. In Figure 2.68, a single euro is missing, so the system reports the open balance in red.

**Figure 2.68 Post with Clearing**

> **Tip:** Accounts with **uncleared open items** can’t be archived.

When posting with clearing, you select **open items** from a list posted to the specified open item account. After selection, the items must balance to zero among themselves. The clearing document created does not change the debit or credit balance of the account; it only matches open items. The system creates a **clearing document**, and the clearing document number is updated on the original documents from which the open items originate.

If you match the wrong items, you can **reset clearing documents** for items cleared incorrectly, as shown in Figure 2.69. Another reason to reset clearing is if you need to **reverse a document that created an open item you cleared**. You can’t reverse a cleared document, so resetting clearing is required first.

**Figure 2.69 Reset Cleared Items**

---

## 2.6.6 Default Values for Data Entry

As an aid to minimize repetitive data entry, you can set **default values** for many fields in areas of **financials** (financial accounting, controlling, SAP Financial Supply Management [SAP FSCM]) and **logistics** (materials management and sales and distribution).

An exhaustive list of fields you can default for every new SAP S/4HANA release is maintained in a blog post: [Setting User Defaults in SAP S/4HANA](https://blogs.sap.com/2017/09/14/setting-user-defaults-in-sap-s4hana/).

The **default value** can be overwritten with a manual entry or by automatic derivations such as **substitutions**. Figure 2.70 shows a list of available fields for financial accounting.

**Figure 2.70 Financial Accounting User Default Values**

---

## 2.6.7 General Ledger Overview

SAP has released an **overview dashboard app** (Figure 2.71) for **general ledger accountants** to track various **key figures**, view notification inboxes, and access apps via quick links.

All reports and live tiles are updated in **real time** with actual system data, which may increase app-load time initially. This dashboard is intended as a **single screen** for general ledger accountants to monitor all relevant information.

**Figure 2.71 General Ledger Overview**

---

## 2.7 Important Terminology

In this chapter, the following terminology was used:

- **Account group**  
  An element that categorizes general ledger accounts. Controls the number range and types of accounts that can be created.

- **Chart of accounts**  
  A complete register of general ledger accounts to cover business needs of the assigned company codes. There are three levels:  
  - **Operational chart of accounts**  
  - **Local chart of accounts**  
  - **Group chart of accounts**

- **Client**  
  The highest organizational unit, equivalent to a corporate group or group of affiliates.

- **Company code**  
  The most important organizational unit in financial accounting representing the **legal entity** for which a complete, self-contained set of accounts can be created.

- **Document splitting**  
  A function that makes account assignments defined as splitting characteristics to all lines of a document based on specific rules.

- **Document type**  
  Categorizes business transactions and defines the relevant account types and the number range of the documents.

- **Extension ledger**  
  A delta ledger added on top of an underlying ledger for special valuation purposes.

- **Fiscal year variant**  
  Defines the start and end dates of the fiscal year and the posting periods available during the year.

- **Parallel accounting with accounts**  
  A method using separate sets of general ledger accounts for specific accounting functions valuated differently by separate accounting principles.

- **Parallel accounting with ledgers**  
  A method using **ledgers** to depict separate accounting principles.

- **Posting key**  
  Defines whether a line amount is **debited or credited** and the type of account posted to. Also maintains a **field status** at the posting key level.

- **Posting period variant**  
  Controls the open and closed periods for company codes. Multiple company codes can be assigned to a single variant to control periods jointly.

## Chapter 2 General Ledger Accounting

### Segment reporting
**Segment reporting** is a reporting requirement of **IFRS** and **US GAAP** legal reporting which stipulates that **company codes** need to be able to produce complete **balance** and **P&L statements** per major business activity segment. In **SAP S/4HANA**, this requirement is covered with the **profit center** and **segment account assignments** in conjunction with **document splitting**.

### Standard ledger
A **ledger** that holds values for separate valuations; often it represents a separate **accounting principle**.

### Tax code
