A **key** that controls the **tax rate** and **tax account** posted to.

### Tolerance group
Assigned to each user, it defines the **maximum amounts** a user can post, as well as the **maximum discounts** they can grant.

---

## 2.8 Practice Questions

These practice questions will help you evaluate your understanding of the topics covered in this chapter. The questions shown are similar in nature to those found on the **certification examination**. Although none of these questions will be found on the exam itself, they will allow you to review your knowledge of the subject.

Select the correct answers, and then check the completeness of your answers in the next section. Remember that, on the exam, you must select **all correct answers** and **only correct answers** to receive credit for the question.

1. Your customer operates 20 company codes in 10 different countries and three continents. What is the minimum number of **clients** you must configure in the **SAP S/4HANA system** to depict this scenario?
   - A. 3  
   - B. 10  
   - C. 1  
   - D. 20  

2. What types of objects are maintained separately per client? (There are **three** correct answers.)
   - A. **Master data**  
   - B. **ABAP programs**  
   - C. **Organizational units**  
   - D. **Transactional data**  
   - E. **Function modules**  

3. True or False: You can install as many **SAP Best Practices packages** as needed in the same client.  
   - A. True  
   - B. False  

4. What can you manually select to copy when you copy a **company code**? (There are **three** correct answers.)
   - A. **Controlling area assignment**  
   - B. **User profiles and roles**  
   - C. **General ledger account data**  
   - D. **Company code currency**  
   - E. **Document splitting rules**  

5. What are the three basic steps required to define a new **company code**? (There are **three** correct answers.)
   - A. **Adjust global parameters**  
   - B. **Copy existing company code**  
   - C. **Copy existing controlling area**  
   - D. **Define new segments**  
   - E. **Adjust basic and address data**  

6. Which of the following assignments can be adjusted for the **company code**? (There are **three** correct answers.)
   - A. **Company**  
   - B. **Fiscal year variant**  
   - C. **Segment**  
   - D. **Chart of accounts**  
   - E. **Leading ledger**  

7. True or False: You need to assign the **workflow variant** to a company code to be able to perform standard workflow scenarios such as **parked document approvals**.  
   - A. True  
   - B. False  

8. Which of the following organizational units are part of the enterprise structure of **financial accounting**? (There are **three** correct answers.)
   - A. **Functional area**  
   - B. **Operating concern**  
   - C. **Business area**  
   - D. **Plant**  
   - E. **Segment**  

9. For which of the following **account assignments** can you configure the system to create complete **balance sheet reports**? (There are **three** correct answers.)
   - A. **Cost center**  
   - B. **Profit center**  
   - C. **Segment**  
   - D. **Company code**  
   - E. **Profitability segment**

    - A. True  
    - B. False

    - A. True  
    - B. False

    - A. **Organizational chart of accounts**

    - E. **Group chart of accounts**

    - A. **Chart of accounts**  
    - B. **Field status group**  
    - C. **Account type**  
    - D. **Account group**  

14. True or False: With the **block indicator** set on the **chart of accounts**, you can no longer perform postings to the company codes assigned.  
    - A. True  
    - B. False  

15. Which fields in the company code definition of a **general ledger account** are always required? (There are **two** correct answers.)
    - A. **Sort Key**  
    - B. **Account Currency**  
    - C. **Field Status Group**  
    - D. **Group Account**

    - B. False

    - D. **Reversal Reason**

    - B. False

## 2.9 Practice Question Answers and Explanations

1. Correct answer: **C**  
The key word in the question is **minimum**. You have to think then if there are any restrictions for how many company codes, countries, or even continents. Because there are **no restrictions** on what kind of organizational units are mapped on the client, the answer is that you can set everything up in a **single client**.  

2. Correct answers: **A, C, D**  
If you understand the concept of **client-dependent** and **client-independent objects**, this is an easy one. You can think of examples of objects for each category to find the correct option:  
- **Organizational unit:** Company code is only available in the client created.  
- **Master data:** General ledger account is only available within the chart of accounts of a specific client.  
- **Transactional data:** General ledger posting is posted to a company code, so it’s only available on the specific client.  
**ABAP code**, whether programs or function modules, is always **client-independent**. If you change a program in a specific client, the change affects all the objects in **all clients**.  

3. Correct answer: **A**  
True. Because each country has at least one **SAP Best Practices package**, it’s obvious that there has to be a way to support many packages on the same client. In principle, you can install **as many SAP Best Practices packages as desired** in a single client.  

4. Correct answers: **A, C, D**  
The three correct options are detailed earlier in this chapter (in the **Company Code** section); however, it isn’t always easy to remember so many details. To answer this, then, you might consider which objects are defined or assigned on the **company code level**. For example, this would directly eliminate splitting rules because all splitting Customizing is on the **client level**. Users, roles, and so on aren’t really discussed in the SAP S/4HANA financial accounting SAP Training and Adoption courses nor in this book.

## Financial Accounting Training and Certification

Remember, all **correct answers** must be referenced directly in the **financial accounting training materials**. The closest discussion to **users, roles, and authorizations** concerns the **tolerance profiles**, which operate across **company codes**.

---

## 5. Company Code Creation Steps

Following are the three steps in the correct order:

- **Copy an existing company code**, preferably the one that most closely resembles the one you want to create.
- **Adjust basic and address data** by changing the name and address details of the new company code.
- **Adjust global parameters** by checking all core settings such as the chart of accounts, fiscal year, and others.

**Correct answers:** A, B, E

---

## 6. Core Objects and Assignments in Financial Accounting

You need to be familiar with the **core objects** and their assignments:

- The **leading ledger** is assigned to all company codes because there is only a single leading ledger per client.
- The **segments** are defined on the client level and assigned to **profit centers**.
- Profit centers are assigned to company codes, but this fact may be rejected in certification exams due to ambiguity.

**Correct answers:** A, B, D

---

## 7. Workflow Variant Definition

The **workflow variant** is defined as the location where **rules** are set.

- In certification exams, if an answer seems obvious, it usually is.

**Correct answer:** A

---

## 8. Organizational Units and Reporting

Key organizational units and uses:

- The **functional area** is used for **cost of sales accounting** in financial accounting.
- The **business area** depicts a separate **business division**.
- The **segment** is used for **segment reporting**.
- The **operating concern** is a **management accounting (profitability analysis)** organizational unit.
- The **plant** is the basic **logistics organizational unit**.

**Correct answers:** A, C, E

---

## 9. Balance Sheet Reports and Characteristics

- The **company code** is the default level for **balance sheet reports**.
- **Profit center** and **segment** can be configured as **splitting characteristics** for document splitting, enabling balance sheets at their level.
- The **cost center** and **profitability segment** can only be posted for **P&L accounts** that are **cost elements**.

**Correct answers:** B, C, D

---

## 10. Operating Concern and Assignments

- The **operating concern** is assigned **one-to-many** to the **controlling area**.
- The **company code** is assigned to the operating concern **indirectly**, through its assignment to the controlling area.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 11. Purchasing Organization Assignment

- If the **company code** is not assigned to the **purchasing organization**, the system derives it using the **plant**.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 12. Chart of Accounts Assignments

- **Operational** and **country/local chart of accounts** are assigned to the company code.
- The **group chart of accounts** is assigned to the **operational chart of accounts**.
- No other types of chart of accounts exist in the system.
- Certification exams cannot include made-up system objects.

**Correct answers:** B, D, E

---

## 13. Chart of Accounts and Account Group Definitions

- In the **chart of accounts**, you define the **maximum length** of accounts.
- In the **account group**, you define the **number range** which controls the length of the field by default.
- The shorter of the two definitions takes precedence for account length.

**Correct answers:** A, D

---

## 14. Indicator Blocking Assignments

- The **indicator** blocks accounts in the chart of accounts from being assigned to a company code.
- This does **not** affect accounts already assigned before the indicator was set.
- It does **not** stop you from posting to accounts of the chart of accounts.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 15. Account Creation Requirements

- The **account currency** and the **field status group** must always be defined to create an account.
- These are not affected by the **field status definition** of the account group.
- The **group account** is defined on the chart of accounts level and is required when the group chart of accounts is assigned.
- The **sort key** is optional but recommended for better reporting on line items.

**Correct answers:** B, C

---

## 16. Field Status Priority

- **Suppress** field status has the **highest priority**.
- Priority order: **Suppress > Display > Required > Optional**.
- This prioritization is standard in **SAP S/4HANA**.

**Correct answer:** C

---

## 17. Secondary Cost Accounts

- Used to post **transfer postings** in controlling.
- The balance for secondary cost accounts is always **zero** for a company code.
- You can debit a secondary account only by crediting another secondary account.
- Secondary cost accounts are a **new feature** in SAP S/4HANA; previously known as **secondary cost elements**.

**Correct answer:** C

---

## 18. Retained Earnings Account Definition

- You only need to define the **retained earnings account** manually if you have more than one.
- In this case, **automatic assignment** becomes impossible.
- You must input the correct type manually.

**Correct answer:** A (True statement)

---

## 19. Local Chart of Accounts Assignment

- The relationship when assigning a **local chart of accounts** in the company code is **one-to-one**.
- One local account can only be assigned to a single account of the **operational chart of accounts**.

**Correct answer:** D

---

## 20. Company Code and Leading Ledger Assignment

- All company codes are assigned **at minimum** to the **leading ledger**.

**Correct answer:** B

---

## 21. Standard Ledger Assignment

- A **new standard ledger** is **not assigned** to any company codes until done **manually**.
- When creating a ledger by copying, you can choose to copy assignments and settings from the original.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 22. Ledger Group and Extension Ledger

- The ledger group containing the **extension ledger** is **generated automatically**.
- There is no way to assign an extension ledger to any other ledger group.
- Posting to an extension ledger's group updates only the **extension ledger**.

**Correct answer:** A

---

## 23. Account Sets and Valuation Differences

- You only need to create two sets of accounts for accounts where there is a **valuation difference**.
- Not all accounts need duplication.
- In most cases, accounting entries can be valuated in a **single way** for all accounting principles, using common accounts.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 24. Extension Ledger Groups and Valuation

- Although limited to **manual postings**, an **extension ledger group** can be assigned to an **accounting principle**.
- This allows for a **complete, separate valuation**.

**Correct answer:** A (True statement)

---

## 25. Accounting Principle Object

- The **accounting principle object** carries **no valuation rules or checks** by itself.
- Some SAP Best Practices packages or client 000 may have predefined accounting principles.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 26. Period Variants and Calendars

- **Open and closed periods** are defined per **period variant**.
- Start and end dates of the calendar year are universal and **not defined in SAP system**.

**Correct answers:** C, D

---

## 27. Currency Types in SAP S/4HANA

- The system supports **10 currency types in parallel** per company code/ledger combination.
- Two currencies are always reserved: **company code currency** and **global currency (controlling area currency)**.
- Up to **8 custom currency types** can be assigned.

**Correct answer:** B

---

## 28. Posting Key Functionality

The **posting key** determines:

- The **type of account** being posted (general ledger, asset accounting, accounts payable, accounts receivable).
- Whether the line is a **debit or credit entry** (e.g., 40 = debit, 50 = credit for general ledger postings).

**Correct answers:** A, D

---

## 29. Maximum Exchange Rate Deviation

- Defined in the company code's **global settings**.
- **Maximum tax amount** is not relevant here.

**Correct answers:** A, B, C

---

## 30. Tax Code Definition in FTXP

- Tax codes are defined per country in **Transaction FTXP**.
- Assign relevant **tax percentage rates** per tax type.
- Determine if an account is relevant for tax in **general ledger account maintenance** at the company code level.

**Correct answers:** A, D

---

## 31. Segment Requirement for Document Posting

- Setting the **segment as required** ensures no document can be posted without it.
- The system raises an error and blocks posting if a line is missing a segment assignment.

**Correct answer:** C

---

## 32. Entry View Document Posting

- The **entry view** is the posted document before considering document splitting or ledger-specific line items.
- Typical posting lines in entry view:

  - One line for the **supplier**
  - One line for the **expense**
  - One line for the **tax**

- Total of **three lines** in the entry view (updated in table BSEG).

**Correct answer:** B

---

## 33. Universal Journal Line Items

- Updated in table **ACDOCA**.
- Reflect the document **after** document splitting and ledger-specific line items.
- Document splitting with one expense line does not create new lines.
- Standard ledgers are updated; extension ledgers are updated indirectly through underlying ledgers.
- Lines analytically:

  - One line for the supplier per standard ledger
  - One line for the expense per standard ledger
  - One line for the tax per standard ledger

- Total of **six lines** in the Universal Journal.

**Correct answer:** D

---

## 34. Posting Date and Period Determination

- The **posting date** defines the period for posting.
- Closed periods cannot be posted to, except **special posting periods** (13, 14, 15, 16 in a 12-period fiscal year).
- For special periods, posting date must be in the **last period** of the fiscal year.

**Correct answer:** C

---

## 35. Changeable Fields in Document Header

- Only two fields are **changeable** in the document header:

  - **Document reference**
  - **Document header text**

- Other fields require **reversing and reposting** for correction.

**Correct answer:** D

---

## 36. Document Reversal Process

- When reversing documents, you must define:

  - The **posting date** for the reversal document
  - The **reversal reason**

- The **reversal document type** depends on the original document type.
- The **document date** matches the original and is not entered manually.

**Correct answers:** C, D

---

## 37. Negative Reversal Posting

- With a **negative reversal**, the system posts a **negative amount** on the same debit/credit side as the original.
- This keeps the total debit/credit for the account unchanged by the incorrect posting.

**Correct answer:** B (False statement corrected)

---

## 38. Clearing Account Requirement

- The **clearing account** does not have to be limited to a **general ledger account** only.

**Correct answer:** A (True statement)

## Intercompany Postings and Clearing Accounts

You can define a **customer** or a **vendor account** to be posted to for the **clearing line items** that balance **intercompany postings** for each **company code**. You must define an appropriate **posting key** as well.

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

---

## Summary Section 2.11

### Question 39 – Correct answer: B

False. Although the grouping of the amounts is different, the **financial result** is always the same with either the **cost of sales** or **period accounting methods**. The difference between the two is in the breakdown detail of the **costs** and **revenues**.

---

## 2.10 Test Takeaway

You’ve gained a good overview of all basic **general ledger accounting objects** and **configurations** in **SAP S/4HANA**. You saw the basic **organizational units** that make up the **enterprise structure** from the financial accounting perspective, and you learned about their **assignments** and basic **configurations**.

The same goes for the **master records** such as the **general ledger account** and the **profit center**. You should be familiar with the concept of **parallel accounting** and the two solutions proposed by SAP to cover the requirement for **multiple valuations**.

**Document splitting** is a fundamental capability in SAP S/4HANA that provides the means for corporations to report on **segments** for their legal statements.

Finally, you should understand how the basic **transaction processing** works for **general ledger document posting** and management.

If you’re already familiar with **new general ledger accounting** in SAP ERP, you’ll notice that the differences aren’t groundbreaking. However, there is a lot of difference in the underlying **table architecture**, which isn’t a subject in scope for an associate-level certification.

What the end user notices is the difference in the frontend, where using **SAP Fiori apps** provides a **dynamic** and **intuitive** environment.

---

## 2.11 Summary

**General ledger accounting** is the fundamental building block required for further **financial accounting configuration**, and a solid setup here in full alignment to the customer's requirements is required for a successful **SAP S/4HANA implementation project**.

You should now understand how common **accounting requirements** are covered by the system, as well as how to manage the simple postings in **general ledger accounting**.

In the next chapter, we’ll analyze the **accounts payable** and **accounts receivable** master records, functions, and documents.

# Chapter 3  
## Accounts Payable and Accounts Receivable

### Techniques You’ll Master

- Manage **business partner accounts** for customers and suppliers
- Perform basic **accounts payable** and **accounts receivable** transactions
- Run **dunning** for receivables
- Manage **correspondence**
- Post to alternative **reconciliation accounts**

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

---

### Introduction

The focus of this chapter is to explain **accounts payable/accounts receivable** component processes and configurations in **SAP S/4HANA**.

It discusses the **business partner master record maintenance**, **accounts payable/accounts receivable invoicing and integration**, **manual and automatic payments**, **dunning**, and **correspondence**.

---

### Real-World Scenario

As a **financial consultant**, you’ll often be required to either configure the **accounts payable** and **accounts receivable components** yourself or manage the integration of these with the piece of the application you’re working on.

No business exists without **customers**, and it’s hard to imagine many businesses without any **suppliers**. The accounts payable/accounts receivable components are tightly integrated with many components outside the SAP ERP Financials scope, mainly **purchasing** and **sales and distribution**.

In SAP S/4HANA, **customers** and **suppliers** are mapped through the **business partner**, a central **master record** that is common for other areas such as **purchasing**, **sales**, **human resources**, **real estate**, and many more, including the **industry solution space**.

You need to understand where **Customizing** for the **business partner** ends and Customizing for the **customers** and **suppliers** begins.

**Posting invoices**, managing **payments**, performing **dunning**, and sending **correspondence** are just a few of the transactions performed in the scope of **accounts payable/accounts receivable**, and you need to be able to configure these and guide customers to use them effectively.

---

## 3.1 Objectives of This Portion of the Test

The purpose of this portion of the certification exam is to test your general knowledge of the **accounts payable** and **accounts receivable** components.

The certification exam expects you to have a good understanding of the following topics:

- Manage **business partners**
- Manage **invoices** (customer and supplier)
- Manage **payments** (customer and supplier)
- Manage **automatic payments**
- Configure and use **dunning**
- Configure and use **correspondence**
- Describe integration with **logistics** (purchasing and sales)
- Define **terms of payment** (and payment types)
- Configure and use **special general ledger indicators**

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

---

## 3.2 Business Partners

**Business partners** in the **SAP S/4HANA** system represent entities with which your company interacts for business purposes.

In SAP S/4HANA, you don’t create **customer** and **supplier master records** directly; these are all created through the **business partner object** with a process called **customer/supplier integration**.

In a new SAP S/4HANA system based on best practices, the **customer/supplier integration** is already configured and works seamlessly.

In an SAP ERP system planned to be migrated, the consultant takes steps before (mostly) and after the transition to SAP S/4HANA to prepare the integration with business partners in SAP (if it wasn’t already used).

The required configuration to transition to SAP S/4HANA isn’t in scope for the **application associate certification**.

It’s enough to understand the **basic settings** for a **business partner** and where you need to configure the **business partner**, **customer**, and **supplier**.

---

### 3.2.1 Categories

Each business partner you create is assigned to one of three **categories**, which define some of the general data fields you maintain (as shown in Figure 3.1):

- **Persons** (i.e., a private individual)  
  Maintain a **first** and **last name**, and add details such as **gender** and **academic title**.

- **Organizations** (e.g., a company)  
  Enter details such as the **name**, **legal form and entity**, and **industry**.

- **Groups** (e.g., a married couple)  
  Enter two names and the **group type**.

You can’t configure additional business partner categories.

After you create a business partner, it’s no longer possible to change the **business partner category**; instead, you should create a new master record.

You define the type of **business relation** your company has with the business partner through the **business partner role assignment**, as shown in Figure 3.2.

The business partner role of **general business partner** is automatically assigned to every business partner. Here, you maintain **general data** such as **name**, **address**, **contact**, and **bank details**.

You can create a business partner in one or more **roles**; the **general data** will be common for all additional roles assigned.

---

### 3.2.2 Business Partner Roles

Although you can define your own **business partner roles**, the ones delivered should suffice in most cases.

However, you might want to define your own roles if you need to manage the required fields or the **number ranges** assigned to the business partner differently.

**Business partners** might have roles added and removed over time; for example, when you’re still identifying **potential suppliers** for a product you need, you might create multiple **prospective suppliers** to perform evaluations.

This would be a custom **business partner role**, probably with more **optional fields** given that no actual **invoice document** will be posted to the business partner at this stage.

When you select the actual supplier, you can delete the **prospective role assignment** in the business partner master record and create the business partner in the **supplier role** and the **supplier (financial accounting) role**.

---

### 3.2.3 Role Grouping

By using the **role grouping functionality**, you can define which roles are maintained **simultaneously** (see Figure 3.3).

This is used as a **job aid** to speed up **master data creation**.

Of course, this also means that a single individual or department knows how to maintain all the relevant **data fields** correctly.

If the company works with **central master data maintenance**, it might make sense to group roles in this way to make sure, for example, that a customer is always maintained for **sales and distribution** as well as **financial accounting**, or that a supplier is maintained for **materials management** in SAP ERP and **financial accounting**.

Central maintenance like this means the business partner is completely ready to use after the data is saved.

It isn’t uncommon to have customers that the **sales department** has “neglected” to maintain, for example. This means the business partner can’t be used for **sales operations**.

**Warning:**  
The role grouping shouldn’t be confused with the **business partner grouping**.

The **business partner grouping** is maintained separately and defines the **number assignment** for the business partner master record.

In addition, the **grouping characteristic** is assigned and determines the **customer/supplier account group** when creating a customer or supplier.

Each **account group** of the customer and supplier that is used is assigned to a **business partner grouping**.

---

### 3.2.4 Number Range Definition

The **number range** for suppliers and customers in an SAP S/4HANA system should generally be driven by the **business partner**, as shown in Figure 3.4.

In the delivered SAP **Best Practices system**, the customers and suppliers inherit the same number as the **business partners** for which they are created.

For the business partner to take the lead in **number assignment** for customers and suppliers, the **customer/supplier account groups** are assigned to **number range intervals** with **external numbering**.

The **business partner** usually has an **internal number range** assigned.

When created, a number is assigned to the business partner.

When the business partner is also assigned the **supplier role**, for example, the system will create the supplier master record with the same number (the same thing happens if the business partner is also extended with the **customer role**).

This way, the business partner, independent of its role, has a **single recognizable number** throughout.

**Tip:**  
Things are more complicated in a system converted (or to be converted) from an SAP ERP system because suppliers and customers will have completely different and independent **account numbers**.

Usually, the customer and supplier numbers are used for the initial business partner creation, and the logic is switched when normal operation is resumed.

Information about the configuration of **customer and supplier integration** isn’t in scope for the  
**SAP Certified Application Associate – SAP S/4HANA for Financial Accounting Associates** exam.

However, it’s in scope and part of the curriculum for the  
**SAP Certified Application Professional – Financials in SAP S/4HANA for SAP ERP Finance Experts** exam.

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

## 3.2.5 Business Partner Types

The **business partner type** is an additional grouping characteristic for the business partner, as shown in Figure 3.5. The business partner type is connected to a **field status** via which you can control the optional and required fields for maintenance.

For example, you might assign a **payment block** by default on travel expenses from **employees** but not from **managers**. You make the payment block field a **required entry** for the employee type so that you don’t forget to maintain it. 

With the same types, an additional example is the **contact person**, for which it might be required to enter the name and contact details of the assistant for users with the **manager** business partner type, but the assistant entry would remain optional for the **employee** business partner type.

---

## 3.2.6 Business Partner Field Attributes

You can define **field selections** in four separate levels for business partners (see Figure 3.6):

- **Configure Field Attributes per Client**  
  Define the **field status** for the business partner generically.

- **Configure Field Attributes per BP Role**  
  Define the fields ready for entry for specific roles. By default, all customers share the same field status; the same applies to all suppliers.

- **Configure Field Attributes per Activity**  
  Assign different field statuses depending on the **activity performed** (e.g., create or change). This protects fields from changing after a master record has been created and posted to. For example, the **reconciliation account** is usually set to required during creation and display-only during change activity.

- **Configure Field Attributes per Business Partner Type**  
  Define fields ready for entry for specific business partner types. These types are optional and used only if additional reporting elements or a separate field status control level is needed.

The **field status priorities** (from strongest to weakest) for conflicts between these field status levels are:

1. Suppress  
2. Display  
3. Required  
4. Optional  

If a field is set to **Required** on client level and **Optional** elsewhere, the field will be **required**.

For field status conflicts within multiple roles, the priority differs (from strongest to weakest):

1. Required  
2. Optional  
3. Display  
4. Suppress  
5. Not Specified  

If a field is to be **suppressed**, it must be suppressed or undefined in **all roles**.

---

## 3.2.7 Customer and Supplier Account Groups

In the **financial accounting component**, you create and maintain **account groups** for **customers** and **suppliers**. These group different customers and suppliers based on criteria such as location, size, or affiliation (see Figure 3.7).

For example, usually a separate account group is configured for **domestic** and **foreign** customers/suppliers. In Europe, further categorization such as **EU** or **non-EU** may be used.

You can define your own account groups in **Customizing** (and with the **Account Groups Customer app** and **Account Groups Supplier app**).

---

## 3.2.8 Account Group Details

The basic settings maintained for the account group fall under three screen areas (see Figure 3.8):

### General Data

- Enter the **Name** of the account group.  
- Enter a **Number Range** (should be external and driven by the business partner group).  
- Select whether this is a **One-Time Account**.

### Field Status

- Controls which fields are ready for entry in the business partner maintenance (accounts payable/accounts receivable specific fields).  
- Advised to keep these **optional** to drive all field definitions from the business partners (see Figure 3.9).

### PartnerDetermProced

Partner functions define the **business roles** a partner plays in sales/distribution (customers) and purchasing (materials management) processes.

Examples of partner functions (for suppliers):

- **AZ:** Alternative payee  
- **OA:** Ordering address  
- **VN:** Supplier  
- **CR:** Carrier  
- **CA:** Contract address  
- **GS:** Goods supplier  
- **DP:** Delivering site  

The business partner is connected to the account group (customer and supplier) through the business partner grouping (see Figure 3.10). By selecting the same number, the business partner drives the number assignment for the customer/supplier master record.

---

## 3.2.9 One-Time Accounts and Normal Accounts

An important categorization in accounts receivable/accounts payable account groups is between **one-time accounts** and **normal accounts**.

- **One-time account:** Used to post customers or suppliers with whom you don’t have and don’t expect to have permanent business relations. Creating a master record for such accounts would be redundant.

The one-time customer or supplier uses a **business partner master record** without specific general, bank, and tax details. These are entered during posting of the actual document in a special popup (Figure 3.11). 

Payment details are specified per document but can also be defaulted in the master record of the one-time account.

The separate details of individual one-time accounts are stored in customer and supplier lists. Later, you can report in line-item reports on a one-time account by adding the supplier name.

A key setting is defining fields that trigger the **dual-control workflow** (Figure 3.12). If enabled, the system requires an approval step to confirm certain changes in master records. Payments are blocked until approval.

Use the **Confirm Customer List (Accounting)** and **Confirm Supplier List (Accounting)** apps to display accounts pending approval for changes.

---

## 3.2.10 General Data

When creating the **general data** of a business partner (common for all roles assigned), maintain:

- **Basic data:** Business partner grouping (defines the number assigned) and identification details (depend on business partner category) as shown in Figure 3.13.

- **Additional Information area:** Maintain overall blocks applying to all roles for posting, payments, purchasing (for suppliers), billing, and delivery (for customers).

- Maintain corresponding **Customer** and **Alternative Payee** fields for suppliers, and **Supplier** and **Alternative Payer** fields for customers.

- By selecting **Alternative Payer Allowed in Document/Payee in Document** indicator, you can enter an alternative payer/payee (even not maintained in the system) directly during invoice processing.

- Enter a list of allowed payer/payees in the master record and select from it at document entry.

When assigning a customer in a supplier master record (or vice versa), there is an option to display a **single balance** for the business partner and clear open amounts between business partner/customer or business partner/supplier.

To do this, set **Clearing with Supplier** and **Clearing with Customer** in the company data section of the customer and supplier roles, then assign relevant roles.

Figure 3.14 displays some relevant standard roles for suppliers and customers with validity dates. Roles can be assigned temporarily.

After assigning roles, enter **Address** and **Standard Communication details** (Figure 3.15). These are on the general business partner role level and common for all roles.

Different address details can be assigned to different time periods (e.g., when a business partner moves).

The most important communication detail is the **communication language**, which is used for correspondence output to the business partner.

Other maintained data on the general business partner role level includes **bank details** (ID, Account Number, Account Holder, IBAN if valid) as shown in Figure 3.16.

In many countries, **tax numbers** are important as unique business partner identifiers and often required in reports.

For customers and suppliers, use the **company code details** (maintained per company code, Figure 3.17) to maintain essential info for financial accounting transactions, such as:

- **Reconciliation Account:**  
  The **general ledger account** posted to when posting to customer or supplier account. Can only be posted to through customer or supplier.

- **Sort Key:**  
  Used to populate the **Assignment Number field** in line items of customer/supplier documents, automatically transferring values from fields like Document Number, Posting Date, Reference Number, etc. Multiple fields can be combined.

- **Payment Terms:**  
  Defines default payment terms for invoices, including installment payments and discount percentages.

## Business Partners Section 3.2

### Payment Methods

- **Payment methods** include bank transfers, checks, and others.

### Tolerance Group

- Leaving this blank assigns the business partner to the **default tolerance group** defined.

### Posting Block / Payment Block

- With **posting blocks**, no document can be posted to the business partner.
- With **payment blocks**, only payments are restricted.

### House Bank

- The **default bank** used for payments or receipt of payments.

### Head Office

- Entering another **business partner** here enables the **head office/branch accounting** scenario.
- A branch may sell goods independently, but accounting is performed centrally.
- Sales orders post to branch accounts; sales and transaction figures post to the head office account.
- Payments are cleared centrally by the head office.
- Correspondence can be handled centrally or decentralized by branches.
- Leave blank for **decentralized processing** by branches.

### Individual Payment

- Selecting this option generates a **separate payment document** for each invoice.

### Clearing with Customer

- Allows clearing between **supplier and customer items** when both are connected.

### Correspondence

- Details such as **Accounting Clerk, Phone, Account at Supplier** can be maintained per company code assignment.

### Withholding Tax Type / Withholding Tax Code

- Maintained at the **company code level** for tax details.

### Purchasing and Sales Data in SAP S/4HANA

- Materials management and sales details are transferred as **characteristic values** on accounting line items.
- Stored in the **Universal Journal** for reporting.
- Data such as **purchasing group** can be transferred with **account-based profitability analysis (CO-PA) characteristics**.

### Figures Related to Purchasing and Sales Data

- **Figure 3.18:** Supplier Purchasing Data shows payment terms maintained in purchasing/sales details.
  - These terms take priority over company code level but can be overridden manually.

- **Figure 3.19:** Customer Sales Data

### Business Partner Contact Details

- Personal and contact details such as **phone numbers, email address, building, floor, and office** can be maintained.
- Refer to **Figure 3.20: Business Partner Contact Details: Supplier**.

---

## 3.3 Payment Terms

The **terms of payment** define dates and amounts due for transactions with business partners. This section covers discounts, installment payments, payment blocks, block reasons, and tolerance settings.

### 3.3.1 Payment Term Definition

- The system comes with **predefined payment terms**, but you can customize terms to meet customer requirements.
- Terms are defined with a **four-digit alphanumeric code** and a **Sales text** field.
- The **Own Explanation** field can override the automatic explanation below (see **Figure 3.21**).

#### Important Definitions in Configuration:

- **Day Limit**  
  Defines the last valid day in the month for the payment term (e.g., 15 means the term is valid for invoice dates up to the 15th).  
  Allows multiple rules for the same payment term code with different day limits.

- **Account Type**  
  Defines if the term applies to **vendors**, **customers**, or both, preventing wrong entries and simplifying selection.

- **Baseline Date Calculation**  
  - **Fixed Day**: Specific baseline date in the invoice month (e.g., "20" sets the baseline to the 20th).  
  - **Additional Months**: Month offset added to the fixed day (e.g., "1" sets baseline to 20th of the next month).  
  - Manual overriding of baseline date is possible during journal entry.

- **Tip:**  
  Entering day “31” adjusts automatically to the last day of shorter months.

- **Payment Block/Payment Method Default**  
  Assign a default **payment block** and **payment method** for the payment term.

- **Default for Baseline Date**  
  Options to propose baseline dates based on:  
  - No Default (manual update required)  
  - Document Date (most common)  
  - Posting Date  
  - Entry Date (system date at entry time, not manually changeable)

- **Payment Terms Details**  
  Define actual payment dates and **discount percentages** (see **Figure 3.22** for example with 3%, 2% discounts and final due date).

### 3.3.2 Installment Payments

- Enables automatic splitting of the open amount into **multiple installments** with separate due dates.
- Define a **base payment term** and separate terms for each installment.
- Assign base term to master records; system sets due dates accordingly.
- Connection between base and installment terms set in **Customizing**; you specify order and percentage for installments.
- Credit memos linked to invoices inherit payment terms; otherwise, due on baseline date.
- You can enter payment terms for credit memos without invoice links by entering “V” in the **Reference** field.

- Refer to **Figure 3.22** and **Figure 3.23** for installment payment configuration and examples.

### 3.3.3 Payment Block Reasons

- Also called **block key**, used to indicate the reason for a payment block (helpful for reporting).
- Definitions include (see **Figure 3.24**):  
  - **Change in Payment Proposal:** Allows unblocking in payment proposal processor.  
  - **Manual Payments Block:** Blocks item from being cleared with a manual payment.  
  - **Not Changeable:** Relevant to **payment workflow scenarios**; block removed only via approval.

### 3.3.4 Customer/Supplier Tolerance

- Similar to the general ledger tolerance profile (Chapter 2).
- Settings specify conditions where **payment differences** within tolerances are automatically posted as cash discount adjustments or unauthorized deductions.
- Differences outside tolerance require manual processing.

- Refer to **Figure 3.25: Customer/Supplier Tolerance Settings**.

---

## 3.4 Invoicing

There are three major ways to post invoices in SAP S/4HANA:

- Directly in **financial accounting** without other component integration.
- Through **purchasing**, integrated with financial accounting.
- Through **sales and distribution**, integrated with financial accounting.

In integrated scenarios, fewer manual entries are needed in financial accounting because purchase and sales orders provide necessary details.

## Financial Accounting Journal Entry

For the **financial accounting journal entry**, you first select the **company code** and then maintain the following details:

- **Document (invoice) date** and **posting date**
- **Amount** and **currency**
- **Tax code** and whether the tax amount is calculated automatically
- **Reference** (usually the invoice number)
- **Short explanation text**

### Tip

When using the apps for entering **outgoing** or **incoming invoices**, you get information about the **customer** or **supplier** entered directly on the **header section** of the screen (see Figure 3.26). You see the most basic **address and bank information** and can branch directly to the **master record** as well. You also can open a report directly for the **open items** of the customer/supplier.

After filling in the **customer/supplier account information** and any other fields marked as required, you can check the **Payment details tab** (Figure 3.27). Here you’ll see the chosen **payment terms**, as well as the calculated **baseline** and **due dates**.

The system will also display the details of the planned **discounts** according to the chosen **payment method**; you can also change these detailed definitions manually on the line item. You can directly enter a **cash discount (CD)**, the relevant **payment method (Payt Meth.)**, **payment currency (PmntCurrcy)**, and amount in said currency (**Pmnt/c amt**), and your **House bank details**. Another potentially important entry field is the **payment block reason (Pmnt block)**.

### Invoice Entry Screen Features

On the **invoice entry screen**, you have the option to display a side **Tree** with **input help** for your entries. You can select from three types of objects:

- **Screen variants for items**

For the line items of the invoice, you select the relevant **expense** (or **revenue**) accounts, and then you must enter a **controlling account assignment**. When entering the line items for the expenses/revenues, there is an overwhelming number of **account assignments** and fields to select for entry.

Because of this, you can define **screen variants** for the displayed fields to help the user make the choices relevant for the entry (Figure 3.28). There are a few standard variants delivered by **SAP**, and you can create your own as well using **Transaction SHD0 (Transaction Variant)**.

### Account Assignment Templates

The **account assignment template** acts as a “prefilled” document. When you save a template, all **general ledger account line items** entered are saved without the amounts. Templates make sense for **recurring expenses** without a fixed periodicity. 

Account assignment templates are **personal** by default; however, you can also create **global templates** by starting their name definitions with a forward slash (“/”).

### Held Documents

If, for example, you get distracted by something urgent in your mailbox or you need to ask someone something about the posting while entering a document, you can save the document as a **held document**. This ensures that you won’t lose the data you’ve entered up to that point.

You can retrieve documents to complete and post them from the **Held Documents folder** in the Tree. Only the user that created the held document can see and retrieve the document to continue working on it.

Unlike with document parking, a held document doesn’t receive a **document number**.

### Parameter ID and User Defaults

In addition to the options in the Tree, there are other features that can speed up document entry. You can enter values for the **parameter ID** in the **user maintenance** under the **Parameters tab**. The system defaults the parameter ID when in relevant application screens. 

The value defined in the parameter ID field works for many applications and reports. 

Steps to maintain Parameter ID (without SAP Fiori):

1. Find the field you want to default (e.g., **Company Code 1**), and select the (F1) help.
2. In the popup screen, select the **Technical Details** button.
3. In the new popup screen, find the **Parameter ID** field.
4. Go to the **user maintenance transaction (Transaction SU01)**, under the **Parameters tab**, and enter the **SET/GET Parameter ID** and the **Parameter value** you want to default for the selected user.

End users use the **Maintain User Profile screen (Transaction SU3)** to enter parameters in the same way, but only for the users they log on as.

With **SAP Fiori**, it’s much easier to maintain the parameter ID for the end user (in fact, it’s transparent that the user is maintaining a parameter ID). In the **user settings**, under **Default Values**, a list of fields per component is displayed (Figure 3.30). 

The user can set a single value here or, where it makes sense, more than one value as a default (using the **Additional Values** option). Setting multiple values or ranges of values makes more sense for reporting.

### Accounting Editing Options

Accessing the **Accounting Editing Options** screen gives the user a lot of control over many **posting parameters** for document entry and document display. There are too many detailed options to go over, but you can see the available selection in Figure 3.31.

### Tip

It helps to visualize screens during the exam; however, you’re generally not expected to remember screens and fields. **Understanding the options available** and how to use them is the expectation.

### Invoice Posting with Purchase Order Reference

The standard screen for posting **purchasing invoice verifications** is like the screen for posting **ingoing/outgoing invoices** (Figure 3.32). When building the line items, you enter the **purchase order reference**, and here, you can reference a purchase order.

When you reference a document, the line items are transferred with the relevant **account assignments**. You can confirm the entries as they are from the purchase order if correct or change them to match the actual invoice if there are differences.

### Billing Documents

A **billing document** can be an order-related invoice, delivery-related invoice, credit memo, or one of many other types (see Figure 3.33). A billing document is **open until it’s posted to financial accounting**.

Many of the sales and distribution field values are transferred to the **Universal Journal** through **accounting-based CO-PA characteristics**. These values can then be analyzed in **financial accounting** and **controlling reporting**.

---

## 3.5 Manual Payments

Broadly speaking, posting a **manual incoming payment** clears **customer open items**, and posting a **manual outgoing payment** clears **supplier open items**. This is reversed for clearing **credit/debit memos**.

On the screen for posting payments (there is little difference between incoming/outgoing), you enter the following data (Figure 3.35):

### Manual Payment Entry Data

**General Information**

- Enter the **company code**, **posting date**, **document date**, **value date** (the date on which the payment is actualized), and **reference**.

**Bank Data**

- Enter the **bank general ledger account**, **house bank ID** and **account**, **amount** and **currency**, any **transaction fees**, and an **assignment** (usually filled automatically by the relevant sort key).

**Open Item Selection**

- Enter the **supplier** or **customer** who is making or receiving the payment and select **Show Items** to get a list of **open items posted**.

### Open Items and Discounts

In the **Open Items list**, when you select the relevant open items (**invoices, debit or credit memos, unassigned payments**) to clear, the items are transferred to the **Items to Be Cleared** list. 

Here the **discount per item** is proposed per the **payment method due dates/discounts**. You can also change the proposed discount in accordance with tolerances assigned to the user and customer/supplier.

When the **Balance of the document** (displayed at the top right of the screen) is zero, you can then **simulate the entry** to check all the proposed line items. Once confirmed, you can **post the document**. The **open items are cleared**, and the **payment document** is assigned as the **clearing document** in the cleared line items.

---

### 3.5.1 Posting on Account

You can select to **post on a customer/supplier account** when you post a payment to a customer or supplier account **without reference to a specific item** (see Figure 3.36). This is used when clearing isn’t possible at the time of entry.

When clarified, you usually match the payment with the relevant open items. This option can be used when a **payment difference** is too large to manage in other ways.

When payment differences do arise, and they are outside your assigned **tolerance limits** (or you don’t want to post the difference as a loss), you can:

- Select to post a **partial payment**
- Handle the difference with a **residual item**
- Use a **separate payment difference posting**

You can enter **(customizable) reason codes** to indicate the reason for the difference.

A **partial payment** doesn’t clear the open item; both the open item and the payment remain as open items on the account and are connected through the reference to the invoice.

When a third item is received, or sent, you then clear the three items among themselves (e.g., open item and two payments, or invoice item, payment, and credit/debit memo).

With the **residual item**, the system clears the payment and the open item and then generates a new open item from the difference. Both the payment and the original open item are cleared.

The new open item is posted under a new document that references the original document. The new item can inherit the payment terms of the original item or be assigned different ones.

Finally, you can handle the difference manually by:

- Posting, for example, to a separate **general ledger account** or **posting on account**.
- Writing the difference off as **unrecoverable** through manual posting to a **loss (or gain) account**.

---

### 3.5.2 Foreign Currency

Another type of payment difference can occur from **currency exchange differences**. The exchange rate at the time of invoicing for invoices in **foreign currency** can be different from the exchange rate at the time of payment.

The payment is made with the correct foreign currency amount; however, you have a **loss or gain** from the currency fluctuation.

In **Customizing**, you assign a **revenue or expense** from the **foreign currency valuation account** to the **reconciliation accounts** (and any general ledger accounts) that have transactions in foreign currencies.

## 3.6 Automatic Payments

The **automatic payment program** in **SAP S/4HANA** is designed to manage **outgoing (and incoming) mass payment transactions**. It is fully customizable to adapt to the specific needs of each implementation in any country. You can make **domestic payments, foreign payments, and intercompany payments**; clear down payments and open items between customers and suppliers; and more.

The automatic payment program first generates a **payment proposal** based on the parameters you set. You can modify the payment proposal (e.g., manually block or unblock items for payment) as required and then process the payment. Depending on the payments made and the payment methods used, the system will print checks and prepare **electronic bank transfer files** or lists of payments for manual execution.

**Tip**  
The academy and certification focus on the automatic payment program’s **Customizing, outgoing payment proposal and run, and payment medium file export**. Other functions aren’t analyzed in much detail. Although the EU’s **Single Euro Payments Area (SEPA)** is an interesting subject, it’s out of scope for the certification and won’t be analyzed in this guide.

---

### 3.6.1 Customizing the Payment Program

Most **Customizing** required for the automatic payment program (see Figure 3.37), outside the configuration of invoice posting and business partner master records, is performed through **Transaction FBZP** (though the Customizing transactions also can be found separately in the SAP IMG tree).

**Note**  
The **House banks** button and link in Figure 3.37 is no longer valid with SAP S/4HANA. It leads to the old Transaction **FI12**, which has been replaced with the new bank account management applications that work in **SAP Fiori** and **Web Dynpro**.

![Figure 3.37 Customizing the Payment Program (Transaction FBZP)](image-link-placeholder)

---

### 3.6.2 Company Codes

The first Customizing settings you must define are some basic specifications for any **company codes** involved in payment transactions, as shown in Figure 3.38:

- **Sending company code**  
  This is the company code that interacts with the business partner. It’s usually the company code for which you’re making the definition. If left empty, the **Paying company code** is defaulted also as the Sending company code.

- **Paying company code**  
  Enter the company code that participates in the payment transactions. This can be the same as the company code for which you’re making the definition or another company code when, for example, payments are processed centrally. Both the sending and paying company code play a role in the grouping of payment transactions, and a separate payment document will be processed when any of these are different. Items can be grouped into one payment for company codes with the same paying company code and the same sending company code.

- **Separate Payment per Business Area**  
  If business areas are used, the system can produce a separate payment document for each business area.

- **Pyt Meth Suppl.**  
  These payment method supplements act as an additional characteristic to split the payment documents. You create the two-digit keys and assign them in customer and supplier master records. These are then copied to the document as well, where you can change the proposed value coming from the master record.

- **Tolerances Days for Payable**  
  This parameter allows you to specify a **grace period** in the form of the number of days by which the cash discount period and the period for the net payment may be exceeded (to perform a delayed payment).

- **Outgoing Pmnt with Cash Disc. From**  
  Enter the minimum percentage rate for which the system will post a payment early to receive a discount. Discount percentages lower than this rate are ignored, and payment is executed at the due date for net payment.

- **Max. Cash Discount**  
  When checked, the maximum cash discount is always used when paying supplier invoices even if the payment is made after the predefined period.

- **Sp. G/L Transactions to Be Paid/Sp. G/L Trans. for Exception List**  
  You can set the special general ledger transactions for customers and suppliers that you want to include or exclude from the payment run.

![Figure 3.38 Company Code Payment Settings](image-link-placeholder)

---

### 3.6.3 Customization

For each company code that has been defined as a paying company code, you can define the following details (Figure 3.39):

- **Minimum Amount for Incoming/Outgoing Payment**  
  Any payments below the amount threshold you define here aren’t made.

- **No Exchange Rate Differences/No Exch.Rate Diffs. (Part Payments)**  
  This checkbox determines whether the program will calculate and post **exchange rate differences**.

- **Separate Payment for Each Ref.**  
  This checkbox determines whether the program will perform a separate payment for each document reference. Clearing between customer/supplier items isn’t performed in this case (unless the reference is the same).

- **Bill/Exch Pymt**  
  This checkbox determines whether the program is to process **bills of exchange**.

- **Direct Debit Pre-Notifications**  
  This checkbox determines whether to print **direct debit prenotifications** to inform the payer of a coming direct debit before the collection date.

![Figure 3.39 Paying Company Code Settings](image-link-placeholder)

---

### Forms

You can define an **SAPscript** or a **PDF-based default form** for the payment advice note and the **Electronic Data Interchange (EDI)** accompanying sheet. You also define some standard texts (e.g., address details) that are to be used in the forms.

Payment methods have separate configurations on the **country level** and on the **company code level** because a company code might not make use of all payment methods defined for the relative country.

---

### 3.6.4 Country Level

On the country level, you define first which **payment methods** are valid (e.g., **SEPA direct debit** is valid for European countries, so you would define it only for those). A payment method (**Pymt Meth.**) is represented by a single-digit alphanumeric key and a short **Description** (Figure 3.40). You define the following by payment method and country:

- **Payment method for**  
  Determine whether the payment is used for **incoming** or **outgoing** payments.

- **Payment method classification**  
  Control which other control keys you can define (e.g., if it’s an allowed payment to perform employee payments).

- **Required master record specifications**  
  Maintain additional data on the business partner if required per the payment method definition.

- **Posting details**  
  Define how the posting is handled for the payment method you’re defining:  
  - **Document Type for Payment**: Specify the document type used to post the document with the payment program.  
  - **Clearing Document Type**: Specify the document type used to post **cross-company-code payments**.  
  - **Payment Order Only**: If selected, the system doesn’t post a payment document, so no clearing is performed. Instead, a **payment order** is generated with information that will be used later to clear the open items.

- **Payment medium**  
  The payment medium format that defines the form of the **data media exchange (DME)**.

**Note**  
In SAP S/4HANA, only the **payment medium workbench (PMW)** can be used for DME files. The **RFFO*** reports are obsolete.

- **Currencies Allowed**  
  The currencies allowed to be used for posting with the payment method. Leave this definition empty if you don’t want to restrict it.

![Figure 3.40 Payment Method: Country Settings](image-link-placeholder)

For each company code, you select which payment methods are valid from the ones defined on the country level. For each one used, you define the following (Figure 3.41):

- **Amount limits**  
  You define a **Minimum Amount** and **Maximum Amount** allowed for the payment method. When the amount to be paid is outside the defined limits, the payment method isn’t used. If you manually enter the payment method in a line item, the limits are ignored, and the payment method is used.

  **Example:**  
  If you’ve set the maximum amount for checks to **$10,000 USD**, and there is an open item of **$11,000 USD**, the payment program won’t select the item for payment for this payment method.

  **Note**  
  The **distribution amount (Distribution amnt)** tells the payment program to group payments so that they don’t exceed the set distribution amount. This only works if the system can make payments below the set amount for all payment groupings.

  **Example:**  
  If you set a distribution limit of **$15,000 USD**, have two open items to pay of **$17,000** and **$16,000 USD**, and two credit memos for **$2,500** and **$3,000 USD**, the system makes two payments of **$14,000** and **$13,000 USD** (*$17,000 - $3,000* and *$16,000 - $2,500*, respectively).

  If instead you had a single credit memo of **$5,500 USD**, the system would not split the credit amount. In this case, the payment method isn’t selected, and the system would use either a different payment method or place the items in the payment exception list, if no valid payment method could be assigned automatically.

  The distribution amount check is made even if you’ve set the payment method manually for the open item.

- **Foreign payments/foreign currency payments**  
  Define whether the payment method can be used to pay **foreign business partners** and whether a **foreign currency** can be used for payment (among the currencies defined on the country level of the payment method). Also, define whether transfer to a bank abroad is allowed. If not, the payment method isn’t applicable unless the business partner maintains a bank account in the country of the paying company code.

![Figure 3.41 Payment Method: Company Code Settings](image-link-placeholder)

- **Grouping of items**  
  The system can group payments of items according to the following criteria:  
  - **Single Payment for Marked Item:** All items for which the specific payment method is entered explicitly are paid individually with separate documents.  
  - **Payment per Due Day:** A separate payment is made per due day defined by the payment terms for the item.  
  - **Extended Individual Payment:** Each open item is paid with a separate document. An exception is made for credit memos that reference the invoice; in this case, the payment is consolidated. This setting is incompatible with the distribution amount limit.

- **Bank selection control**  
  The system can be set to optimize the payments:  
  - **Optimize by Bank Group:** The system selects the optimal pair of banks (you configure bank grouping separately in the bank master). This can be used to avoid transfer charges, for example.  
  - **Optimize by postal code:** Prioritizes the house bank that is geographically nearest to the address of the business partner. This might make sense if you print and send checks by mail, for example.



## Form Data

You define the **name of the issuer** printed on the form or output in the payment medium and how the correspondence in payment transactions (**payment advice notes, checks, bills of exchange**) is sorted. **Pyt. Adv. Ctrl.** You define the number of lines printed in the form for the note to payee and when to print a payment advice note (not shown in Figure 3.41).

This concludes the configuration of the **payment media** for **company codes**. We’ll very briefly go over the **PMW** and form definition, as these are advanced subjects and not in scope in any real detail for the certification.

### 3.6.5 Payment Medium Workbench

The **PMW** is a tool to define and create **DME formats**. These can be used directly during the **payment run**. The formats are usually defined in the **data medium exchange engine (DMEE)**.

SAP delivers many common **standard payment formats** for countries. These can be copied and changed in **Customizing** through the DMEE without requiring any technical skills. You change the payment format using an application, as shown in Figure 3.42, which shows the **XML structure** of the **SEPA Credit Transfer form** on the left.

The PMW also handles **payment advice notes** centrally and the definition of **notes to payees**.

![Figure 3.42 DMEE Tree Definition for SEPA Credit Transfer](#)

When you execute the **payment run** for the payment program, the **generic payment medium program** is triggered to create the payment media using the definitions for the form as maintained in the **DMEE Customizing**.

After completing the configurations for the payment methods, you define how the system selects the bank from which to perform payments through the **automatic payment program**. Figure 3.43 shows the individual configured steps in the left hierarchy.

![Figure 3.43 Bank Selection for Payment Program](#)

The configuration involves the following screens and settings:

- **Ranking Order**  
  You define the order in which the **house banks** are to be considered for payment (Figure 3.44). The definition is per paying **company code**. You rank the banks per **payment method** and **currency**. You can leave either or both the payment method (**PM**) and currency (**Crcy**) fields blank to make a more generic ranking for the banks.

- **Bank Accounts**  
  You define the **bank account ID** and **bank subaccount** that is posted for each house bank, payment method, and currency combination (Figure 3.45). You can leave the Currency field blank, but the House bank, Payment Method, Account ID, and Bank Subaccount are required.

- **Available Amounts**  
  You can manually set the **amount available** in the bank accounts for payment (Figure 3.46). The payment program won’t use the house bank if there aren’t enough funds available here.

![Figure 3.44 Define Ranking Order](#)  
![Figure 3.45 Bank Accounts Definition](#)  
![Figure 3.46 Available Amounts Definitions](#)

- **Value Date**  
  The **value date** is calculated as the day of the payment run plus the **days to value** (Figure 3.47). Most transactions take at least a day to be processed, depending on the payment method. **Cash management** in SAP S/4HANA uses the value date for **cash flow reporting** and **liquidity forecasts**.

- **Expenses/Charges**  
  When posting incoming and outgoing payments, **bank charges** can be entered for any expenses relevant to the payments made or received. Figure 3.48 shows how you can connect amounts charged to the amount of the payment for printing on the payment form. The system doesn’t post the amount defined here; that’s done manually in a separate process.

![Figure 3.47 Value Date Definition](#)  
![Figure 3.48 Charges Definition](#)

After configuring the **bank determination**, that concludes all **Customizing** for automatic payments. We’ll now go over the steps of performing an **automatic payment run** up to and including creating the payment media.

### 3.6.6 Automatic Payment Run

When setting up a new **payment run**, you enter the **Run Date** and **Identification** (Figure 3.49). These fields act as a key for identifying the specific payment run.

![Figure 3.49 Payment Run Parameter Identification](#)

### 3.6.7 Payment Selection Parameters

Based on the parameters you define, the system chooses which **open items** to evaluate for payment. You enter the following data to set the parameters (Figure 3.50):

- **Company Code**  
  Each run can be executed for multiple company codes belonging to the same country (enter one after the other separated by a comma).

- **Payment Method**  
  You define which payment methods can be used in the run. If you’ve set a method in an open item that isn’t included, the open item is ignored. You can enter multiple payment methods per run.

- **Posting Date**  
  This is the date on which the system will post the payments. Often you can align the run date with the posting date, but there is no requirement to do so.

- **Docs Entered Up To**  
  You set the cutoff date for documents to be evaluated for payment. Invoices with a posting date later than this date are ignored.

- **Customer Items Due By**  
  You can set the due date up to which customer items are to be evaluated. You set the date by which an open customer item must be due for it to be included in the payment run. If you leave the field blank, the system takes the payment run posting date as the due date limit. If you want items to be paid that aren’t due until after the posting date, enter a later date in this field.

![Figure 3.50 Payment Selection Parameters](#)

- **Next Payment Date**  
  You enter the date for which you’ll execute the next payment run. The system will evaluate open items and pay items that would be overdue if you waited for the next payment run or to take advantage of **discounts** offered for early payment.

- **Exchange Rate Type**  
  You can enter a specific **exchange rate type** with which you would like to calculate the currency translations.

- **Supplier/Customer**  
  You define which suppliers and customers you want the payment run to evaluate for payment.

- **Free Selection**  
  In this area, you can flexibly choose values for fields from the entered documents or **master records** that you want to use to select specific line items for payment. You can use a field as a criterion for including or excluding the items from the list. For example, you could evaluate only items, customers, and suppliers that have no payment block.

- **Additional Log**  
  This area provides more detailed logs for the item selection.

### 3.6.8 Review

After entering the **selection parameters**, you can schedule the **payment proposal run** or execute it immediately. Depending on the number of items to evaluate, the system processes the proposals and provides the **payment proposal** for evaluation and revision.

When reviewing the proposal, you receive a list of items that will be paid and a list of **exceptions** (Figure 3.51). The system selects and groups the items into payments per the Customizing settings and the parameters you set.

![Figure 3.51 Revise Payment Proposal](#)

Depending on the configurations you’ve made, the system will create documents for the items that will have less of a discount (or no discount) on the proposed next payment run date or that will be **past due** on the proposed next payment run date.

The system will put items in the **Exceptions list** for various reasons, and for each item, you’ll receive a **message** detailing those reasons. The following are a few examples of messages you might receive:

- Item is blocked for payment.
- Account is blocked for payment.
- Unconfirmed change to master record.
- Alternative payee is blocked for payment.
- Unconfirmed change to payee master record.
- No valid payment method found.
- Payment method in the document should not be considered in this run.
- Payment methods for this run are not specified in master record or in item.
- Minimum amount for payment has not been reached.

Some of the causes for having items placed in the Exceptions list can be eliminated directly from the screen for revising the payment proposal (Figure 3.52). You can enter payment methods manually for items for which the method wasn’t determined, and you can do the same for bank details. You can also unblock items for payment, depending on the blocking reason code of the item.

![Figure 3.52 Review Payments](#)

Documents that are in the payment run are blocked from being modified (outside the screens of the payment program) to avoid any inconsistencies. You also can’t post manually to any of the items in the Payments list at this point.

If you need to change an invoice line item or perform a manual payment, you can delete the payment proposal, perform your changes, and re-execute the payment proposal.

When you have a final proposal that you’re happy with, you schedule the **payment run**.

### 3.6.9 Payment Run

The system will post the proposed **payment documents** and clear the relevant **open items**. The postings will include all relevant **foreign currency gains/losses**, **tax** and **withholding tax amounts**, and **discount amounts**. The payment is made against the defined **bank subaccount**. The usual process is for the subaccount to be cleared with the main bank account upon receipt of the **bank statement**.

**Note:** In countries where you must receive a bank statement confirming payment before posting a payment, you can select the **Payment Order Only** checkbox in the payment methods definitions of the relevant country.

The payment document generated is similar to the document of a manual payment with some special characteristics:

- The **run date** and **identification** are written on the header text of the document.
- If the system can determine a **value date** from the payment method and bank definitions, it uses this date. If not, the system uses the **posting date** as the value date.

You can use the **automatic scheduling application** for the payment run to automate the payment run process. You enter the same parameters as are available in **Transaction F110**.

After you’ve entered the parameters, you can **save a variant** for the report and use the variant to schedule the program to run in the background. You can create **periodic runs** if you use identical parameters.

You can view the output of the payment program using the **Revise Payment Proposal** app if you’ve selected the **Proposal run checkbox** (see Figure 3.53). If the checkbox isn’t selected, the payment run will be performed (with the option to also print the payment media).

You can view the results of the payment run in the **Manage Automatic Payments** app, in the **Summary tab** (Figure 3.54).

![Figure 3.53 Schedule Payment Runs](#)  
![Figure 3.54 Manage Automatic Payments: Payment Run Review](#)

### 3.6.10 Payment Media Creation

The relevant **payment media** can be generated at the same time the payment run is performed, or you can generate these in a second step after the payments are made.

In this case, you select the payment run by entering the **Run Date** and **Identification** and then selecting the **Payment Medium Format** (Figure 3.55).

![Figure 3.55 Payment Medium Creation](#)

Figure 3.56 shows partial output from the **XML file** generated for a **SEPA payment** that uses a form provided with the system.

---

## Dunning Section 3.7

## 3.7 Dunning

The **dunning process** is used to remind customers (and sometimes suppliers that have a debit balance) to pay **overdue open items**. The reminders sent out can become progressively stricter and carry a **late payment penalty** as well. Dunning with **SAP S/4HANA** is a **rule-based automated process** controlled through the dunning configuration and execution applications.

Basic configuration for dunning includes three steps (see Figure 3.57):

- **Define Dunning Areas**
- **Define Dunning Keys**
- **Define Dunning Block Reasons**

---

### 3.7.1 Define Dunning Areas

**Dunning areas** are used to subdivide a company into more areas responsible for dunning (Figure 3.58). These are optional, and if you don’t define them, the system essentially uses the **company code** as the single dunning area.

---

### 3.7.2 Define Dunning Keys

**Dunning keys** can be assigned to line items for two basic reasons (Figure 3.59):

- To restrict the **dunning level** of an item so that the item will be dunned up to the level indicated here.
- To **output an item separately** in the dunning notice.

---

### 3.7.3 Define Dunning Block Reason

Items **blocked for dunning** aren’t considered when you execute a dunning run. You define various **dunning block reasons** (the ones shown in Figure 3.60 are delivered with the system/best practices) to classify the item blocks and use them as filtering characteristics in reports.

---

### 3.7.4 Dunning Procedures

The **dunning procedure** is the main Customizing object for dunning (Figure 3.61). It’s maintained at the client level and assigned to partners.

SAP provides **standard dunning procedures** predefined through best practices. Additional procedures can be freely created in Customizing and are represented by a **four-digit alphanumeric code**.

In the overview maintenance for a dunning procedure, you enter a description and maintain the following settings (Figure 3.62):

- **Dunning Interval in Days**  
  Enter how often dunning is to be performed for a business partner. For example, if dunning runs are weekly and this value is 14 days, the partner's items are analyzed every second run.

- **Number of Dunning Levels**  
  Defines how many levels of dunning apply progressively stricter warnings and penalties.

- **Total Due Items from Dunning Level**  
  Defines the dunning level from which all due items of the business partner account are totaled, regardless of days overdue.

- **Min. Days in Arrears (Acct)**  
  Number of days an item must be overdue before dunning is performed.

- **Line Item Grace Periods**
