  Defines how many grace days each line item has before being dunned. Does not affect total days in arrears.

- **Interest Indicator**  
  Assigns how interest is calculated (per item or overall overdue amount). Defaults from the dunning procedure unless changed in the business partner master record.

- **Public Holiday Calendar ID**  
  Takes public holidays into account when requesting payment.

- **Standard Transaction Dunning/Special G/L Transactions**  
  Specifies whether the procedure applies to standard line items, special general ledger line items, or both.

- **Dunning Even for Credit Account Balance**  
  Overrides the default that prevents dunning if the partner has a credit balance.

- **Reference Data**  
  Allows referencing another procedure to use the same dunning text definitions without separate maintenance.

---

### 3.7.5 Dunning Level Maintenance

After maintaining the basic data, details for **dunning levels**, **dunning charges**, **dunning texts**, and **dunning special general ledger indicators** are maintained (Figure 3.63).

For each **dunning level**, define the following:

- **Days in Arrears/Interest**  
  Number of days past due until a partner is assigned to this level.

- **Calculate Interest?**  
  Indicates if interest on the due amount is calculated and charged.

- **Always Dun?**  
  Specifies whether a dunning letter is always sent even if no changes occurred.

- **Print All Items**  
  Prints all open items, not just overdue, to give a complete view.

- **Payment Deadline**  
  Days added to the issue date of the dunning run, creating the payment deadline.

---

### 3.7.6 Dunning Text Maintenance

In maintenance for **dunning text**, you assign a **form** for each dunning procedure level (Figure 3.64). 

- The form defines the **wording** and **formatting** of the dunning letter sent to customers and suppliers per level.
- Editing or creating forms according to customer standards is typically performed by a **technical consultant**.
- Figure 3.65 shows an example of a **3rd dunning letter** with interest.

---

### 3.7.7 Dunning Charges

**Dunning charges** are defined per currency. You enter the charge as either:

- A **fixed amount**, or  
- A **percentage rate** multiplied by the total overdue items.

You can set multiple charges per dunning level depending on the **minimum overdue amount** (Figure 3.66). For example:

- Up to €1,000 EUR: Fixed €10 EUR charge  
- Above €1,000 EUR: 1% charge

You can also set a **minimum overdue amount** for changing a dunning level per currency (Figure 3.67). This minimum can be:

- An **absolute amount**, or  
- A **percentage of the total open items** per business partner per dunning area.

Use cases for minimum amounts:

- Apply a minimum threshold for aggressive dunning letters proportional to the customer's open items.
- Select the **NoRed. checkbox (no reduction)** to keep a partner at a higher level even if minimums aren't met.

There is also a separate minimum amount for calculating charges based on percentages.

---

### 3.7.8 Special General Ledger Indicators

Select which **special general ledger indicators** are valid for the dunning procedure from the full list available (Figure 3.68).

---

### 3.7.9 Company Code Settings

In the **Environment** section of the dunning procedure definition, maintain dunning settings per **company code** (Figure 3.69):

- **By Dun.Ar. (dunning by dunning area)**  
  Posts dunning notices separately for each dunning area instead of by company code.

- **By Dun.Lev. (separate dunning notice for each dunning level)**  
  Prints separate notices for partners per dunning level, so a business partner may receive more than one notice.

- **Ref.CoCode (reference company code)**  
  Assigns forms derived from the referenced company code. Useful for shared layout forms across codes.

- **Dun CoCd (dunning company code)**  
  Allows entering a different company code for centralized dunning letter processing. Customers doing business with multiple company codes will receive a single dunning notice.

Additional sender details such as **address**, **tax number**, **bank details**, and **company logo graphics** can be maintained for dunning notices, sometimes driven by legal requirements.

---

### 3.7.10 Dunning Groupings

Optional setting to define **dunning groupings** by a two-digit code and description with up to two document fields for grouping.

- The system groups dunning notices sharing values in the defined fields.
- Groupings can be valid for **suppliers**, **customers**, or **both**.

Example use cases include:

- Grouping items referring to the same **sales order**.
- Grouping dunning notices for specific projects via the **work breakdown structure (WBS) element**, as shown in Figure 3.70.

---

### 3.7.11 Dunning Details

Dunning details are entered in the **business partner master record**. You maintain fields such as:

- **Dunning Procedure**
- **Dunning Level**
- **Grouping Key**

(Figure 3.71)

You can also enter the **dunning key (Dunn. Key)** or a **dunning block reason (Dunn. Block)** directly on document business partner line items (Figure 3.72).

---

### 3.7.12 Dunning Run

Complete a dunning run by executing these steps in the **Create Dunning Notices** app:

1. Enter **selection parameters** for open items to be evaluated. Required fields include (Figure 3.73):

   - **Run On**: The date of the dunning run.

## Identification

- **Key** to identify the specific run (in conjunction with the date).

### Dunning Date

- The **date of dunning**, which will be printed on the dunning notices and form the basis for calculating days in arrears.

### Docmnts Posted up To

- The system uses this **date as a cutoff** for selecting items.
- The system evaluates the **document dates** of the documents.

### Company Code

- The **company code(s)** for which you’re executing dunning.

### Customers/Vendors

- **Account ranges** for customers and vendors.

---

## Dunning Run Process

2. **Schedule the dunning run.**  
   The system evaluates all relevant items and provides a **dunning proposal**.

3. **Modify the dunning proposal.**  
   The accounts receivable accountants evaluate the proposed list of dunning notices, the assigned levels, and so on.  
   You can execute the proposal run again after deleting the initial proposal.

4. **Print and send the dunning notices.**  
   The system groups the notices as configured.

---

## 3.8 Correspondence

The **correspondence functionality** in **SAP S/4HANA** provides standard ways of communicating various information with suppliers and customers.  
You can use correspondence **ad hoc** to send information or set up scheduled periodic jobs for standardized communication.

### 3.8.1 Correspondence Types

- The **basic Customizing object** for correspondence is the **correspondence type**, which defines what’s communicated to your business partners.
- The system comes with many **preconfigured correspondence types** such as:
  - **Payment notice**
  - **Account statement**
  - **Open items list**, and more.
- **Correspondence types are valid cross-client**.

When defining a correspondence type, you enter a **five-digit code** and the **description**.  
You can also select the following settings (Figure 3.74):

- **Acct Required**  
  Must enter a specific **account** as a parameter to print the correspondence.

- **Doc.Necessary**  
  Must enter a specific **document number** to print the correspondence.

- **Individual Text**  
  Must select the **language** in which to print.

- **Cross-Comp.Code**  
  Correspondence type can be used **across company codes**.

- **Date details**  
  Define up to two **custom dates** to be entered, named appropriately.

---

### Print Program and Variants

- For each correspondence type, define the **print program** and **variant** to enter (Figure 3.75).
- The system comes with **default assignments** and **standard forms** for each payment method.
- You can select different combinations per **company code** or use the same for all.
- Each variant is assigned a **form**.
- **Forms are customizable** by technical consultants.

### Business Partner Data Usage

- Many fields in the **business partner master** are used to create correspondence, such as:
  - **Address**
  - **Tax details**
  - **Bank details**
- **Accounting details, payment definitions, correspondence, and withholding tax details** are used per company code.
- Assign a **default correspondence type** to the **tolerance group**; this becomes the default for the business partner.

---

### 3.8.2 Payment Differences

- Assign **reason codes** for payment differences in line items (Figure 3.76).
- Reason codes can also be assigned to **default correspondence types**.
- If not assigned, define the correspondence type manually.
- Example: For a **partial payment with a residual item**, assign a **reason code** to the residual item.
- The residual item is linked with a correspondence type and you can request and print that correspondence.
- If an invoice has **multiple line items with different reason codes**, the system uses the **default correspondence type** set for the business partner, ignoring line-item definitions.

---

### 3.8.3 Printing Correspondence

- Use the **Create Correspondence app** to print correspondence (Figure 3.77).
- Must select a **company code** and **correspondence type**.
- Depending on the type, you may need to input:
  - **Customer or supplier account**
  - **Document number**
  - Additional **date definitions**
- You can **preview** before final printing.
- Correspondence can be sent **electronically** via **email** or **fax**.

---

## 3.9 Special General Ledger Accounting

**Special general ledger indicators** modify the **general ledger reconciliation account** posted during transactions to depict different business postings.

### Use Cases
- **Down payments received or sent**
- **Down payment requests**
- **Guarantees**
- **Security deposits**, and so on.

### System Configuration

- Defined on the **client level**.
- Many types preconfigured via **SAP Best Practices** (Figure 3.78).
- Categories:
  - **Down payments**
  - **Bills of exchange**
  - **Others** (e.g., transferring amounts to doubtful receivables or guarantees)

---

### Types of Special General Ledger Transactions

- **With offsetting entries**  
  - Fixed offsetting account determination (automatic offset entries).  
  - Example: Posting guarantees, with predefined offsetting account.  
  - Possibly not included in the financial statement or included in notes.
  - Can be free offsetting entries (manual entry of offsetting item).  
  - Example: Posting received payments to specific bank subaccounts.

- **Noted items (without offsetting entries)**  
  - Not included in the financial statement.  
  - Used to track and trigger payments or dunning.  
  - Example: **Down payment requests**.  
  - Posts a single line item with no effect on balance or general ledger values.

---

### 3.9.1 Configuring Special General Ledger Indicators

- Configure and create new indicators in **Customizing**.
- Indicators are **single-digit and cross-client**.
- When creating/maintaining an indicator, define:

  - **Noted Item**  
    Whether the indicator is a noted item.

  - **Rel.to Credit Limit**  
    Whether it influences the **credit limit** (and performs relevant checks with SAP Credit Management).

  - **Commitments Warning**  
    Provides an information message about existing special general ledger amounts when posting (useful for down payments).

  - **Target SP. G/L Ind.**  
    For noted items, configure the **follow-on special general ledger indicator** that clears the item  
    (e.g., special indicator F for down payment requests references indicator A for down payments).

  - **Special G/L transaction types**  
    Classify as **down payments, bills of exchange, or other**.

  - **Posting Key**  
    Relevant posting keys to post debits and credits.

- Define an **alternative reconciliation general ledger account** per main reconciliation account (Figure 3.80).

---

### Note

- In **SAP S/4HANA**, all general ledger accounts are **line-item managed** by default.
- This contrasts with traditional SAP ERP, where line item management is optionally toggled.

---

### Posting Special General Ledger Indicators

- Enter the **special general ledger indicator manually** during postings in financial accounting (Figure 3.81).
- The system posts to customers and suppliers with posting keys as shown in Table 3.1.

| Account Type | Posting Key | Description                     |
|--------------|-------------|--------------------------------|
| Customer     | 09          | Special general ledger debit    |
| Customer     | 19          | Special general ledger credit   |
| Supplier     | 29          | Special general ledger debit    |
| Supplier     | 39          | Special general ledger credit   |

- In many SAP Fiori apps, posting key assignment happens automatically when the special general ledger indicator is assigned.

---

### 3.9.2 Down Payments and Down Payment Requests

- Integrated with **purchasing** and **sales and distribution** functionalities.
- When posting a **purchase order**:
  - Indicate on header and line items if a **down payment** is required (see Figure 3.82 for category selections).
  - This creates a **down payment request** in financial accounting (a noted item with special indicator F).
- When making a **down payment**:
  - Assign relevant purchase order lines.
  - Removes the down payment request obligation by automatically assigning the special indicator A to the down payment posting.
- When posting the **final invoice** from the supplier:
  - Assign the down payment to the invoice.
  - The system connects the invoice open item with the down payment debit amount.
  - The down payment is moved from the **down payment reconciliation account** to the **main reconciliation down payment account**.

## Figure 3.82 Down Payment Category Selection on Purchase Order

In **sales and distribution**, when billing is performed with the **FAZ billing type**, the system triggers a **down payment request** (special general ledger indicator **F**) to be sent to the customer, indicating you expect the down payment by the agreed due date. When the down payment is received, the noted item is deleted.

The down payment request is replaced by the **down payment** once received (special general ledger indicator **A**). When an item is invoiced, the associated down payment is moved to the normal reconciliation account as a **credit open item** and can be cleared against the invoice together with the received payments.

---

## 3.9.3 Posting to Different Reconciliation Accounts

There is an additional option to post to a **different reconciliation account** when posting to customers. You can configure the reconciliation account as **ready for input** during document posting without entering a special general ledger indicator.

This option is useful when the system uses many special general ledger indicators to support all requirements for posting to alternative accounts.

### Steps to Make the Reconciliation Account Selectable During Document Entry:

1. Select the **Rec.Act Ready** checkbox (reconciliation account ready for input) in the **general ledger account master record definition** (Figure 3.83).

2. Change the **account group** for reconciliation accounts to allow maintenance of the reconciliation account, as shown in Figure 3.84.  
   (The default SAP S/4HANA setting suppresses this field.)

3. Configure **valid alternative reconciliation accounts** per reconciliation account to specify entry options (Figure 3.85).  
   The field will then be ready for entry when you select an account with the main reconciliation account configured (Figure 3.86).

---

## 3.10 Reporting

There is no need to detail the various **reporting options** as they are more related to business processes than configuration. However, several reports provide quick views of **accounts payable and accounts receivable key figures** and allow drilling down to analyze potential problem areas (Figure 3.87).

### Overview Pages in SAP S/4HANA 1809 Release

Starting with the **1809 release** of SAP S/4HANA, overview pages offer key metrics and reports for **accounts receivable and accounts payable** accountants (Figures 3.88 and 3.89).

### Accounts Receivable Overview (Figure 3.88)

The **Accounts Receivable Overview** page has several reports with useful information on the front page. You can drill down for more detail. Highlights include:

- **Receivables amount breakdown** by accounting clerk, company code, risk class, or country  
- **Receivables aging analysis**: amounts to be received by due date  
- **Days sales outstanding**: average number of days to collect revenue after a sale

### Accounts Payable Overview (Figure 3.89)

The **Accounts Payable Overview** page displays important **key performance indicator (KPI)** reports and live tiles. You can drill into each report for details, printouts, and analysis. Highlights include:

- **Payable aging analysis** for due and undue amounts, breaking down amounts by due date  
- **Days payable outstanding**, analyzing the average days to pay suppliers in two calculations:  
  - **Direct days payable outstanding**: top 10 suppliers with highest or lowest values  
  - **Indirect days payable outstanding**: aggregate 12-month rolling monthly averages for accounts payable balance and purchases  
- **Cash discount utilization**: measures how well cash discounts are utilized comparing actual versus potential discounts

### Additional Reporting Features

Many typical analysis reports are available for **business partner account balances** and **line items** (Figure 3.90).

- Reports are **real-time** and read directly from line-item information, offering a summarized, analyzable view.  
- No separate storage for balances; limited reporting characteristics from **preconfigured aggregation tables**.

The **customer and supplier line-item reports** offer filtering by item status (Open or Cleared) and inclusion of special general ledger transactions.

Example output (Figure 3.91) shows selection of open items and normal items. You can:

- Select fields to view  
- Save specific layouts and criteria  
- Perform reversals  
- Send correspondence  
- Set/remove dunning blocks  
- Block/unblock payments  
- Open master record or line item details by clicking the account or document number  

---

## 3.11 Important Terminology

The following key terms were used in this chapter:

- **Automatic payment program**  
  Handles payment transactions for customers and suppliers. It generates a payment proposal, which is reviewed and executed. The system generates payment documents and clears relevant open items, printing payment media accordingly.

- **Business partner**  
  The unifying master record for customers and suppliers across SAP S/4HANA subsystems, with real-time integration into financial accounting.

- **Business partner categories**  
  Define whether the business partner is a **person**, **organization**, or **group**. This controls some basic data.

- **Business partner grouping**  
  Defines number ranges for business partners. Customer and supplier account groups are assigned here.

- **Business partner role**  
  Specifies types of business relations with the partner (e.g., customer or supplier in financial accounting). Roles can be grouped for simultaneous maintenance.

- **Business partner type**  
  Additional grouping with a separate field status.

- **Correspondence type**  
  Defines the form of communication (printed or sent). Used to standardize communication regarding amounts owed, open items, etc.

- **Customer/supplier account groups**  
  Group customers and suppliers by criteria in financial accounting. They help separate normal customers/suppliers from **one-time** accounts without permanent master records.

- **Dunning areas**  
  Subdivide a company code for dunning responsibility, allowing configuration of different rules per area.

- **Dunning block reasons**  
  Assigned to document line items to exclude them from dunning. Preconfigured or custom reasons can be used.

- **Dunning procedure**  
  Assigned to business partners to activate dunning, defining dunning levels, charges, special ledger indicators, and letter forms/texts.

- **Dunning program**  
  Generates dunning letters for customers (and suppliers with debit balances) informing about payments due. Produces a proposal list to review before printing letters.

- **Payment block reasons**  
  Indicate why a payment is blocked and how to unblock it.

- **Payment medium workbench (PMW)**  
  Handles all **electronic payment medium** creation and definitions using XML forms (DMEE Tree) assigned to payment methods.

- **Payment methods**  
  Define valid payment types on **country**, **company code**, and **business partner** levels. Payment methods can be maintained per document line item.

- **Special general ledger indicator**  
  Used to post to different reconciliation accounts than the main one in customer/supplier master records. Controls the business transaction type. Examples include noted items, free offsetting entries, automatic offsetting entries, down payment requests, down payments, bills of exchange, guarantees, and value adjustments.

- **Terms of payment (payment terms)**  
  Define due dates and amounts to be paid or received. Configured in Customizing and assigned to business partners and document line items.

---

## 3.12 Practice Questions

*(Content not provided in the source text)*

## 3.12 Practice Questions

These **practice questions** will help you evaluate your understanding of the topics covered in this chapter. The questions shown are similar in nature to those found on the **certification examination**. Although none of these questions will be found on the exam itself, they allow you to review your knowledge of the subject.

Select the correct answers, and then check the completeness of your answers in the next section. Remember that, on the exam, you must select **all correct answers and only correct answers** to receive credit for the question.

1. Which **business partner categories** does the system support? (There are three correct answers.)  
 - A. Group  
 - B. Agency  
 - C. Person  
 - D. Organization  
 - E. Public sector  

2. You’ve mistakenly created your business partner with the wrong business partner category. You’ve saved the data but haven’t made any postings. What can you do to correct this?  
 - A. Change the setting directly in the business partner master record.  
 - B. Contact the system administrator to change the table entry in the backend.  
 - C. Create a new business partner using the correct category.  
 - D. Delete the company code assignment for the business partner, correct the category, and reassign the company code.  

3. True or False: After assigning a **role** to the business partner and saving your data, you’re no longer able to remove the role assigned.  
 - A. True  
 - B. False  

4. True or False: The **business partner role grouping** is where you assign the business partner **number range**.  
 - A. True  
 - B. False  

5. You’re configuring a new **SAP S/4HANA system**. What are your options for defining the **number range assignments** for business partners?  
 - A. The supplier drives the number range used.  
 - B. The customer drives the number range used.  
 - C. The business partner drives the number range used.  
 - D. Whichever account is created first drives the number range used.  

6. Which **business partner objects** can you define **field statuses** for? (There are two correct answers.)  
 - A. Account group  
 - B. Client  
 - C. Role  
 - D. Type  

7. Which field cannot be changed during document posting for the **one-time customer**?  
 - A. Customer Number  
 - B. Customer Name  
 - C. Customer Industry  
 - D. Customer Country  

8. True or False: **Bank details** for a business partner are part of the **general business partner role**.  
 - A. True  
 - B. False  

9. Which field in the business partner master can you configure so that the **document reference** is transferred to the line item?  
 - A. Assignment  
 - B. Reference  
 - C. Line Item Text  
 - D. Sort Key  

10. A business partner is both a customer and a supplier. The customer has a sizable open amount unpaid. You want to make sure that the **payment program** posts no outgoing payments to the business partner until he has paid part of the outstanding amount. How can you do this?  
 - A. Assign an overall payment block in the general business partner role details.  
 - B. Assign a central purchasing block in the general business partner role details.  
 - C. Assign a payment block in the customer business partner role details.  
 - D. Assign a payment block in the supplier business partner role details.  

11. What can you achieve by using the **head office/branch scenario**?  
 - A. Settings changed for the head office master record will be transferred to the branch account.  
 - B. Postings made to the head office also can be paid to the branch account.  
 - C. Invoices posted to the branch become open items for the head office.  
 - D. Correspondence and dunning letters are printed and sent to both the branch and the head office.  

12. Which configuration can you use to define **separate payment terms** for the same **terms of payment key**?  
 - A. Day limit  
 - B. Company code  
 - C. Country  
 - D. Installment payment  

13. You’ve agreed to terms of payment with a business partner that is a customer and a supplier. The same terms are to be used both ways (incoming and outgoing). You’ve defined a new **terms of payment key**, but when trying to update the supplier business partner role, you don’t find the payment term available to select. What must you do?  
 - A. Create a new payment term for the supplier business partner role.  
 - B. Enter the payment term manually during invoicing.  
 - C. Maintain the account type in the terms of payment.  
 - D. Change the field status of the business partner role to make the payment terms an optional field.  

14. You’ve negotiated payment terms that include **three installment payments** with your customer. How many terms of payment must you define?  
 - A. 1  
 - B. 2  
 - C. 3  
 - D. 4  

15. What does assigning a **screen variant** during document entry do?  
 - A. It defaults values for fields in the document line item.  
 - B. It changes the fields that are ready for entry in the document header.  
 - C. It changes the fields that are ready for entry in the line items.  
 - D. It defaults values for fields in the document header.  

16. When setting up the system, you want to maintain **default values for users** of a company code. Which application do you use?  
 - A. User Maintenance  
 - B. Maintain User Profile  
 - C. Default Values (SAP Fiori)  

17. Your customer doesn’t want to implement **profitability analysis**, not even account-based, because the company doesn’t understand its value. Which argument would you use to persuade the customer?  
 - A. Profit and loss statements can be analyzed by sales-specific characteristics.  
 - B. Balance sheets can be analyzed by sales-specific characteristics.  
 - C. Sales orders can be forecasted as liquidity items in cash flow reports.  
 - D. Down payment integration can be performed with sales and distribution.  

18. What can you enter in the header section of the **Post Outgoing Payments** app? (There are three correct answers.)  
 - A. Value date  
 - B. Bank fees  
 - C. Discount amount  
 - D. Customer  
 - E. Payment terms  

19. You receive a payment for an invoice that is smaller than the owed amount. How can you manage **payment differences** in the **Post Incoming Payments** app? (There are two correct answers.)  
 - A. Partial payment  
 - B. Residual item  
 - C. Change due date  
 - D. Reject payment  

20. When a payment in **foreign currency** clears the amount of the invoice exactly in the foreign currency but in the local currency is more than the invoiced amount, what does the system do?  
 - A. Post to profit from exchange rate differences.  
 - B. Leave the amount as an open item to be reconciled with open amounts in the future.  
 - C. Return the difference back to the customer.  
 - D. Adjust the local currency amount to clear the invoice exactly.  

21. What is the correct order of steps when configuring the **payment programs**?  
 - A. All company codes, paying company codes, payment methods in country, payment methods in company code, bank determination  
 - B. All company codes, payment methods in country, paying company codes, payment methods in company code, bank determination  
 - C. All company codes, bank determination, paying company codes, payment methods in country, payment methods in company code  
 - D. Paying company codes, payment methods in company code, all company codes, payment methods in country, bank determination  

22. In the **payment method settings** for the company code, what options do you have for **payment optimization**? (There are two correct answers.)  
 - A. Optimization by due date  
 - B. Optimization by discount  
 - C. Optimization by bank group  
 - D. Optimization by postal code  

23. What can you change for items that are in the **exceptions list of the payment proposal**? (There are three correct answers.)  
 - A. Payment block  
 - B. Payment term  
 - C. Payment method  
 - D. Bank selection  
 - E. Reason code  

24. On what level do you assign **dunning areas**?  
 - A. Client  
 - B. Company code  
 - C. Functional area  
 - D. Segment  

25. When assigning **dunning charges** to a **dunning procedure**, what options do you have? (There are two correct answers.)  
 - A. Assign a fixed amount without assigning a dunning charge percentage.  
 - B. Assign a fixed amount and a percentage. The system posts the larger amount.  
 - C. Assign a fixed amount and a percentage. The system posts the smaller of the two amounts.  
 - D. Assign a dunning charge percentage without assigning a fixed amount.  

26. True or False: You can assign **correspondence types** directly to a **payment difference reason code**.  
 - A. True  
 - B. False  

27. True or False: You can change all delivered **special general ledger indicators** and assign your own to business processes.  
 - A. True  
 - B. False  

28. At which point is the **down payment request** created in the integrated down payment process with purchasing?  
 - A. Purchase requisition  
 - B. Purchase order  
 - C. Goods receipt  
 - D. Invoice verification  

29. True or False: The **special general ledger indicator** is the only way to post to a customer or supplier using a different **reconciliation account**.  
 - A. True  
 - B. False  

30. Which **KPIs** can you find on the **accounts payable overview page**? (There are two correct answers.)  
 - A. Day sales outstanding  
 - B. Cash discount utilization  
 - C. Aging analysis  
 - D. Collection effectiveness index  

---

## 3.13 Practice Question Answers and Explanations

1. Correct answers: **A, C, D**  
The partner categories are **person**, **organization**, and **group**. These are fixed categories; you can’t change or add any. **Agency** and **public sector** fall into the **organization** category.  

2. Correct answer: **C**  
The only way to correct this is to create a new business partner and mark the erroneous one for deletion. Changing this isn’t a matter of authorization, nor does it make any difference if you’ve posted on the business partner or assigned it to a company code. However, if you’ve posted, the best option is to reverse the documents and repost on the correct business partner.  

3. Correct answer: **B**  
False. You can change the role assignment, and some roles are even designed to be **temporary roles**.  

4. Correct answer: **B**  
False. This is incorrect. You assign the business partner **number range** in the **business partner grouping**. The role grouping is only useful for performing common maintenance of more than one business partner role and has no part in the number range definition.  

5. Correct answer: **C**  
In a new **SAP S/4HANA system**, the **business partner** is defined first and is assigned a number. The customer and supplier created for the business partner inherit the business partner account number.  

6. Correct answers: **C, D**  
This is a bit of a trick question. In the certification, you won’t see trick questions, so kudos if you got this one right! All the objects displayed can have a separate **field status definition**, but only two of them can be considered **business partner objects**: business partner **role** and business partner **type**.  

7. Correct answer: **A**  
The **customer number** can’t be changed. The customer number isn’t an identifying characteristic for **one-time customers** because more than one will share it! You can enter the customer name, industry, country, and other address and bank details during the posting transaction in the special popup window.  

8. Correct answer: **A**  
True. **Bank details**, meaning the business partner’s bank accounts for where they receive and from where they send their payments, are assigned in the **General Data** section and are thus **common** and usable independent of the assigned business partner roles.

## Bank Details in Customer/Supplier Payment

The **bank details** you enter in the customer/supplier payment section (such as **House Bank, Account ID**) are defined **per company code**. These details specify from where the **company code** should pay or receive payments.

---

## Sort Key and Assignment Field

The **sort key** defines what is transferred to the **assignment field** on the line item. Important distinctions include:

- The **assignment** field is where information is transferred.
- The **reference** field is a **document header** field.
- The **line-item text** can carry information but is a **document-level field**, not maintained in the business partner master data.

Remember to carefully read what the question asks to avoid confusion.

---

## Payment Blocking

- An **overall payment block** blocks **both incoming and outgoing payments** and is similar to assigning a block on the customer.
- A **purchasing block** prevents ordering goods from the supplier.
- Blocking the supplier for payment ensures **no automatic payment** of open items without manual supervision.

### Exam Tip

Questions with a lot of text often contain only essential information. Most exam questions are concise, so don't panic if you encounter a longer question.

---

## Head Office/Branch Scenario

- The scenario involves **centralized open item and payment management**.
- There is **no automatic master data synchronization** with the head office.
- Payments are made to the head office where the open items reside.
- Correspondence may be sent either to the head office or branch, depending on **business partner master data settings**.

---

## Day Limit Key and Terms of Payment

- The **day limit key**, along with the **terms of payment**, allows differentiation of payment terms.
- You can define multiple terms of payment, differentiated by the **day limit**.
- Changing payment terms with the same key is done at the **client** level because they are **client-dependent**.

---

## Troubleshooting Payment Terms Configuration

- Incorrect configuration may omit the **supplier account type** in the terms of payment.
- Creating additional payment term records unnecessarily adds complexity.
- Simplifying configurations benefits the end users.

---

## Configuring Installments

- To configure **installments**, create a **base payment term**.
- Assign an **additional payment term** per number of installments.
- In **Customizing**, assign each installment payment term to the base payment term.

---

## Screen Variant in Payment Processing

- A **screen variant** simplifies the **line-item section** of the screen.
- It shows only required fields or a smaller selection of account assignments.
- The **header section** and predefined values are unaffected.

---

## User Maintenance as Consultant

- Use **User Maintenance applications**: **Transaction SU01** or preferably **Transaction SU10**.
- These transactions allow changing **users other than your own**.
- User profiles and default values in **SAP Fiori Launchpad** default for the **logged-on user only**.

---

## CO-PA Characteristics and Universal Journal

- Many sales and distribution fields transfer as **CO-PA characteristics** to the **Universal Journal** line item.
- Information on the line item in the Universal Journal is **available for reporting**, including the **P&L statement**.
- **Account-based CO-PA** is recommended to be activated by default in **SAP S/4HANA**.
- CO-PA updates typically apply to **P&L accounts**, not balance sheet accounts.

---

## Payment Entry Fields

- **Discount Amount** is a **line-item field** as it may vary per cleared item.
- **Payment Terms** usually do not change during payment entry.

---

## Handling Smaller Payments than Open Items

- Use either a **partial payment** or a **residual item**.
- Differences handled manually if needed (post to **general ledger** or post on account).
- There is no functionality to **reject a payment** automatically.
- Changing due dates is irrelevant for posting a payment.

---

## Currency Exchange Differences Posting

- Posting of differences from **currency exchange** is done automatically.
- They post to accounts specified in Customizing for **profits or losses** on exchange rate differences.

---

## Configuration Order for Payments

The correct configuration order is:

1. **All company codes**, assigning paying company codes to those that do not perform payments.
2. **Paying company codes**, configuring codes that perform payments.
3. **Payment methods per country**, defining usable payment methods.
4. **Payment methods per company code**, setting valid methods for each company code.
5. Define **bank determination** for automated payments.

---

## Bank Optimization Settings

- Options include **optimize per bank group** to prioritize paying from the same bank group as business partners.
- Optimize by **postal code** to select the closest preferred bank according to postal codes.

---

## Payment Modification Permissions

You can:

- Remove the **blocking reason** (if allowed by Customizing).
- Enter or change the **payment method**.
- Enter or change the selected **house bank account**.
- Alter the **discount amount** within tolerances.

---

## Dunning Areas

- Used to subdivide **company codes into areas of responsibility** for dunning.
- Assigned at the **company code** level.
- May reflect segments or functional areas but without system assignment or connection.

---

## Dunning Charges

- Dunning charges can be assigned as either an **absolute value** or a **percentage** of the overdue amount.
- Charges are entered **per level** and **per outstanding amount**.
- Both methods are mutually exclusive (cannot select both simultaneously).

---

## Payment Difference Reason Codes

- You can assign a specific **correspondence type** in the payment difference reason codes to generate correspondence regarding differences.

---

## Special General Ledger Accounts

- Certain processes require specific **special general ledger accounts** configured correctly.
- For example, down payment requests use account type **F**, and down payments use **A**.
- These configurations should **not be changed**.

---

## Down Payment in Purchase Order

- Enter a **down payment expected** in the purchase order.
- This creates the **down payment request** in financial accounting.

---

## Reconciliation Account Configuration

- The **reconciliation account field** can be configured as **changeable/selectable** during document posting.
- This configuration may eliminate the need for special general ledger transactions.

---

## Payables vs. Receivables Functions

- Functions related to payables include:
  - **Tracking cash discounts** to maximize discount benefits.
  - Conducting **aging analysis** for payables.
- Receivables KPIs differ and are not applicable in this context.

---

## 3.14 Test Takeaway

You now understand the role of the **business partner** in SAP S/4HANA for **accounts payable** and **accounts receivable** accounting. This includes:

- Configuring **roles and fields** in the business partner master record.
- Integration of business partners with **customers** and **suppliers**.
- Defining, assigning, and using **payment terms** and understanding **baseline date calculation**.
- Configuration and use of **payment installments**.
- Defining and assigning **payment blocking reasons** and **tolerance groups**.
- Posting **incoming and outgoing invoices** directly in financial accounting with integration to purchasing and sales.
- Performing **manual payments** and configuring **automatic payment programs**.
- Managing communication through **dunning** and **correspondence**.

## Summary Section 3.15

**Accounts payable** and **accounts receivable accounting** are very integrated components. They serve as the direct communication point for the **purchasing functionality** and the **sales and distribution functionality**. However, they also offer a complete standalone solution capable of handling many customer and supplier business operations autonomously.

The components are designed to be flexible to adapt to the requirements of your company, **local legal authorities**, and the business partners you do business with. The **SAP S/4HANA system** offers useful applications for processing **payments, dunning, and correspondence**. The functionality is proven and is mainly taken over from the **SAP ERP system**.

With **SAP S/4HANA**, SAP focuses on offering specialized applications that integrate seamlessly with the core SAP S/4HANA product and take advantage of the power and flexibility of **SAP HANA**. For example, one of the latest developments for accounts receivable accounting is to incorporate **machine learning** with **SAP Cash Application**. Manually matching payments to invoices is labor-intensive, but with machine learning, the application can learn payment-matching patterns and significantly boost automatic matching rates.

In the next chapter, we will discuss **asset accounting**, another component with many integration points and its own set of organizational units, master data, and daily and periodic business processes.

---

# Chapter 4  
## Asset Accounting

### Techniques You’ll Master

- Create and maintain **charts of depreciation** and **depreciation areas**
- Create and configure **asset classes**
- Create and maintain **asset master records**
- Process **asset transactions**
- Manage **assets under construction (AUCs)**
- Perform periodic processing and valuation
- Use **asset reporting**

---

### Introduction

The focus of this chapter is to explain **asset accounting processes in SAP S/4HANA**. It covers basic organizational units of asset accounting, such as the **chart of depreciation** and **asset classes**, integration with the **general ledger**, asset accounting transactions, and period-end closing.

---

### Real-World Scenario

**Fixed asset accounting** is one of the most important financial accounting components. Depending on the company and industry, managing fixed assets and their valuations can be a major part of the accounting department's tasks. Fixed assets have their own accounting language that must be understood and translated into system configurations and processes.

As a separate component, **asset accounting** has its own set of organizational units, master records, and daily and periodic activities. It is a very mature product in SAP S/4HANA and can flexibly cover almost all situations.

It’s rare that companies will use a separate specialized system to process fixed assets, and even then, many integration points need to be managed. Designing and performing the migration of fixed assets can be a major activity during a **greenfield implementation project**.

Financial accounting consultants may not always work with fixed assets, which may cause forgetting some details. Those specializing in management accounting might never work directly with fixed assets.

Fixed assets have integration points with:

- **Investment management**
- **Overhead cost accounting**
- **Project system**
- **Purchasing**
- **Plant maintenance**
- Core financial accounting components like **general ledger accounting**, **accounts payable**, and **accounts receivable**

The closer integration of financial accounting with SAP S/4HANA means it's important to have a complete view of all major financial accounting components, especially those sharing the same table via the **Universal Journal architecture**.

---

## 4.1 Objectives of This Portion of the Test

The certification exam tests your knowledge in **asset accounting handling with SAP S/4HANA**. For the exam, you need a good understanding of the following topics:

- **Organizational units** in asset accounting and their integration with the general ledger and controlling
- **Asset class configuration**
- **Asset master records management**
- **Asset transactions**
- **Asset depreciation and valuation configuration**
- **Asset parallel valuation accounting**
- **Assets under construction (AUCs)**
- **Investment support measures**
- **Asset year-end closing**
- **Asset reports**
- **Manual legacy data transfers**

**Note:** Asset accounting makes up **20%** of the total exam.

---

## 4.2 Fixed Asset Accounting

**Asset accounting** in SAP S/4HANA provides the means for managing and monitoring **fixed assets**. It is a subsystem of **financial accounting**. You can use asset reports to get detailed information about actual transactions, current balances, and future planned asset values.

Asset accounting is integrated with other components outside financial accounting. For example, when an asset is purchased or produced in-house, you can directly post the **invoice receipt**, **goods receipt**, or **withdrawal from warehouse** to assets in asset accounting.

All actual asset transactions update the **Universal Journal** directly on the individual asset level. Asset accounting covers the entire lifecycle of an asset, from the **purchase order or initial acquisition** (which can include an **AUC settlement**) to the **asset retirement**.

The system calculates most values for **depreciation, interest**, and others automatically. The transactional information and simulations of future values are accessible using standard reports, either on an individual asset basis or for multiple assets.

Each country has specific basic accounting rules for asset accounting. SAP S/4HANA comes preconfigured with basic settings according to **local principles** for all countries. Most fields are customizable for rule changes or special customer cases.

---

![Figure 4.1 Country Information](image_link_placeholder)  
*Figure 4.1 Country Information - default details for Germany*

---

## 4.3 Chart of Depreciation

A **chart of depreciation** is a directory of **depreciation areas** arranged according to business requirements. It organizes legal requirements for depreciation and valuation of assets.

- Each chart contains rules valid for a specific country or economic area.
- Usually, one chart is created for all company codes in a country.
- You determine the types of valuation and required depreciation areas before implementing asset accounting.

To define a chart of depreciation:

1. Copy a template chart (delivered via SAP Best Practices or standard templates defined for a country).
2. Modify or delete unnecessary depreciation areas.
3. Update the description for the copied chart.

The chart becomes active once assigned to a **company code**. Each company code using asset accounting is assigned to a chart of depreciation. Each asset inherits the valuation settings of the chart through the company code.

---

![Figure 4.2 Copying Chart of Depreciation](image_link_placeholder)  
*Figure 4.2 Copying Chart of Depreciation*

![Figure 4.3 Assigning Company Code to Chart of Depreciation](image_link_placeholder)  
*Figure 4.3 Assigning the Company Code to the Chart of Depreciation*

---

## 4.4 Depreciation Areas

**Depreciation areas** calculate fixed asset values according to different accounting principles or other valuation purposes. They manage depreciation terms and values necessary for valuation assigned to each asset.

- A depreciation area can update the **general ledger** via posting or calculate **statistical values** for reporting.
- A chart of depreciation can have up to **99 depreciation areas**.

In SAP S/4HANA, create a depreciation area for each additional **currency type** maintained at the ledger/company code level for currency availability across valuations.

- Depreciation areas have **two-digit numeric keys**.
- Assign a meaningful description to each area.
- Each area must be assigned to an **accounting principle** and, through it, to a **ledger group**.

---

![Figure 4.4 Depreciation Area Definition](image_link_placeholder)  
*Figure 4.4 Depreciation Area Definition within the Chart of Depreciation*

---

### 4.4.1 Configuration

Each depreciation area’s details screen allows further configuration. Main settings include:

- **Real Depreciation Area**  
  Values are normally committed to the **database**. If unchecked, the area is a **derived area** based on other areas' values.

- **Area Does Not Post**  
  Used for areas created purely for **reporting purposes** (e.g., other currencies).

- **Area Posts in Real Time**  
  Standard for depreciation areas that post **acquisition and production costs (APC)** and **depreciation** to the general ledger when using the **ledger approach** for parallel valuation. Only one area posts in real time with the **accounts approach**.

- **Area Posts Depreciation Only**  
  Areas that post only **depreciation**, not APC values. Commonly used for **cost-controlling valuations**.

- **Area Posts APC Immediately, Depreciation Periodically**  
  Used in the **accounts approach** for areas posting both types of values, except the real-time posting area.

- **Value Maintenance**  
  Contains rules defining allowed value types for various valuations.

**Tip:**  
Depreciation is always posted **periodically**; real-time posting of depreciation does not exist because it is periodic by nature. However, **depreciation calculation** is a **real-time activity** performed whenever asset value or useful life changes.

## 4.4.2 Derived Depreciation Areas

**Derived depreciation areas** are usually areas for which the values are calculated from combining values of two or more other areas (adding or subtracting values from each), as shown in Figure 4.6. They are commonly **delta areas**, which provide an immediate view of the difference between two valuations.

**Tip:**  
Derived areas were common in **SAP ERP** because they were required for handling **parallel asset accounting** with ledgers before the introduction of new asset accounting with **SAP ERP 6.0 EHP 7**.  

---

## 4.5 Asset Class

The **asset class** is the main structuring element for fixed assets. You can define any number of asset classes in the system, with the definition at the **client level** (Figure 4.7). Asset classes structure your fixed assets according to criteria such as **type of asset**, **default valuation settings**, and others. All assets are assigned to an asset class when created.

The **SAP S/4HANA** system includes common asset class categories preconfigured with **SAP Best Practices** packages. You can create additional asset classes as needed by your customer.

When creating an asset class, you define the following:  
- The four-digit code (**Class**)  
- Long text (**Asset Class Description**)  
- Short Text  

You can also create new asset classes by copying an existing one, which automatically copies the default values of the depreciation area section.

### Asset Class Details

In the asset class details (Figure 4.8), you define:

- **Account determ.**: Controls the **general ledger accounts** posted for various asset transactions.  
- **Scr.Layout Rule**: Controls the fields available for input during asset master record maintenance.  
- **Number range**: Controls the asset number assigned upon saving the master record.  
- **Status of AuC**: Determines whether the asset class is used to create **Assets Under Construction (AUCs)**.

In a separate **Customizing transaction**, you can store default values for fields per asset class, including the **master data section** and the **depreciation section** with entries per depreciation area. These values are proposed but changeable.

If you want to ensure specific fields are filled with specific values, you can define and use a **substitution rule**.

---

## 4.6 Account Determination

You can post both **asset balance sheet values** and **depreciation values** from individual depreciation areas to separate **balance sheet accounts** or **income statement accounts** in the **general ledger**, as shown in Figure 4.9.

Accounts are specified per **chart of accounts** and **depreciation area** individually in the **account determination key**. You define account determination keys in asset accounting Customizing and assign the key to particular asset classes after configuration.

### Key Points on Account Determination

- Account determination keys usually share similar codification and naming as their relevant asset classes.
- The same account determination key can be assigned to many asset classes, but customers may prefer assigning different keys for maximum flexibility.
- Account determination details are maintained per **chart of depreciation** and **chart of accounts** to support specific reporting needs of any company code in any country.
- On a detailed level, specific **balance sheet** and **profit and loss (P&L)** accounts are maintained for any asset transaction relevant to the supported asset classes (Figure 4.10).
- Using the **ledger approach** to parallel accounting allows all depreciation areas to have the same account definitions, with posting differentiated by ledger group.
- Using the **accounts approach** requires maintaining separate account sets per depreciation area to avoid conflicting postings.
- All balance sheet accounts defined in account determination are **asset reconciliation accounts**.

---

## 4.7 Screen Layouts

The **screen layout** for the asset determines which fields in the **asset master records** are used. For each field in the asset master record, you specify whether it is **required**, **optional**, **display-only**, or **suppressed (hidden)**.

You configure different sets of keys for:

- The **master data section** of an asset  
- The **depreciation details**

You define **screen layout rules** for the master record section and assign them to asset classes (Figure 4.11). The same screen layout can be valid for multiple asset classes. The **logical field groups** and fields inside these groups are predefined.

### Additional Field Status Options

Besides defining the field status, you can select additional checkboxes for:

- **Class (asset class)**: Allows setting a default value for this field on the asset class level.  
- **MnNo. (main asset number)**: Allows the field to be changed on the main asset master level.  
- **Sbno. (asset subnumber)**: Allows the field to be changed for the asset subnumber. If not selected, the value is inherited from the main asset and cannot be changed.  
- **Copy**: Determines whether the field value is copied from a reference asset when creating another asset.

You can also maintain the **tab layout** of asset master maintenance by assigning logical field groups to tabs (Figure 4.12). The goal is to make all needed fields available without overwhelming users with too many fields.

Depreciation screen layouts are assigned per asset and **depreciation area** (Figure 4.12). A default layout per depreciation area is proposed per asset class. SAP provides two depreciation screen layouts by default, which you can copy and customize.

Possible field definitions are the same as for master record layouts.

---

## 4.8 User-Defined Fields

Assets are complex accounting subjects, and customers have various field requirements. **SAP S/4HANA** offers **custom fields** that customers can define for their own purposes.

All custom fields can be used as **reporting criteria**, allowing selection, filtering, and display of values in reports.

### Custom Fields Available for Definition

- **Evaluation Groups 1 to 5**: Flexible fields to store any information. Four keys are four digits long, and one key is eight digits long. Each key can have a description and a default value set per asset class if allowed by screen layout definition.  
- **Environmental Protection**: Checkbox to save the reason for an environmental protection investment.  
- **Reason for Investment**: Field to enter an explanation for capital expenditure.  
- **Asset Super Number**: Can be assigned to assets for grouping purposes.

---

## 4.9 Asset Master Data

**Asset master records** mirror your fixed assets used in daily business. Master data includes the **main asset number** and the **asset subnumber** (an asset referring to a main number).

### Methods to Create Asset Master Records

- Enter the **company code** and **asset class**, input required data, and adapt standard values proposed by the asset class.  
- Enter a **reference asset** and change fields proposed from the copy of the referenced asset.

You can also create multiple asset master records by entering the number of similar assets to be created. In this case, maintain values for the first asset and either use the same details for all other assets or maintain separate values for specific fields (Figure 4.13). The range of changeable fields is customizable, and changes can be made after save.

### Time-Dependent Assignments

In the **Time-Dependent** tab of the default layout, you assign:

- **Cost accounting objects** such as cost centers, internal orders, and work breakdown structure (WBS) elements  
- Location, profit center, and **segment**

Assignments are period-dependent, allowing assets like printers to be allocated to different departments or cost centers over time. Reports and depreciation postings use the values valid for the selected period/year.

### Asset Subnumber Functionality

An **asset subnumber** is a separate asset still connected to the main asset number. The main asset gets the subnumber 0. Each subnumber shares the same asset number but has a separate subnumber.

- Subnumbers can be defined as **internal** or **external** assignment.  
- External assignment is usually internal during data migration and reverted to internal after completion.  
- Used to monitor **subsequent improvements** or report on **asset components** via subnumbers.  
- Subnumbers generally inherit data from the main asset, with inherited fields defined in field status Customizing.

---

## 4.10 Integration with Plant Maintenance

**Equipment** is the main master record in the **plant maintenance** component of the SAP S/4HANA system. SAP provides standard integration between the **fixed asset master record** and **equipment**.

- Equipment numbers can be entered manually in the asset master record or updated in the equipment master record.
- An asset can be assigned to multiple equipment master records, but an equipment record can only be assigned to one asset (Figure 4.14).

### Configuration of Integration (Figure 4.15)

1. Configure the system to **create and assign an equipment master record** when creating a new asset master record.  
2. Configure the system to **change account assignments** of the asset when the equipment changes, and vice versa.

## 4.11 Asset Transaction Types

Every transaction in **asset accounting** carries an **asset transaction type**. There are groups of transaction types for specific operations:

- **Acquisitions**
- **Retirements**
- **Transfers**
- **Postcapitalizations**
- **Investment support measures**
- **Depreciations**
- **Write-ups**

The group a transaction type is assigned to defines many basic characteristics for the transaction, such as which **value fields** are updated, the valid **fiscal year** (current or previous), the **sign** (positive, negative) of the sum of postings for a fiscal year, and more. These **transaction type groups** are hardcoded system settings and cannot be changed.

Each transaction type has a set of **controls** that you configure. These specifications can differ according to the transaction type group. Depending on the transaction type group, you define settings such as:

- **Debit/credit**
- **Capitalize/retire**
- **Document type**
- **Posting to affiliated company**
- **Post gross/net**
- **Asset history sheet group**

In Figure 4.16, you can see the definitions maintained for **transaction type 100** of **group 10 (Acquisition)**. The **SAP S/4HANA** system comes with transaction types preconfigured to cover most customers' requirements.

---

## 4.12 Asset Acquisitions

An **asset acquisition** capitalizes an asset and usually signifies the start of **depreciation calculation**. There are three basic ways to post external acquisitions in **SAP S/4HANA**:

- **Acquisition with automatic offsetting**
- **Acquisition integrated with accounts payable**
- **Asset acquisition with purchase order integrated with materials management**

### 4.12.1 Acquisition with Automatic Offsetting

The **acquisition with automatic offsetting** entry is often used to capitalize an asset when the **invoice** isn't yet received or has been posted to the supplier already. The system debits the **asset** and credits a predefined **offsetting account**. The offsetting entry will balance back to zero with the pending (or posted) invoice entry.

For example, if an asset is worth **$10,000 USD**:

| Line Item | Account           | Debit/Credit | Amount   |
|-----------|-------------------|--------------|----------|
| 1         | Asset clearing    | Debit        | $10,000  |
| 2         | Offsetting account| Credit       | $10,000  |

When the invoice is posted with **10% tax**:

| Line Item | Account          | Debit/Credit | Amount   |
|-----------|------------------|--------------|----------|
| 1         | Supplier account | Credit       | $11,000  |
| 2         | Offsetting account| Debit        | $10,000  |
| 3         | Tax account      | Debit        | $1,000   |

On the initial screen for posting acquisition (Figure 4.17), you can:

- Select an existing **asset master record** or create one on the fly
- Post to a specific **accounting principle** or **depreciation area**
- Enter minimum fields such as **Description**, **Asset Class**, and **Cost Center**
- Use **MasterData** button to fill in additional details
- Post to **multiple assets** simultaneously

The transaction requires date definitions, amount, quantity (if valid), and line-item text.

Figure 4.18 shows the **additional details screen** where:

- **Document type**, **Offsetting Account**, and **Transaction Type** fields are automatically filled based on Customizing settings
- Other fields are optional and blank by default

### 4.12.2 Acquisition Integrated with Accounts Payable

This method is used when purchasing an asset **without a purchase order**. It updates both **accounts payable** and **asset accounts** in a single step.

An example posting (single asset acquisition) shows:

| Line Item | Account          | Debit/Credit | Amount   |
|-----------|------------------|--------------|----------|
| 1         | Supplier         | Credit       | $11,000  |
| 2         | Asset clearing   | Debit        | $10,000  |
| 3         | Tax              | Debit        | $1,000   |

You use the **complex posting screen** to enter this document:

- Fill **document header** first
- Build each line item in separate screen
- Manually enter **posting key** (70 to debit asset) and **transaction type** (100 for acquisition)
- Add more asset acquisition lines by entering posting key, asset account, and transaction type
- Use **More** button to enter **Reference Date** (asset capitalization date)

Figure 4.19 displays the line item entry for accounts payable integrated acquisition.

### 4.12.3 Asset Acquisition with Purchase Order Integrated with Materials Management

This is the most common acquisition method for companies. The posting is similar to accounts payable integrated posting, but includes **purchase order details** and is posted through the **materials management invoice verification**.

Document flow:

- **(Optional) Purchase Requisition:** Often the first purchasing step. May assign a specific asset master record here.
- **Purchase Order:** Required step for asset buying. Assign **category “A”** in order line item to enter an asset in account assignment.
- Decision to post a **valuated goods receipt**:
  - **Valuated Goods Receipt:** Capitalizes the asset at goods receipt posting value.
  - **Invoice Receipt:** Adjusts asset value if necessary.
  - **Nonvaluated Goods Receipt:** Asset not updated during goods receipt; values posted on invoice receipt; goods receipt date used as capitalization date.

In integrated external acquisitions:

- System posts entry document **without ledger group specification**
- Debits **asset clearing account**
- Creates additional **accounting-principle-specific documents** for each accounting principle
  - These balance the technical clearing account back to zero
  - Debit actual **asset reconciliation account**, credit asset clearing account

For example, if updating two accounting principles:

- One operational document debits asset clearing account
- Two accounting-principle-specific documents for each principle debit the same clearing account

Figure 4.20 shows asset accounting view. Switch accounting principles by selecting **AP/Currency 1**. The **Document Header Info** displays which principle is visible:

- **IFRS** document posted to ledger group **0L 2**
- Local **GAAP** document posted to ledger group **2L 3**

The **asset technical clearing account** is a general ledger account not entered in asset account determination. Separate configuration defines this account for integrated acquisition.

Accounting-principle-specific documents may use a different **document type** from the entry document:

- Supplier invoices use **document type KR**
- Accounting-principle-specific documents post as document type **AA** (asset document)

#### Note

- For the **ledger approach to parallel valuation**, the operational document is identical.
- For the **accounts approach**, one accounting-principle-specific document clears asset technical clearing account, other documents post clearing balance to a different clearing account.
- This happens because in the accounts approach all postings are made to the **leading ledger**.
- Zero balance is achieved by matching the asset technical clearing account with the **acquisition offsetting account** defined per depreciation area.
- All depreciation areas in accounts approach must be assigned to a **ledger group/accounting principle**, but all ledger groups map to a single **leading ledger**.

### 4.12.4 Gross and Net Document Types

The standard system provides two types of **document types** for asset capitalization posting:

- **Gross Document Type**

  - Examples: **AA**, **KR**
  - Capitalizes the full invoice amount **minus tax**
  - **Cash discounts** are ignored

  ![Figure 4.21 Gross Entry: Cash Discount Ignored](#)

- **Net Document Type**

  - Examples: **AN**, **KN**
  - Capitalizes invoice amount minus tax and minus anticipated **cash discount** based on payment terms

  ![Figure 4.22 Net Entry: Cash Discount Considered](#)

## Asset Acquisitions Section 4.12

### Net Entry: Cash Discount Considered

**Note:**  
At the time of payment of the invoice, the amount capitalized for a **net posting** will be recalculated if the **cash discount** differs from the one calculated during posting. This adjustment will occur automatically in a company code with **document splitting** activated. If document splitting isn’t active, you can execute the **Profit and Loss Adjustment** program to correct the capitalization amounts for the relevant asset, as shown in Figure 4.23.

---

## 4.13 Asset Retirements

There are two basic ways to perform **asset retirements**: **scrapping** and **selling**. Both lead to the asset being removed from your asset registry, as opposed to assets that have been fully **depreciated**, which remain, even with no accounting value.

**Asset sales to customers** are generally performed through **financial accounting**, not sales and distribution, because selling assets usually isn’t a normal business activity for most companies. The posting is performed through the **complex posting transaction**, similar to acquisition integrated with the supplier.

### 4.13.1 Posting an Asset Sale Invoice

To post an asset sale invoice:  
- **Debit the customer**  
- **Credit the general ledger Revenue from Fixed Asset Sale account**  

You don’t credit the asset directly with posting key 75 and a sale transactions type. The **revenue account** has a special configuration provided by its **field status group** to accommodate asset retirements. When using this account, you mark the **Asst. Retirement checkbox**, and the system produces a popup window to enter details for the asset sale (see Figure 4.24).

### 4.13.2 Creating Asset Retirement

The **Create Asset Retirement** popup window (refer to Figure 4.24) is where you enter definitions for the following:

- **Asset:** The asset (or asset subnumber) the sale concerns. Only a single asset per line can be entered; add lines crediting the revenue from the fixed asset sale account as needed.  
- **Transaction Type:** The retirement transaction type with the default **210** for a normal asset sale in the current fiscal year proposed by the system. You can change this if required.  
- **Asset Val. Date:** The asset value date is the date for calculations in asset accounting. This date is very important for calculating the **profit or loss from the asset sale**.  
- **Compl. Retiremnt:** This checkbox indicates whether the asset is to be fully or partially retired.

**Tip:**  
If performing a **partial retirement**, indicate the retirement amount, retirement quantity (if relevant), or the percentage of the asset to be retired. The system adjusts the values accordingly, and the asset will remain in the asset registry of the company with the reduced value.

### 4.13.3 Asset Sale Line Items

When performing a retirement, the system calculates all related values automatically and updates all **accounting principles** and **gain/loss accounts**. In Figure 4.25, you can see an example of the lines generated for an asset sale.  

- The lines without the **ledger group** are manually entered during posting (customer, revenue from asset sale).  
- Other lines are generated automatically and are **accounting-principle-specific**.

Calculations depend on values for each accounting principle and different **depreciation amounts**. The system calculates the depreciation up to the asset value date.

**Example:**  
- Asset sold for **$50,000 USD**  
- Acquisition value: **$40,000 USD**  
- Depreciation up to sale: **$2,500 USD**  
- Profit for the sale: **$12,500 USD**  

The revenue from the asset sale is balanced by the clearing from the asset disposal account. Posting is similar for other accounting principles (only values and ledger group vary). Note that it’s possible to have a **profit in one accounting principle** and a **loss in another**, with adjustments made accordingly.

You can also perform asset sales **without customer integration**. This transaction looks like a nonintegrated asset acquisition with an added tab for partial retirement specifications (see Figure 4.25).

A similar application is used for **asset scrapping**, except that there is no customer and no revenue, meaning **no profit**. Partial scrapping can also be performed by selecting amount, percentage, or value. The application supports scrapping for multiple assets.

### 4.13.4 Retirements Worklist

The **SAP S/4HANA system** offers the possibility to perform retirements (nonintegrated sale or scrapping) using a **worklist**. The steps are:

1. Execute the report with specific selection criteria to select the exact assets to retire.  
2. Create a worklist for the items, indicating the purpose as **Retirement without revenue** or **Retirement with revenue** (see Figure 4.26).  
3. If there is revenue, distribute it to selected assets.  
4. Edit and release the worklist.

---

## 4.14 Asset Transfers

**Asset transfers** are transactions that remove values from one asset and transfer the same value to another. 

Two types of transfers are supported: **intracompany** and **intercompany**.

### 4.14.1 Intracompany Transfers

An **intracompany asset transfer** is performed within a company code between two asset master records of the same or different asset classes (see Figure 4.27).

Main reasons for posting an asset transfer:  
- The initial asset wasn’t created in the right asset class; create a new asset (correct class) and transfer values.  
- To transfer part or full value of the asset to different assets to better depict asset components (e.g., track location).

**Note:**  
You could also use the asset transfer to settle **Assets Under Construction (AUCs)**, but this isn’t the recommended method.

### 4.14.2 Intercompany Transfer

An **intercompany transfer** represents the transfer of an asset from one company code to another within the same corporate group (see Figure 4.28).  

- The system posts a **retirement** for the sending company and an **acquisition** for the receiving company code.  
- At the corporate group level, this transfer should **balance to zero** in the group asset history sheet.

Reasons for intercompany transfer:  
- The asset has moved and needs to be reassigned to a new company code.  
- Corporate reorganization requires assignment of assets to a different company code.

A key distinction:  
- If the company codes are assigned to the **same company**, the transfer is posted as a **transfer**.  
- If assigned to **different companies**, the system posts a **retirement** in the sending company and an **acquisition** in the receiving company.

### 4.14.3 Transfer Methods

The **transfer method** (refer to Specifications for Revenue in Figure 4.28) defines how values are transferred between assets. Three transfer types exist:  

- **Gross Method:** Transfers the **historic values** of the asset to the new asset (see Table 4.4).  
- **Net Method:** Transfers the **net book value** of the sender to the receiver (see Table 4.5).  
- **New Value Method:** Capitalizes the new asset at a manually entered **revenue amount** (see Table 4.6).

In cases where company codes use different charts of depreciation with mismatched depreciation areas, you can create **cross-company-code** (or cross-system) **depreciation areas** to map depreciation areas between the differing charts.  

- These mapped areas share functionality across charts but have different keys.  
- The cross-company depreciation area is defined only by a key and description; it carries no depreciation definitions.

| Asset Acquisition and Production Cost | Accumulated Depreciation |
|--------------------------------------|--------------------------|
| **Sender:** 20,000                    | 4,000                    |
| **Receiver:** 20,000                  | 4,000                    |

*Table 4.4 Gross Method*

| Asset Acquisition and Production Cost | Accumulated Depreciation |
|--------------------------------------|--------------------------|
| **Sender:** 20,000                    | 4,000                    |
| **Receiver:** 16,000                  |                          |

*Table 4.5 Net Method*

| Asset Acquisition and Production Cost | Accumulated Depreciation |
|--------------------------------------|--------------------------|
| **Sender:** 20,000                    | 4,000                    |
| **Receiver:** 15,000                  |                          |

*Table 4.6 New Value Method*

---

## 4.15 Low-Value Assets

**Low-value assets (LVAs)** are always completely depreciated in the **year of acquisition**. Generally, their values are not reported individually.  

LVAs are maintained in specific **LVA asset classes**. In **Customizing**, you configure the maximum asset value to be considered an LVA, done at the **country level** (see Figure 4.29), but it can be specified at lower levels, including per company code and depreciation area.

LVAs can be managed:  

- **Individually:** Acquisition value of the single asset is compared to maximum amounts per depreciation area.  
- **Collectively:** Acquisition value is divided by the quantity entered, then compared to maximum amounts.

---

## 4.16 Assets Under Construction

**Assets Under Construction (AUCs)** require a separate asset class since they must be displayed in separate accounts for the financial statement.

An **AUC**:  
- Does **not post depreciation**, ensured by assigned **depreciation key 0000** (see Figure 4.30).  

**Tip:**  
You can calculate depreciation for internal reporting on a depreciation area that doesn’t post values.

Special tax depreciation and **investment support** can be posted to an AUC. Even when fully capitalized, AUCs can receive **credit memos**, meaning **negative APC values** must be permitted.

When AUCs move from the under-construction phase to the useful life phase, values are transferred to one or more **final assets**. This transfer can be:  

- A **one-step summary settlement** (e.g., an intracompany asset transfer)  
- Or via **line-item management**, allowing controlled capitalization of posted values per depreciation area.

You must:  

- Assign a **settlement profile** to the company code.  
- Define **distribution rules** per expenditure and depreciation area to specify the value percentage or amount allocated to each final asset.

## Figure 4.30 Asset Under Construction Depreciation

In **Figure 4.31**, you can see an example of an **Asset Under Construction (AUC)** with five separate lines. Three lines represent the **IFRS accounting principle** and two represent the **local GAAP**. 

The green traffic light in the first column indicates the **settlement rule** is maintained.

## Figure 4.31 Settlement Maintenance per Line on Assets Under Construction

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

### Definition of the Settlement Rule

In **Figure 4.32**, the definition of the settlement rule is displayed. 

- **Cat column**: Defines the **settlement category** (e.g., fixed asset or cost center).  
- **Settlement Receiver column**: Specifies the **settlement receiver**.  
- **% column**: Defines the **settlement percentage**.

You don’t have to perform a full settlement of the asset values because the AUC project might continue to produce other assets, or the remaining value might be posted as an **operating expense**.

## 4.17 Investment Support Measures
