Many countries provide **financial incentives** for certain types of investments in assets. These **subsidies** are managed in the **SAP S/4HANA Cloud system** through the **investment support functionality**.

Investment measures are configured per **depreciation area**, which is specific to an **accounting principle** (usually the local accounting principle). The depreciation area must support **investment support measures**.

### Defining an Investment Measure (Customizing)

In **Figure 4.33**, you can see the customizing details for investment support measures. When defining an investment measure, you enter:

- **Invest.Support**: Name and description of the investment support.  
- **Support Area**: Depreciation areas where the measure should be managed.  
- **Valid From/Valid To**: Validity period of the investment measure.  
- **Max.perc.rate**: Maximum percentage rate (regarding **Asset Purchase Cost (APC)**) and/or maximum amount. The system compares posted amounts to this limit and uses the lower value.  
- **Base Area**: Base depreciation area from which asset **APC** values are derived.  
- **Retention Per.**: Minimum period to keep an asset before invalidating support if sold early. The system allows selling before this period but may require repayment.  
- **Per.From**: Start date for the retention period (e.g., capitalization date or ordinary depreciation start date).  
- **Repayment type for premature retirement**: Used if the asset is retired early.  
- **Time-Dependent Data**: Account assignment for all transactions relating to the support measure.  
- **Default Values & Check Specifications**: Plausibility check for assigning a support measure to an asset.

You input the **investment support keys** in the asset master data. Although there is no limit to the number of keys per asset, each must have a different depreciation area if assigned to the same asset.

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

## Asset Depreciation

### Posting Investment Support Values

You post investment support using special **transaction types**, where "##" corresponds to the investment measure code:

- **I##**: Claiming investment support.  
- **K##**: Postcapitalization (claims and value adjustments).  
- **J##**: Write-offs from asset retirements (without obligation to repay support value).

### Handling Investment Support Measures

Depending on **legal accounting requirements**, investment support measures can be handled in two ways:

- **Liabilities side**: Shown as a special **reserve**, depreciated separately and posted on a separate depreciation area.  
- **Assets side**: Reduce the **APC price** and are depreciated on the same depreciation area as general ledger depreciation.

The system offers more automation on the **liability side**, such as issuing warnings and automatic posting in case of retirements before the retention period ends.

## 4.18 Asset Depreciation

**Depreciation posting** is a periodic activity executed during **period-end closing**. The depreciation is calculated and stored in the asset accounting component **after any asset transaction** or master data change that might influence depreciation.

The system uses the **calculated depreciation values** when posting depreciation; the depreciation calculation is not redone during posting.

### 4.18.1 Calculation of Depreciation

Depreciation calculation is based on **depreciation keys** assigned per **depreciation area**. 

The **calculation methods** control how each depreciation key works. Types include:

- **Base method**  
- **Declining balance method**  
- **Maximum amount method**  
- **Multilevel method**  
- **Period control method**

New depreciation keys are created to comply with new legal regulations, often by copying and modifying existing methods. When a new key is assigned to assets, a **recalculation of depreciation** updates planned depreciation values.

**Figure 4.34** shows the assignment of a calculation method to a depreciation key.

If the **APC value** changes in the year (e.g., partial sale), depreciation already posted stays unchanged, but depreciation in future periods is adjusted based on the remaining period. The system catches up differences immediately in the following period.

### 4.18.2 Time-Dependent Depreciation Definitions

You can define **time-dependent changes** to an asset’s depreciation terms by specifying a new period interval from which new depreciation settings take effect.

Time-dependent definitions include:

- **Depreciation key**  
- **Useful life** (year or period)  
- **Variable depreciation portion**  
- **Absolute or percentage scrap value**

When using time dependency, the system does **not** smooth values over remaining periods. Changes must comply with the depreciation area's value rule definitions.

**Figure 4.35** shows detailed depreciation area definitions for an asset. Selecting **More Intervals** leads to **Figure 4.36**, displaying the intervals.

### 4.18.3 Depreciation Posting Run

The **depreciation posting run** posts depreciation to the **general ledger accounts** in financial accounting.

- The transaction **debits** the depreciation expense account.  
- It **credits** the accumulated depreciation account per asset and depreciation area based on asset class account determination.

For example, with 100,000 active assets and three depreciation areas posting depreciation, the system posts **300,000 document line items**.

**Figure 4.37** shows scheduling the asset depreciation run.

Advantages of detailed posting include:

- **No need for reconciliation**: Single source of truth for reporting.  
- **Depreciation posts even if some assets cause errors**: The system posts depreciation for all possible assets and allows re-executing depreciation to post missing lines after corrections.

Because one side posts to an **expense account**, the system also posts to a **controlling account assignment** (usually the cost center on the asset master record).

The depreciation program runs **in the background**, usually during off-peak hours. Test runs can be executed:

- **Online** for up to 1,000 assets.  
- **As background jobs** for unlimited assets.

Testing helps identify assets with errors before committing the actual run. The system outputs a log after posting, showing details for each line item per depreciation area, as in **Figure 4.38**. Similar logs are available for test runs.

© 2024 by **Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

## 4.19 Asset Year-End Process

Asset accounting balances are line items in the **Universal Journal**. The **carryforward** for these items is executed through the **balance carryforward program** in general ledger accounting.

This is usually done near the end of the fiscal year or the start of a new fiscal year. Balance carryforward must be successful to post in asset accounting for the new fiscal year.

You can have up to **two fiscal years open simultaneously**:

- Open a new fiscal year with balance carryforward.  
- Close the previous fiscal year when no further transactions occur.

If two fiscal years are open already, you cannot post to a third year until one is closed.

### Closing a Fiscal Year

Close a fiscal year using the:

- **Year-end closing program** (shown in **Figure 4.39**).  
- **SAP GUI app: Display Settings for Company Code in Asset Accounting** (shown in **Figure 4.40**).

The program ensures:

- All **depreciation is posted fully**.  
- No **assets contain errors**.

Upon successful closing, posting in that fiscal year is blocked. If needed, you can **reopen a fiscal year** by ledger/depreciation area and must close it again through the year-end program.

## 4.20 Asset Reporting

**Asset reporting** is how you keep track of all the **asset balances** and **transactions**, and how you can simulate **depreciation values** in future periods. There are two basic report categories: reports for **individual assets** and reports for **multiple assets**. We’ll go over the most important reports for each category.

### 4.20.1 Asset Accounting Overview

With the **Asset Accounting Overview** app (Figure 4.41), you can view multiple **key performance indicators (KPIs)** and **asset accounting reports** in a single screen. The app can be used as a central operations and information hub. You can drag and drop cards to organize reports according to your priorities. Filters and built-in navigation links to related apps are available.

The following is a list of key reports the app displays:

- **Asset Balances**  
  Shows total planned asset **net book values** as of the end of the current fiscal period.
  
- **Asset Acquisitions**  
  Shows the total value of acquisitions within the selected period.
  
- **Asset Retirements**  
  Shows the total value of retirements within the selected period.
  
- **Open Purchase Orders (Account Assignment A)**  
  Shows relevant items by either **Value Still to Be Invoiced** or **Value Still to Be Delivered**.
  
- **Asset Transactions by Period**  
  Shows the proportion of acquisitions and retirements in the selected period.
  
- **Depreciation to Be Posted**  
  Shows value to be posted by **depreciation type** for the current period.
  
- **Asset Depreciation Values**  
  Shows asset depreciation values for the current period.
  
- **Asset Master Worklist**  
  Shows current number of assets by status.
  
- **Assets Under Construction (AUC)**  
  Shows AUCs in the current period.
  
- **Asset Transactions**  
  Shows acquisitions and retirements displayed by **Asset Class**, **Account Determination**, and other characteristics.
  
- **Origin of Assets**  
  Shows asset origin displayed either by **Country** or **Supplier**.

---

### 4.20.2 Asset Value Report

The most important report for checking values for an individual asset is the **Asset Values** app (also called the **asset explorer** in SAP GUI), shown in Figure 4.42. You get a complete overview of the planned and posted values of the asset per depreciation area and year. 

You can check and directly display the transactions posted to the asset in the year as well as see and drill down to related objects such as **cost center**, **general ledger account**, **supplier**, and so on. You can perform **value simulations** based on what-if scenarios, such as changing the **depreciation key**.

In the **Comparisons** tab, you can compare values (plan and actual) between different depreciation areas. You can also view the details and valuation methods of the **depreciation key** assigned to the asset and selected depreciation area.

---

### 4.20.3 Manage Fixed Assets

The **Manage Fixed Assets** app gives you a fast overview of both **master data** and **asset values**, including simulated **net book values** per depreciation area (Figure 4.43). 

You can attach files in multiple formats and add text notes for the fixed asset. The **Compare Values** function lets you compare planned depreciation and residual net book value of the asset across multiple depreciation areas.

---

### 4.20.4 Asset Balances Report

The **Asset Balances** report provides a quick overview of balances for multiple assets, as shown in Figure 4.44. The following fields are mandatory when executing the report:

- Asset range
- Company code
- Ledger
- Depreciation area
- Year
- Currency type
- Period up to which the values should be selected

Additional filters include **general ledger account**, **asset class**, etc. 

The output displays various key figures such as **APC value**, **depreciation posted**, and **net book value**. Predelivered key figure variants are available for different purposes. Using the **Navigation Panel**, you can add or remove report characteristics to rows and columns. Export to Microsoft Excel is supported for further calculations.

---

### 4.20.5 Asset History Sheet

The **Asset History Sheet** (Figure 4.45) is a **legal requirement** in some countries. SAP offers predefined layouts covering local legal requirements.

This report is similar to the Asset Balances report but uses a specific **key figure group** and focuses on showing changes to asset values within a year. You can create your own key figure groups in **Customizing**.

---

## 4.21 Asset Legacy Data Transfer

**Data migration** of legacy data from a previous system to an **SAP S/4HANA system** is a critical process. You must match the settings of the old system, whether **SAP ERP** (usually easier) or a **non-SAP system**. A mass transfer method is typically used for data migration.

The newest and best method for migration in most areas, including assets, is to use the **SAP S/4HANA migration cockpit**.

### 4.21.1 Migration Preparation Customizing

Prepare for data migration in the system by performing the following **Customizing** steps per company code in the **Legacy Data Transfer** tab of Transaction **FAA_CMP_LDT** (Figure 4.46):

1. Ensure the **company code status** allows data migration.  
2. Define the **document type** to be used while posting. In the standard system, document type **UE** is predefined for all migration activities.  
3. Define the **takeover date** per company code. This is the date of the last period closed in the legacy system. Up to this date, SAP S/4HANA uses **legacy system values**; from this date forward, SAP calculates its own values.  
4. Define the **offsetting account** for legacy data transfer. This general ledger account is used to transfer asset balances.

> **Note:**  
> The **asset offsetting account** is assigned in a financial statement item with other accounts for legacy data transfer (e.g., other general ledger account balances and customer/supplier open items). The total of all accounts for the legacy data transfer must balance to zero once all migration activities are complete.

---

### 4.21.2 Performing Manual Data Migration

The process to manually create a legacy asset is similar to asset creation during normal operation, but you must:

- Enter the **capitalization date** manually.  
- Usually input the **Original Asset**, corresponding to the asset number in the legacy system (Figure 4.47).  

The transaction used is different: **Transaction AS91**, accessed through SAP GUI.

You post transfer values using a separate step (**Transaction ABLDT**, Figure 4.48). The system posts a separate **Universal Journal** entry for takeover values of each asset by:

- Debiting the asset account  
- Crediting the accumulated depreciation  
- Crediting the remaining balance to the offsetting account defined

---

### 4.21.3 Performing Data Migration with the Migration Cockpit

The **migration cockpit** works with **XML templates** for which you maintain actual data in Microsoft Excel (Figure 4.49). Templates are available directly from the migration cockpit in the system. 

In **SAP S/4HANA 2020**, access the migration cockpit through **Transaction LTMC** in SAP GUI. Select **asset accounting** from many available migration objects (Figure 4.50). The cockpit identifies **dependent objects** such as **cost centers** that must be migrated first.

After filling in the template, upload the file. The system automatically:

- Validates data (Figure 4.51)  
- Proposes required missing mapping  
- Identifies other file issues (Figure 4.52)  

Once data is corrected, simulate migration, validate, then run the actual migration. Initial uploads should be done in the **quality system** before production.

---

### Additional Legacy Data Transfer Methods

- **Legacy data transfer using Microsoft Excel** (Transaction **AS100**)  
  An example form is shown in Figure 4.53.

- **Legacy data transfer using Legacy System Migration Workbench (LSMW)** (Transaction **LSMW**)  
  Often involves a screen recording of manual transactions and batch file upload.

- **Legacy data transfer using Business Application Programming Interfaces (BAPIs)**  
  Typically requires a custom program developed with a technical consultant.

---

## 4.22 Important Terminology

- **Account determination**  
  Assignment of all **balance sheet** and **P&L accounts** per depreciation area for **APC**, **depreciation**, and **special reserves postings**. Assigned to one or more **asset classes**.

- **Asset class**  
  Groups assets based on criteria including **general ledger accounts**, default **valuations**, **depreciation settings**, and asset nature. Controls data maintenance screens and number ranges.

- **Asset transaction type**  
  Defines aspects of an asset transaction such as debit/credit, capitalization or retirement by posting, and more. Transaction types belong to **transaction type groups** like acquisitions, retirements, transfers, and depreciation.

- **Asset under construction (AUC)**  
  An asset type being built/produced that acts as a **cost collector** for capital and other expenditures. Upon completion (or intervals), the AUC is capitalized into a final asset.

- **Asset value date**  
  Date defined during posting for which the transaction is updated in asset accounting. Basis for deciding **capitalization date** and **ordinary start date** for depreciation or retirement date for asset sale/scrapping.

- **Chart of depreciation**  
  Organizes all **depreciation areas** valid for a country. Activated for a company code by assigning the chart of depreciation to the company code.

- **Depreciation area**  
  Used to calculate values according to various **legal** and **internal reporting** requirements.

## Depreciation Areas and Accounting Principles

Each **depreciation area** is assigned to an **accounting principle**. A depreciation area can:

- Post all values
- Post only depreciation
- Not post at all

### Depreciation Key

The **depreciation key** defines how depreciation is calculated for an asset, including:

- The **method** of depreciation (e.g., straight line, variable)
- The **depreciation start date** definition (in relation to acquisition date)
- Other relevant calculation settings

### Low-Value Asset (LVA)

An **LVA** is an asset with an acquisition value below a predefined threshold. These assets:

- Are posted to a separate **LVA class**
- Are depreciated fully within the year of acquisition

### Technical Clearing Account

A **technical clearing account** facilitates external asset transactions such as:

- Acquisitions from suppliers
- Sales to customers

This account is:

- Posted in the operational document
- Credited by accounting-principle-specific documents
- Always balances to zero after each posting

---

## 4.23 Practice Questions

These practice questions evaluate your understanding of the chapter and mimic the style of certification exams. Select all correct answers for credit.

1. Which system components are directly integrated with **asset accounting**? (3 correct answers)
   - A. Bank account management
   - B. Investment management
   - C. Purchasing
   - D. Plant maintenance
   - E. Quality management

2. What is true about assigning **charts of depreciation** to company codes?
   - A. All company codes of a single country must use the same chart
   - B. Each company code can be assigned a different chart
   - C. Assignment only to SAP-delivered charts
   - D. A single chart can be used for company codes in multiple countries

3. True or False: A single **depreciation area** can post to multiple ledgers.
   - A. True
   - B. False

4. What is true for **real depreciation areas**?
   - A. Always post to the general ledger
   - B. Can be assigned multiple currency types
   - C. Transactions can be posted independently
   - D. Can calculate values from other depreciation areas

5. Two assets in the same company code post depreciation to different general ledger accounts. What does this imply? (2 correct answers)
   - A. Different asset classes
   - B. Separate account determinations
   - C. Separate accounts for acquisition and production costs (APC)
   - D. Separate cost centers assigned

6. True or False: Two assets in the same asset class but belonging to different company codes with the same chart of depreciation can post to different accounts.
   - A. True
   - B. False

7. How can you default a value for the cost center for the entire asset class for buildings?
   - A. Use asset subnumbers
   - B. Change the assigned screen layout
   - C. Change the assigned tab layout
   - D. Enter in default account assignments for the general ledger account

8. Which of the following are types of **user fields**? (2 correct answers)
   - A. Group asset
   - B. Serial number
   - C. Evaluation group
   - D. Asset super number

9. To avoid copying the asset text when copying an asset, you should:
   - A. Change the assigned screen layout
   - B. Change the assigned tab layout
   - C. Change the asset class definitions
   - D. Create a dummy reference asset with no text

10. For which asset type is the **asset main text** always prefilled?
    - A. Asset super numbers
    - B. Group assets
    - C. Asset subnumbers
    - D. Mass-created assets

11. You execute a report based on location and miss an asset. Possible reasons? (2 correct answers)
    - A. Asset fully depreciated
    - B. Asset was sold to a customer
    - C. Equipment assigned to the asset was moved
    - D. Asset was partially scrapped

12. True or False: The document type in the **asset transaction type** is proposed but adjustable during posting.
    - A. True
    - B. False

13. Which transactions lead to **asset capitalization**? (3 correct answers)
    - A. Purchase order in purchasing
    - B. Valuated goods receipt
    - C. Assets under construction (AUCs) settlement
    - D. Intracompany transfer
    - E. Nonvaluated goods receipt

14. True or False: In both the **ledger** and **accounts** approaches, the technical clearing account is posted to by all accounting-principle-specific documents.
    - A. True
    - B. False

15. True or False: When posting an integrated asset sale to a customer, you enter a debit for the customer with posting key **01** and credit for the asset with posting key **75**.
    - A. True
    - B. False

16. When making a partial sale, how can you calculate the amount of value reduction for the asset? (3 correct answers)
    - A. By quantity
    - B. By posted depreciation
    - C. By profit (or loss)
    - D. By retirement amount
    - E. By percentage

17. True or False: To post intercompany asset transfers, you maintain the cross-company-code clearing accounts.
    - A. True
    - B. False

18. When posting an amount above the maximum value threshold for an asset in the LVA class, how does the system respond?
    - A. Produces an error; asset must be split or posted to another class
    - B. Warning message; depreciation key adjusted to normal depreciation
    - C. Posts up to LVA threshold, remainder to generated asset subnumber
    - D. Adjusts asset quantity to stay below maximum threshold

19. You have an invoice for transport expenses for your **AUCs** capitalizable per IFRS but not local GAAP. Best approach?
    - A. Post to AUCs; manage settlement per depreciation area
    - B. Post to clearing account; clear per ledger group (capitalize IFRS, expense local GAAP)
    - C. Post to AUCs; post partial scrapping for local depreciation area after settlement
    - D. Post twice: expense to local ledger and capitalize for IFRS

20. The **cross-company-code depreciation area** is required in which intercompany transfers?
    - A. All intercompany transfers
    - B. Transfers with nonmatching depreciation areas
    - C. Transfers between company codes in different countries
    - D. Transfers where asset class changes

21. An online **depreciation test run** is limited to how many assets?
    - A. 100
    - B. 1,000
    - C. 10,000
    - D. No limit

22. True or False: You can execute the **depreciation posting run** for a single depreciation area.
    - A. True
    - B. False

23. True or False: After a depreciation run completes even when assets have errors, you no longer need to fix those asset errors.
    - A. True
    - B. False

24. When should the fiscal year close for **asset accounting** be carried out?
    - A. Directly before balance carryforward
    - B. Directly after balance carryforward
    - C. When the previous fiscal year is closed
    - D. When the last nonspecial period of the previous year is closed

---

## 4.24 Practice Question Answers and Explanations

1. **Correct answers: B, C, D**

- **Investment management** integrates closely with **AUCs**.
- **Purchasing** integrates from purchase requisition phase; asset is a required field on purchase order.
- **Plant maintenance** integrates through equipment master record connection.
- **Bank account management** and **quality management** are not directly integrated with asset accounting.

2. **Correct answer: B**

- No restriction on charts of depreciation per country.
- Each company code is assigned its own chart.
- Charts can be modified, and copying SAP-delivered charts is recommended.
- Different countries require different charts due to local accounting laws.

3. **Correct answer: A**

- True: Accounting principles assigned to depreciation areas, which are linked to ledger groups that can have multiple ledgers.

4. **Correct answer: C**

- Real depreciation areas can be posted to independently.
- They don’t have to post to the general ledger always.
- Each area is assigned a currency type.
- Derived areas calculate values from other depreciation areas.

5. **Correct answers: A, B**

- Different **account determinations** indicate different **asset classes**.
- **Cost centers** do not determine account postings.

6. **Correct answer: A**

- True: Different company codes can have different charts of accounts.
- Account determination is defined per chart of accounts, allowing different accounts posting.

7. **Correct answer: B**

- Defaulting values for the cost center per asset class is done by modifying the **screen layout**.
- Tab layout controls positioning, not defaults.
- Default account assignments don’t affect cost center fields.

8. **Correct answers: C, D**

- User fields include **evaluation group** and **asset super number**.

## Practice Question Answers and Explanations

You usually answer these by a combination of **knowing part of the right answer** and dismissing some of the wrong answers. The **evaluation groups** and **asset super numbers** can be maintained in Customizing and assigned to assets to cover customer requirements for **extra fields and groupings**. The **group asset** is a **depreciation characteristic**; the **serial number** is a standard field that often ties in with equipment from **plant maintenance**.

**9. Correct answer: A**

You define which fields get carried over when an asset is used for reference in the screen layout. This isn’t maintained in the **tab layout** or the **asset class**. The dummy reference asset isn’t a good solution; it’s more of a hack workaround and you wouldn’t ever do something like this. Nevertheless, the option probably wouldn’t appear in the certification exam because ambiguous answers are avoided.

**10. Correct answer: C**

The **asset subnumbers** inherit the **asset main text** from the main asset number, and this can’t be changed.

**11. Correct answers: B, C**

When an asset is integrated with the equipment, changes in the equipment can be configured to update the asset. An asset sold will no longer show up in the company code reports. **Fully depreciated assets** show up in reports because they are still active in the company, and **partial scrapping** would not deactivate the asset either.

**12. Correct answer: A**

True. You do maintain a **default document type** for posting in the **asset transaction type**. This is defaulted in certain transactions when you don’t enter a separate one manually. An example in which this can be changed is the integrated acquisition posting with supplier, in which document type **KR** is used instead of transaction type 100 with the default of **AA**.

**13. Correct answers: B, C, D**

An asset is capitalized when processing a **valuated goods receipt**. The **invoice** is used for confirmation/adjustment of the amount. In contrast, with a **nonvaluated goods receipt**, the asset will be capitalized from the invoice entry. When you **settle the line items posted to an AUC** to the final assets, those are capitalized. When you post an **intracompany asset transfer**, the asset is capitalized on the **asset value date**. The **purchase order** doesn’t capitalize an asset; that happens either on goods receipt (for a valuated goods receipt) or during invoicing.

**14. Correct answer: B**

False. In the **accounts approach**, only one **accounting-principle-specific document** posts to the **technical clearing account**. The rest of the documents post to a different clearing account. If each document posted multiple times to the same account, the account would end up with a balance.

**15. Correct answer: B**

False. On the credit side, you must enter the **revenue account** for an asset sale. This is a special account with the **field status group for asset sales** that allows you to select the asset, dates, and values. You don’t post a credit directly to the asset.

**16. Correct answers: A, D, E**

When you select a **partial sale** in the asset retirement popup, you can choose to sell a specific **quantity** of the asset (if applicable); the value is adjusted based on the **amount for sale/total amount fraction**. When you select a **retirement amount**, you directly input the **amount of value reduction** as a number value. The **percentage method** simply splits the value based on the percentage entered. You can’t use the other options to determine the value.

**17. Correct answer: B**

False. An **intercompany asset transfer** works through a different mechanism than financial accounting **cross-company postings** and doesn’t require separate cross-company account definitions.

**18. Correct answer: A**

When you try to post above the **maximum value** for an asset created in the **LVA class**, the system produces an error. You can only post up to the maximum amount for assets in this class. In this case, you would check if you can split the posting or more likely create the asset in a **“normal” asset class**. The other options have one thing in common: the system is making a lot of decisions and automations. As a rule, the default system keeps things simple. Too much automation runs into problems when dealing with processes and transactions that might be done very differently depending on the company.

**19. Correct answer: A**

Answer A is the best one because it uses the **AUC functionality** as it’s intended to be used. You collect the production-related expenses on a single item (as you would use an internal order or a project), and then you settle the amounts. In **SAP S/4HANA**, the **settlement** is defined on the depreciation area, so you can manage the capitalization separately per accounting principle. Questions with “what is the best” phrasing aren’t part of the certification exam because they are ambiguous, and the questions and answers in the certification exam must be as straightforward as possible.

**20. Correct answer: B**

The **cross-company-code depreciation area** is used exactly for cases in which the sender has areas that need to be mapped to areas with different codification on the receiver side. You might need it for transfers that are between countries, but you also might not because you might need it for changing asset classes. In questions such as these, you look for the answer that answers the question in all cases.

**21. Correct answer: B**

This is a pure knowledge question; you either know it or you don’t. When these kinds of questions are in the certification exams, the exam authors try to make them at least cover useful topics. In this case, this is useful knowledge but not essential.

**22. Correct answer: A**

True. **Depreciation** can be posted for a single depreciation area or a single accounting principle. For an example of why this might be used, you can close periods per ledger at different times, so this might be required in certain periods.

**23. Correct answer: B**

False. The fact that you can maybe go about closing a period without having successfully posted to an asset doesn’t mean that you shouldn’t fix things as soon as possible. If you leave something problematic as is for too long, the **fiscal year change program** won’t be able to close a previous fiscal year, and you’ll be locked in without being able to post to the next fiscal year.

**24. Correct answer: C**

The **SAP S/4HANA system** allows for **two open fiscal years** for you to manage the closing postings of a fiscal year and start posting in the new fiscal year. You close a fiscal year when you close the books of the previous year, and you’re sure there will be no more postings to assets in the closed fiscal year.

---

## 4.25 Test Takeaway

You’ve gained a good overview of all basic **asset accounting organizational units**, and you understand the connections between the **chart of depreciation** and the **company code**. You also recognize the relation of the **depreciation area** with the **accounting principles** and how asset accounting integrates with the **general ledger**.

You’ve learned how to set up and use **asset classes** to group assets per the business needs and reporting requirements of your customers. You know how to create assets and **asset subnumbers**, as well as how to make creating and maintaining assets easier for end users through manipulation of screen fields and layouts. 

You learned about the basic daily transactions posted to assets such as **acquisitions, sales, and transfers**. You also were introduced to special asset categories such as **AUCs** and **LVAs**. You should also understand the **closing process** in asset accounting—both periodic and annual.

Finally, you now understand the concept of **data migration** and how assets and values are brought over to the SAP S/4HANA system from the customer’s legacy system.

---

## 4.26 Summary

**Asset accounting** is a large subsystem in the **SAP S/4HANA Finance line of business**. In addition to being fully preconfigured for each country through **best practices**, it’s configurable to a very detailed level to accommodate all the varying customer, industry, and legal requirements you might come across.

You’re now able to interpret **business requirements** and understand where and how to implement them in the system. You also can configure **master records** and explain all the basic transactions and processes within the **asset accounting subsystem**.

In the next chapter, we’ll review the **closing activities in financial accounting** in detail.

If you’re familiar with **classic asset accounting** as opposed to the new asset accounting used in **SAP S/4HANA**, you should see the benefit in clarity provided by the **real-time update** of all accounting principles, posting to depreciation areas by selecting them in the transactions, and having full clarity on the **line-item level** in the **Universal Journal**.

---

# Chapter 5  
## Financial Closing

### Techniques You’ll Master

- Create **financial statements**  
- Manage **posting periods**  
- Carry forward **balances**  
- Post **accruals** and **deferrals**  
- Execute **foreign currency valuation**  
- Perform **value adjustments**  
- Regroup **receivables** and **payables**  
- Perform closing activities for **materials management**  
- Use **SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing cockpit**  
- Perform **intercompany matching and reconciliation (ICMR)**  

---

## 5.1 Objectives of This Portion of the Test

The purpose of this portion of the **certification exam** is to test your general knowledge of the **closing activities** for financial accounting. The certification exam expects you to have a good understanding of the following topics:

- Manage **financial statement versions** and create financial statements  
- Maintain the **open and closed periods**  
- Post the **balance carryforward**  
- Output an **audit trail report**  
- Manage **accruals** and **deferrals** with manual postings  
- Prepare **balance confirmations**  
- Execute **foreign currency valuation**  
- Post **value adjustments**  
- Perform **accounts payable/receivable regrouping**  
- Perform closing for **materials management**  
- Use the **SAP Financial Closing cockpit**  
- Manage **ICMR**  

> **Note**  
> The financial closing topic makes up **15% of the total exam**.

---

## 5.2 Financial Statement Version

The focus of this chapter is on explaining the basic steps of the **financial accounting closing process** in **SAP S/4HANA**. It discusses:

- **Financial statement versions**  
- **Balance confirmations** in **accounts payable** and **accounts receivable**  
- **Foreign currency valuation**  
- **Reserves for bad debt**  
- **Open item reclassification**  
- The **SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing cockpit**  
- **Intercompany reconciliation**  

---

### Real-World Scenario

As a **financial consultant**, you need to have a good understanding of the **periodic activities** that must be carried out in the system by the **accounting department**. These activities are crucial to a business because many functions can’t be processed unless these activities are completed successfully.

**Closing activities** are usually handled by the **general ledger accounting department**, and other activities are the responsibility of the **accounts payable** and **receivable** departments. Some activities are performed **monthly**, and some are **annual**.

You need to be able to guide your customer to perform these activities. You also should have **overview-level knowledge** of the **SAP Financial Closing cockpit**, as many SAP customers streamline and track closing activities through it. It’s also the default choice when a process spans systems outside **SAP S/4HANA**.

Finally, you need to understand how the process of **ICMR** is performed on a high level, including the logic behind **real-time reconciliation** with **SAP Business Planning and Consolidation (SAP BPC)**.

## 5.2 Financial Statement Version

**Financial statements** are official reports you’re legally required to output at least annually. The basic reports you define in the system are the **balance sheet** and the **profit and loss (P&L) statement**. In **SAP S/4HANA**, you maintain the **financial statement version** to produce the financial statements, as shown in Figure 5.1.

The financial statement version is a structured way of grouping accounts. You can create financial statement versions for other internal and external reporting purposes and for planning. Define financial statement versions in **Customizing** using a **four-digit alphanumeric key** and a description. The basic task is to deliver a structured view of your **chart of accounts** in accordance with **local and global accounting principles**.

SAP Best Practices packages deliver **template financial statement versions** for each country installed with texts maintained in the local language, as required by local authorities. When creating a new financial statement version, you can reference an existing one and make required changes, remembering to maintain translations for newly added nodes and items.

**Figure 5.1** Financial Statement Versions List

---

### 5.2.1 Definitions for the Financial Statement

In the general definitions of the financial statement version, you maintain the following, as shown in Figure 5.2:

- **Maint. language**  
  Usually the official language in which the report will be printed.

- **Item Keys Auto.**  
  Specifies if identification keys of the financial statement items are assigned **manually or automatically**.  
  - Automatic assignment uses an ascending numeric order starting with 1.  
  - Manual keys must be **unique** and are used when entering an explanatory text for them.

- **Chart of Accounts**  
  Optional assignment of a specific chart of accounts to a financial statement version. You can define versions without specific chart of accounts.

- **Group Account Number**  
  Set this indicator for financial statement versions used for the **group chart of accounts**. Enter account numbers from the group chart.

- **Fun.area perm.**  
  Allows assigning **functional areas** to the financial statement version. If activated, function areas can be assigned in addition to accounts to individual nodes. However, this disables the use of the version for planning purposes.

**Figure 5.2** Definitions for Financial Statement Version

---

### 5.2.2 Financial Statement Version Item Hierarchy

Financial statement versions can have up to **20 item hierarchy levels**. For each level, the system calculates a **subtotal** based on accounts assigned in lower nodes (see Figure 5.3).

For each item at all hierarchy levels, assign a **unique key** and relevant **texts**.

At the first hierarchy level, default financial statement version items include:  
- **Assets**  
- **Liabilities and Equity**  
- **P&L Result**  
- **Net Result: Loss**  
- **Net Result: Profit**  
- **Financial Statement Notes**  
- **Not Assigned**

**Figure 5.3** Financial Statement Version Item Hierarchy

---

### 5.2.3 Financial Statement Item Definition

You maintain texts for the **start and end** of the financial statement version item (see Figure 5.4). You can choose to display the **group-level summarized amount**, which is a graduated total calculated from the total of the P&L account balances up to that item. A separate graduated total text can also be maintained.

Accounts can only be assigned to the **lowest-level items**. If an item has lower-level items, accounts cannot be assigned directly to it; they must be assigned to its lower-level items instead (see Figure 5.5).

- **Figure 5.4** Financial Statement Item Definition  
- **Figure 5.5** Allowed and Illegal Account Assignments

You can move a financial statement version item or account range to a new location with **reassignment**, which carries over all lower-level items and account assignments (Figure 5.6).

- **Figure 5.6** Financial Statement Version Node Reassignment

---

### 5.2.4 Account Assignment

Assign accounts and account ranges to hierarchy items. The criteria determine how accounts are displayed based on **balance types (debit or credit)**.

- Accounts may be assigned to different items depending on whether they have a **credit or debit balance**.  
- If an account is assigned to display only when the balance is debit (D), it must be assigned separately with credit (C) if needed (see Figure 5.7).

- **Figure 5.7** Account Assignment in Financial Statement Version

Within the financial statement version item definition, a **check** can be executed (Figure 5.8) that shows:

- **Accts Assigned to 1 Side Only**  
  Accounts assigned under nodes with either only debit or credit selected, but not both. If an opposite balance occurs, the system won’t know where to place the account. To resolve, assign both debit and credit checkboxes (D and C) where applicable.

- **Nonassigned Accounts**  
  Accounts not contained in the financial statement structure. You specify the chart of accounts and company code for this check. Sometimes unassigned accounts are intentional, e.g., in **parallel accounting**.

- **Incorrectly Assigned Accounts**  
  Checks that balance sheet nodes include only balance sheet accounts and others only P&L accounts. Review is needed to ensure correct account masters and assignments.

- **Figure 5.8** Financial Statement Version Checks

---

### 5.2.5 Global Accounting Hierarchy for Financial Statement Version Maintenance

The **Manage Global Accounting Hierarchies** app provides a consistent environment for maintaining master record hierarchies. Introduced with **SAP S/4HANA 1809**, the app aims to unify hierarchy maintenance for financial objects and master data.

You can maintain hierarchies for:  
- Financial statement version  
- Functional area  
- Profit center  
- Cost center  
- Consolidation financial statement item (group reporting)  
- Consolidation reporting item (group reporting)  
- Consolidation segment (group reporting)

- **Figure 5.9** Manage Global Accounting Hierarchies App

Features of managing financial statement version with this app include:  
- Consistent interface common to many financial objects  
- Manage and track versions in multiple time frames  
- Status management to indicate **active and draft** versions  
- Import and export hierarchies from/to spreadsheets  
- Import existing financial statement versions and continue maintenance in the app

- **Figure 5.10** Managing the Financial Statement Version

---

### 5.2.6 Financial Statement Output with SAP Fiori

Use the **Balance Sheet/Income Statement** app to output financial statements (see Figure 5.11).

You have several options:  
- Select to display **only opening values**, **movements**, or **all values combined**  
- Select any **currency type** assigned to the company code and ledger  
- Share output via email or connected apps such as **SAP Jam**  
- Create a **tile** for quick access on the SAP Fiori launchpad  
- Drill down on lowest-level (individual accounts) values to see line item or balance sheet reports  
- Display the full financial statement version or output specific sections using **ALL ACCOUNTS**, **BALANCE SHEET**, **PROFIT & LOSS**, **UNASSIGNED ACCOUNTS**, and **NOTES** tabs  

- **Figure 5.11** Financial Statement Balance Sheet Output  
- **Figure 5.12** Financial Profit & Loss Output  

Additional features:  
- Add filters to view specific segments or use alternative general ledger accounts (Figure 5.13)  
- Include **Profit Center** and **Segment** fields in output (Figure 5.14)  

- **Figure 5.13** Financial Statement Filter Options  
- **Figure 5.14** Financial Statement: Additional Columns  

---

### 5.2.7 Financial Statement Report with ABAP

You can still use the classic **ABAP report RFBILA00** to output financial statements (Figure 5.15).

This report offers advanced output controls such as:  
- Specifying **translation dates and rates**  
- Creating extracts for **consolidation**  
- Showing **zero-balance accounts**  
- And many more options

Through the classic report, you can select and print output using a **customizable form** (see Figure 5.16).

- **Figure 5.15** Financial Statement Classic Report  
- **Figure 5.16** Sample Form Preview

Other reports are also available.

## 5.2.8 Output of Ledger Comparison Report

One useful report is the **ledger comparison financial statement**, where you can directly compare two different ledger statements for the same or separate periods (Figure 5.17).

In the output (Figure 5.18), you get values for each selection and a column with the **variances** between them. You can analyze for specific **segments**, **profit centers**, and **business areas**.

In addition to financial statement reports, there are many other reporting tools available that leverage **line-item analysis**. There are **136 characteristics** available by default in the best practices system (Figure 5.19).

> **Note:**  
> **Characteristics** are reporting attributes such as **company code**, **segment**, **profit center**, **currency**, **period**, etc., and can often be used to filter reports.  
> **Key figures** are value representations such as **total credit balance**, **total debit balance**, **amount in EUR/USD**, **balance carryforward amount**, **quantity**, etc.

---

## 5.3 General Ledger Closing

The basic **general ledger closing operations** include managing the **posting periods**, executing the **balance carryforward** at year-end, and using the **audit journal**.

> **Note:**  
> Categorization of closing tasks as related to **general ledger**, **accounts payable**, **accounts receivable**, or **asset accounting** is somewhat limiting because in **SAP S/4HANA**, multiple areas are affected. This categorization is used for structural reasons in the book.

---

### 5.3.1 Posting Periods

**Managing the posting periods** involves defining the **fiscal periods** during which you can specify the **posting date** for journal entries. The **posting period variant** is assigned to your company code per ledger.

You can customize open periods with two apps:

- **Open and Close Posting Periods:** A customizing app (Figure 5.20) used to update open periods for all company code/ledger combinations assigned.  
- You define settings per **account type**:  
  - **A:** Assets  
  - **D:** Customers  
  - **K:** Suppliers  
  - **M:** Materials  
  - **S:** General ledger accounts  
  - **+ :** All accounts  
  (Specific account types take precedence over generic ones, e.g., **S** stronger than **+**)

You can specify **account ranges** for detailed period assignments. For each entry, you maintain an **authorization group (AuGr)** assigned to users who can post to certain periods.

You maintain up to **three separate intervals**:  

- **Interval 1:** Controls normal operative posting periods open during the year.  
- **Interval 2:** Controls **special periods** for posting to the previous year, based on regulations and policies.  
- **Interval 3:** Controls controlling-related postings, such as allocations and reposting after financial accounting postings have stopped.

The **Manage Posting Periods** app (Figure 5.21) allows most period maintenance from one place, with filters for:

- **Posting Period Variant**  
- **Fiscal Year Variant**  
- **Account Type**

In **SAP S/4HANA**, detailed period blocks for **controlling transactions** can be maintained (Figure 5.22), although this is for specialized control since financial accounting period controls usually suffice.

> **Tip:** The plan is to unify the maintenance into a single app in a future SAP S/4HANA release.

---

### 5.3.2 Balance Carryforward

The **balance carryforward program** moves balances of the **general ledger**, **customers**, **vendors**, and **asset accounts** to the next fiscal year. It is usually executed at the end or beginning of a fiscal year.

The **Carry Forward Balances** app (Figure 5.23) requires you to define:

- New fiscal year  
- Company code  
- Ledger to carry forward

You must execute carryforward for all ledgers, including any **extension ledgers**.

The app performs tasks differently for **balance sheet** and **profit & loss (P&L)** accounts:

- For **balance sheets**, it carries forward balances directly, so the new year's opening balance equals the previous year's closing balance.  
- For **P&L accounts**, balances are transferred to the **retained earnings accounts** in the master record, resulting in zero balance for P&L accounts at the new fiscal year's start.

Because **SAP S/4HANA** is a **line-item-based system**, the app creates line-item entries in the **Universal Journal** with a **special document number** outside normal ranges.

> **Note:**  
> In **SAP S/4HANA Cloud**, balance carryforward is performed **automatically**; the manual app is deprecated and the process transparent to customers.

---

### 5.3.3 Auditing

Clear **auditing reports** are essential in any financial system. Because **SAP S/4HANA** stores data at the **line-item level**, tracing every value's origin is straightforward.

Auditing reports are essential before **archiving** financial accounting data, ensuring you can provide **document and line item lists** for previous years as required by law.

Simple tools include:

- **Balance Audit Trail – Open Item and Balance** app  
- **Audit Trail – Line Items** app  

(Figure 5.24 shows available selection options.)

The **Audit Journal** app (Figure 5.25) outputs an overview of documents by **company code**, **ledger**, and **fiscal year**.

Output is grouped:

- By period in the **COMPACT JOURNAL** tab  
- By day in the **JOURNAL** tab

Additional **control functions** help quickly identify potential problems:

- **Display Journal Entry Changes:** shows line items with old and new values.  
- **Check Multi-Referenced Invoices:** identifies invoices posted more than once.  
- **Check Gaps in Journal Entry Numbering:** displays gaps in document numbering.  
- **Display Update Terminations:** lists system terminations for a date range.  

Filters can be refined (Figure 5.26) and output columns customized to display fields such as **currency types**, **transaction types**, and **segments**.

---

## 5.4 Accruals and Deferrals

Posting **accruals** and **deferrals** ensures balanced **expenditure** and **revenue reporting** over fiscal year periods.

- **Accruals:** Post expenses/revenues to the period they occur but are invoiced/paid in a future month.  
  - Example: Leasing a building paid once a year can be accrued monthly.  

- **Deferrals:** Report expenses already made in the periods they are used.  
  - Example: Insurance premiums paid yearly but reported monthly.

These postings are only for **financial reporting** and are reversed at the start of the next period, so daily operations are unaffected.

Accruals can be posted under **Other Payables** when amounts are known or **provisioned** if estimated.

---

### Example: Processing a Deferral

Assume an annual insurance premium invoice of **$12,000 USD** is received on the first day of the fiscal year:

1. Invoice posted in **accounts payable** as:  
   - Debit to **insurance expense account**  
   - Credit to **supplier account** for $12,000  
2. Payment posted, clearing the supplier account against the bank account.  
3. At period-end, post a **deferral entry** using the **Enter Accrual/Deferral Document** app (Figure 5.27):  
   - Document header: specify **Reversal Reason** and **Reversal Date**.  
   - Document lines: credit $11,000 on the expense account, debit accruals account for same amount, leaving $1,000 on expense account (1/12th of total).  
4. At the next period's start, use **Reverse Accrual/Deferral** app to reverse this posting and return the expense account balance to normal.

---

### 5.4.1 Accrual/Deferral Journal Entry

In the **Reverse Accrual/Deferral Documents** app (Figure 5.28), enter relevant details including:

- **Posting Period** for reversal  
- **Reversal Reason**

Only documents posted with the specified **reversal reason** will be selected. Having a separate **accrual/deferral reversal reason** is useful for this purpose and for reporting.

## 5.4.2 Recurring Journal Entry

Another option for posting **accruals** is to use a **recurring entry document** (Figure 5.29).

In this process, you must ensure that the **document amounts** are the same as the previous period every time because you cannot change the recurring document. You define the **Interval in Months** for which the document entry is to be posted and the **Run Date** for the posting. 

At the end, you create the **recurring entry**, which doesn’t create a document and is only used as a reference for posting recurring entries.

---

## 5.5 Accruals Management

**Accruals management** is a tool that enables you to manage accruals, from performing accrual calculations to posting accrual values automatically. Currently, the tool supports posting **manual accruals** and **purchase order accruals**.

The tool is based on a completely rebuilt **accrual engine** leveraging the **SAP S/4HANA architecture**, offering full integration with the **Universal Journal**. It was introduced with **SAP S/4HANA 1809**.

---

### 5.5.1 Manual Accruals Process

To use **manual accruals** with the accrual engine, you first create an **accrual object**, which is a master record storing information relevant for posting accruals (Figure 5.30). Think of this as the **accrual contract**.

When creating the accrual object for manual accruals, you must define the following:

- **Accrual Object Category**  
  Groups accrual objects for similar use cases (e.g., rent, insurance).

- **Start of Life/End of Life**  
  The **runtime period** that the accrual object is valid.

- **Account Assignments tab**  
  Controls various objects to which the accrual is posted (cost center, profit center, segment, etc.).

- **Item Data**  
  Defines accrual items. An accrual object can have multiple accrual items.  
  - Define **item type**, relevant **ledger group** (system assigns representative ledger)  
  - Enter **amounts**, **currencies**, **quantities**, and **units of measure**  
  - Enter **accrual method**, defining the calculation algorithm (e.g., straight-line, declining balance)

**Tip:** Create a separate accrual item for each combination of **accrual item type** and **ledger group** you want to post to.

After setting up the accrual object, use the **Start Periodic Run – Accrual Engine** app to post accrual amounts for the period. Enter the **Application Component** (manual accruals or purchase order accruals), relevant **company codes**, and other filtering criteria (Figure 5.31). The system returns a results list with an analysis of postings (Figure 5.32).

---

### 5.5.2 Manual Accruals Configuration

Configure settings for **accrual management** in the **SAP IMG** menu under **General Ledger Accounting • Business Transactions** (Figure 5.33).

The initial configuration is complex and is summarized here without detailed analysis. Purchase order accrual configuration is also not deeply analyzed as standard SAP settings are sufficient for most cases.

Steps to activate the accrual engine for manual accruals:

1. Enter the **Application Component "ACAC" (Manual Accruals)** as the customizing component to indicate manual accrual-related configuration.

2. Under **Basic Settings** (Figure 5.34), assign company codes and fiscal years relevant for manual accrual postings.

3. Create your **accrual item types** (rent, insurance, etc.) and optionally define currencies other than the transaction currency for display in accrual management.

   The **accrual item** defines the types of postings performed. You can select all or specific types:
   - **Opening posting:** Complete amount posted on an accrual account.
   - **Periodic posting:** Periodic (usually monthly) posting from accrual account to P&L.
   - **Closing posting:** Used for abrupt deactivation of an accrual object; posts remaining amounts.

   Define **automatic postings** supported by accrual item:
   - None (calculation only, no posting)
   - Opening posting only
   - Periodic posting only
   - All (opening, periodic, and closing)

   Postings can be **complete** or **delta-only**:
   - Complete: System reverses previous amounts and posts the total calculated amount.
   - Delta: System posts only the current period amount.

   Posting date is always the **last day of the period**.

4. Define **accrual methods**, which are formulas used to calculate accrual breakdown by periods. Methods map to **ABAP classes**; custom methods require developer collaboration.

5. Define the **posting schema** and **account determination** for manual accruals, including:

   - Lines included in an accrual posting.
   - **Line-item types** (e.g., periodic recognition type 9003, offsetting 9000) (Figure 5.35).
   - Assign **symbolic accounts** to posting schema lines, mapped to actual general ledger accounts in account determination to keep posting schema chart-of-accounts independent (Figure 5.36).

6. Define **accrual object categories** (Figure 5.37) to group similar accrual objects (categories such as rent, insurance) and assign number ranges.

---

### 5.5.3 Purchase Order Accruals Process

**Purchase order accruals** transfer data from **materials management** to the accrual engine, converting purchase order items into accrual items. The system calculates accrual amounts for each purchase order item.

You can simulate these amounts and periodically execute an accrual run to post all calculated accruals.

**Tip:** Purchase orders for **stock materials** and **assets** are not relevant for accruals and are excluded.

Process steps:

1. **Create purchase order:** Evaluated and transferred to the accrual engine per configuration. An **accrual object** is created for each purchase order.

2. **Display accrual object:** Check system-calculated amounts for each purchase order item.

3. **Review and approve accruals:** Optional workflow allows reviewers to check and approve accrual lists. Reviewers can update amounts based on judgment (Figure 5.38). Separate review apps exist for purchase order owners and controllers; controllers have a separate app for approval.

4. Execute the **periodic posting run** for the purchase order accruals application component (POAC).

**Note on Posting Schema Configuration:**  
Only **periodic postings** (type 9003) are relevant for purchase order accruals; thus, a single posting schema with this line item type is configured. In **account determination**, maintain the general ledger account for periodic accruals and a fallback offsetting account, even though the default offsetting account is the purchase order expense account.

---

## 5.6 Closing Activities in Receivables and Payables

For **accounts payable/receivable**, perform periodic **closing activities** to synchronize with business partners on open amounts and due dates.

You must also execute **foreign currency valuation** for open amounts and post necessary value adjustments for overdue receivables.

Depending on local regulations, you can perform **customer** and **supplier account regrouping**.

---

### 5.6.1 Balance Confirmation

Companies usually generate **balance confirmations** once a year, sending them to customers and suppliers, often with a reply slip to request confirmation in return. This process verifies matching accounting figures between business partners.

Prepare balance confirmations in **Customizing** by defining required forms and assigning them to print programs. Ensure address details are maintained for your company code, with the possibility of assigning different addresses using an **address ID** for differentiation.

The **Customer Balance Confirmation** selection screen offers many options for account/item selection, data output type, and printing (Figure 5.39).

Figure 5.40 shows a sample of the letter printed from the default SAP S/4HANA form.

---

### 5.6.2 Foreign Currency Valuation

**Foreign currency valuation** is the process of identifying and posting the **profit or loss** resulting from fluctuations in **currency exchange rates** when transacting with foreign business partners.

## Foreign Currency Valuation

Depending on local and global **accounting principle** requirements, currency valuation might be done **monthly or annually**. The valuations are usually reversed at the beginning of the next period; however, some countries require that this reversal doesn’t happen for a year-end valuation.

To perform the valuation, you:

- Configure a **valuation method**
- Assign it to the **valuation areas**
- Assign the valuation area to the **accounting principle**
- Define accounts relevant for the automated **account determination** of **P&L**

You access the definition of the valuation methods in **Customizing** (Figure 5.41).

### Valuation Method Configuration

The system comes preconfigured with valid methods for the **local legal requirements** of many countries. Usually, no modifications are necessary, but you can copy existing rules to define your own.

On a high level, you define the following:

- The **valuation procedure** that defines when the system evaluates differences  
  - For example, a **lowest-value approach** posts revaluation only if the new valuation is lower than the current book value.
- How the document should be posted (document type, account groupings, posting by line item)
- The **exchange rate determination**, including the exchange rate types to be used

### Valuation Area Definition

After validating valuation methods, define the valuation area by:

- Assigning the **Valuation Method**
- Selecting valid **currency types** (Crcy type)
- Adding a description (Long Txt) (Figure 5.42)

Assign the valuation area to an **accounting principle**. The **general ledger** is updated through the ledger group assigned to this principle.

### Delta Posting Logic

In Customizing, activate **delta logic** for valuation areas where valuations should not reverse automatically (Figure 5.43).

- Activating delta logic without monthly reversal means no automatic reversal of valuations.
- Selecting the **Mon.Rev. (monthly valuation)** checkbox allows reversal of midyear valuations.
- You can specify runs for **Mid-Year Valuation** or **Year-End Valuation** to potentially use the same valuation area for both month and year-end.

### Accounts Definition for Foreign Currency Valuation

To execute foreign currency valuations, define:

- **Valuation loss** and **valuation gain** accounts (middle column in Figure 5.44) per general ledger account
- **Balance sheet adjustment account**, which acts as a clearing account for valuation differences  
  - Essential for **reconciliation account types** (customer and supplier accounts), since valuation differences are not posted to individual customer/supplier accounts

**Tip:**  
Accounts in the **Exchange rate difference realized** column define **P&L** accounts for realized differences when open items are finally cleared.

### Selection Parameters for Valuation Runs

For valuation runs (Figure 5.45), you can select:

- **Test Run**, **Simulation Run**, or **Update Run**
- Let the system determine posting parameters or set them manually

You can reset valuations completely if errors occur; this reverses both valuation and reversal documents.

**Tip:**  
A **simulation run** posts values to a **special simulation ledger**, allowing analysis in standard reports without legal valuation effects. Data is deleted after a productive run.

You must select which items to evaluate:

- Multiple item types per run (open items for customers, suppliers, general ledger accounts, general ledger balances)  
- Specific selections like customer/supplier ranges or accounts (Figure 5.46)

### Valuation Posting Transactions

The following occurs during valuation:

- Posting adjustments in the valuation period to reflect exchange rate changes according to the valuation method.
- Automatic reversal of valuation posting in the early following period.
- Multiple executions within a period post **delta values** for each run.

A sample log (Figure 5.47) shows the system analyzing items and calculating differences.

### Example: Valuation Postings and Methods

Assume account values over a year (Table 5.1):

| Time of Posting | End of Q1 | End of Q2 | End of Q3 | End of Year |
|-----------------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-------------|
| Value in local currency | 1000 | 998 | 999 | 1001 | 1002 |
| Value in foreign currency | 1000 | 1000 | 1000 | 1000 | 1000 |

Table 5.2 shows postings by financial statement software under different valuation techniques:

| Time of Posting | End of Q1 | Begin of Q2 | End of Q2 | Begin of Q3 | End of Q3 | Begin of Q4 | Year End | Begin of Q1 |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Always evaluate | -2 | +2 | -1 | +1 | +1 | -1 | +2 | -2 |
| Lowest value | -2 | +2 | -1 | +1 | | | | |
| Strict lowest value | -2 | +2 | -2 | +2 | | | | |
| Delta + always evaluate | -2 | +1 | +2 | +1 | | | | |
| Delta + lowest value | -2 | +1 | +1 | | | | | |
| Delta + strict lowest value | -2 | | | | | | | |

### Understanding Valuation Methods

- **Always evaluate** posts differences regardless; with delta logic active, valuation is not reversed.
- **Lowest value principle** posts only if valuation is worse than original posting; values are reversed or left depending on delta logic.
- **Strict lowest value** posts only if new value is lower than current holding.

---

## 5.6.3 Value Adjustments

Value adjustments for **receivables** are done in two ways:

### Individual Value Adjustment

- Posting for a specific business partner with **unrecoverable open amount**
- Post via a **special general ledger transaction**
- Debit expense from the **individual value adjustment account**
- Credit the **customer account** through the **Special G/L indicator** (default type E)

### Flat-Rate Individual Value Adjustment

- Mass rule-based adjustment postings using a program
- Customize the process and execute a **valuation run**

You configure:

- **Value adjustment keys** determining the percentage used (Figure 5.48)
- Assign keys to customers receiving flat-rate adjustment
- Account determination for automatic postings

During execution (Figure 5.49), you enter parameters such as:

- **Val. Method = “3”** (flat-rate individual value adjustment)
- **Key Date** (usually last day of the month)
- **Valuation Area** (same as foreign currency valuation)
- Optional settings, select **Postings** checkbox to generate postings

Proposed valuations are created and can be manually edited. After processing, the valuation run (Figure 5.50) posts adjustments. Standard reports confirm valuation results.

---

## 5.6.4 Accounts Payable/Accounts Receivable Regrouping

Regrouping for **customer and supplier accounts** is performed depending on local/corporate accounting regulations:

- When **receivables and payables** must be displayed separately, transfer supplier **debit balances** to a receivables account in the balance sheet.
- Group payables and receivables based on due dates (e.g. short-term, mid-term, long-term).
- Correct amounts when changing **reconciliation accounts** in master records.

### Regrouping Process

- Use a specific regrouping app configured in **Customizing**
- **Sort method customization** defines rules separately for receivables and payables
- Define account types transferred per time unit (usually years)
- Define accounts for regrouping postings (adjustment/contra account and target account) based on original reconciliation accounts

(Figure 5.51 shows an example for vendor receivables)

### Selection Parameters for Regrouping

All parameter options are available to specify the regrouping scope (Figure 5.52).

- For customers who are also suppliers and affiliated companies, select **Partner Grouping** to consolidate amounts.
- Affiliate company reconciliation accounts are usually separate.

### Changed Reconciliation Account Option

Selecting **Changed Rec. Acct** causes the system to report all items of the changed account using the new reconciliation account from the selected key date.

---
