## 5.7 Closing Activities in Materials Management

As a **financial consultant**, you should be familiar with activities concerning the integrated **closing process** with **materials management**. These include:

- Managing the **physical inventory documents**
- Clearing the **goods received/invoice received accounts**
- Valuating **material stocks**

### 5.7.1 Physical Inventory

**Physical inventory** is a business process in which the actual physical stock is compared and matched with the stock in your books. It’s generally a **legal requirement** to carry out an inventory at least once a year. You perform the inventory for your own stock and **special stock** (e.g., items held for third parties).

There are various types of physical inventory, such as the following:

- **Periodic physical inventory**  
  All stocks of the company are physically counted on the **balance sheet key date**, and the entire warehouse is blocked for material movements while the inventory is ongoing.

- **Continuous physical inventory**  
  Stocks are counted continuously during the fiscal year. It’s important for every material to be counted physically at least once during the year.

- **Cycle counting**  
  Stocks are counted at regular intervals within a fiscal year. These cycles are configurable through the cycle counting inventory in the **material master records**. This method is best for **fast-moving items**.

You update your books per the quantities counted in the physical inventory. The delta is posted in materials management. A sample of such a document is provided in Figure 5.54.

### 5.7.2 Goods Receipt/Invoice Receipt Account Clearing

The standard way to procure materials and assets in **SAP S/4HANA** is with the **three-step reconciliation procedure**: 

1. **Purchase order**
2. **Goods receipt**
3. **Invoice receipt**

When there is an inconsistency between the quantities delivered (from goods receipt) and the quantities invoiced, these are posted to the **goods receipt/invoice receipt clearing account** (defined as shown in Figure 5.55).

Inconsistencies can be caused by:

- Different amounts on the goods receipt and invoice receipt documents
- Wrong pricing information when entering a purchase order
- Not having received the goods receipt although the invoice has already been posted (or the opposite)

As part of your **accounting processes**, you clear the **goods receipt/invoice receipt account** by transferring the values separately to the:

- **Invoiced but not received account**
- **Received but not invoiced account**

To do this, you use the **Reconcile GR/IR Accounts** app (Figure 5.56). With this app, you:

- Create a worklist for items to process
- Check the items
- Match open items to reduce the open amounts

**Tip:** You can integrate a **machine learning service** in **SAP Business Technology Platform** to help with the goods receipt/invoice receipt clearing process. The algorithm proposes the best action based on analyzing how similar items were previously managed.

In **SAP S/4HANA**, you use the **Monitor GR/IR Account Reconciliation** app (Figure 5.57) to:

- Monitor the status and health of the clearing process
- See if responsible processors keep up with the workload
- Identify plants, company codes, and supplier accounts causing reconciliation issues for further investigation

Figure 5.58 shows the detailed **posting Journal Entry** screen for the clearing run. The value of **2,500.00** comes from the price of the material multiplied by the quantity (50 quantity × 50 value).

In the document header (Figure 5.59), you can see all related documents referenced by the clearing process. The document is reversed on the first day of the next period to avoid affecting daily business operations.

### 5.7.3 Stock Valuation

There are three types of **stock** you’re required to valuate:

- **Raw materials, supplies, and consumables (RSC)**  
  Commonly bought from suppliers and often managed by the **moving average price (MAP)** method.

- **Work-in-process (WIP) materials** (also known as **semifinished goods**)  
  Usually produced by the company and often valuated at a **standard price**. WIP can be broken down analytically on the balance sheet if customized.

- **Finished goods (FG)**  
  Produced in-house and generally valuated at a **standard price**.

You can update the balance sheet based on the calculated material prices and quantities using the **Balance Sheet Values by Account** app (Figure 5.60). The app enters the values on the balance sheet in accordance with the inventory in the books and calculated prices (Figure 5.61).

## 5.8 SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing Cockpit

The **SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing Cockpit** supports planning, executing, monitoring, and analyzing all **financial closing tasks** for SAP S/4HANA and integrated systems (Figure 5.62).

### Use Cases

- Activities that **recur periodically**
- Multiple **responsible people**
- Processes with **structured sequences** and **task dependencies**

### Advantages

- A common, accessible, and stable app for all involved
- Activity execution tracking ensures **status transparency**
- Closing tasks are documented for verification and checks
- Manual statuses can be set for tasks executed outside the system
- Manual confirmation and documentation are allowed for checks performed

### 5.8.1 Task Templates

First, create a **task template** by copying an existing standard template. Select the **organizational unit level** (e.g., controlling area or company code), and the system proposes **month-end** or **year-end closing** templates.

After selecting and saving the template, enter the following (Figure 5.63):

- Template name
- Description
- Responsible entity
- Language

The template represents the **complete closing process** for your enterprise (Figure 5.64). After copying, maintain the specific organizational units the template applies to (controlling areas, company codes).

Tasks are structured and organized into **folders** which you can reassess and add as needed.

Supported tasks include:

- **Programs** with variants that can be executed through the cockpit
- **Transactions** assigned and opened through the cockpit (transaction launchpad)
- **Notes** (manual tasks outside the system or reminders)
- **Flow definitions** string programs to allow automatic execution in sequence
- **SAP Business Process Automation by Redwood tasks** control execution in external systems
- **External job reporting** retrieves information for task execution in external systems

When adding a new task (Figure 5.65), provide:

- Description
- Responsible and processor entities (e.g., User)
- Task type and definitions
- Task assignments (optionally assign to task folders)

### 5.8.2 Task List

After assigning tasks to the template, create a **task list**. The system names it the same as the template.

Enter values for the:

- Key date
- Fiscal year
- Posting period

The system transfers the permitted activities from the template to the task list according to the closing type (month-end or year-end). After finalization, **release** the task list to execute and monitor closing.

**Tip:**  
You don’t execute closing directly from the template; the template holds generic tasks, and the task list makes tasks specific for execution.

### 5.8.3 Dependency Configuration

After releasing the task list, define **relationships between programs and transactions**. The system checks them to ensure correct execution sequence.

- Activities can have multiple prerequisites.
- Task folders can be assigned as prerequisites.

Pre-delivered **KPI reports** (Figure 5.66) help monitor the status and progress of the closing process.

## 5.9 Methods for Intercompany Matching and Reconciliation

The **intercompany matching and reconciliation (ICMR)** component is embedded in SAP S/4HANA since the **1909 release**. This solution helps **group entities reconcile intercompany transactions** between corporate entities, a complex process due to increased mergers and acquisitions.

The **ICMR solution** works with system data directly and does **not require** the usual **extraction, transformation, and load (ETL)** processes found in traditional non-real-time solutions. This enables reconciliation and matching **during the fiscal period**, avoiding delays in the closing process.

## Note

**Data managed in external systems** must be uploaded in the system via **file upload** or **application programming interface (API)**; however, the recommendation is to avoid this as much as possible and perform **accounting for all company codes directly** in your **SAP S/4HANA system**.

---

## Tip

The scope of **ICMR** is quite large, so the **academy material** and **certification focus** are on a pretty high level of the functionality. When posting **intercompany transactions**, differences often occur in the reported values due to timing of posting, currency translations, user error, and so on. Intercompany transactions usually involve the **business partner entity**, so generally ICMR focuses on **accounts payable/accounts receivable processes**.

The goal of **ICMR** is to **automatically match documents** posted and identify possible discrepancies present in the data.

---

## 5.10 High-Level Process for Intercompany Reconciliation

The high-level process to perform **intercompany reconciliation** includes the following steps:

1. **Collect data**  
   Data collection happens within **SAP S/4HANA**, directly from the **Universal Journals** of accounting and consolidation (tables **ACDOCA** and **ACDOCU**, respectively). External files, data from interfaces, and data replicated into the system are in scope, but ideally all company codes are in the same SAP S/4HANA client.

2. **Match documents**  
   Using flexible rules, the system runs **matching algorithms** on the items relevant for reconciliation. Matching runs can be triggered manually or set up to run periodically on their own.  
   ![Figure 5.67 Schedule Matching Run](Figure_5_67_Schedule_Matching_Run.png)

3. **Solve discrepancies**  
   The system displays perfectly matched items and those with differences that otherwise seem to match. For any items relevant for reconciliation, you can:  
   - Assign them manually (including reassignment of automatically matched items)  
   - Add a note (with optional due date)  
   - Send a notification (to a user/group with optional due date)  
   - Set notification to done (removes any due date alarms)  
  
   Discrepancies can be solved by correcting the source documents, triggering automatic write-offs (with system request for auto-adjustments), etc.  
   ![Figure 5.68 Manage Unassigned Items](Figure_5_68_Manage_Unassigned_Items.png)

4. **Check reconciliation results**  
   You can check the **reconciliation status** and results on the aggregate levels of the reconciled objects (e.g., a group of companies) and drill down to the source documents.

---

## 5.10 Important Terminology

- **Accounts payable/accounts receivable regrouping**  
  Regrouping payables and receivables to change the way values owed or due are displayed in the balance sheet to comply with local or corporate accounting standards. This includes moving supplier debit balances to receivables, customer credit balances to payables, posting payable receivable amounts to separate accounts, and transferring balances for reconciliation accounts changed midyear.

- **Accrual**  
  Posting of an expense or revenue before an invoice is entered to represent the cost/revenue in the period it is incurred or made for more realistic reporting. For example, if a customer pays $1,000 for four months upfront, you put it into a deferred revenue account and subtract $250 each month.

- **Accrual engine**  
  A framework introduced in the **1809 release** of SAP S/4HANA that enables and automates the calculation and posting of manual and purchase order accruals, fully integrated with the **Universal Journal**.

- **Accrual item**  
  A line item within the accrual object specifying the accrual calculation and posting per accrual type and ledger group.

- **Accrual object**  
  A contract-like master record holding all information needed to calculate, manage, and post accruals for a business transaction.

- **Balance confirmation**  
  Communication with suppliers/customers requesting confirmation of transaction balances to ensure values are consistent with their books.

- **Carryforward**  
  Process executed to bring balances to the new fiscal year:  
  - Balance sheet accounts: Opening balance of new year matches closing balance of previous year  
  - P&L accounts: Opening balance is 0 as closing balances are transferred to retained earnings

- **Deferral**  
  Spreading incurred expenses or billed revenues over the periods in which they occur. For example, paying $12,000 upfront for six months of rent is deferred and debited $2,000 monthly.

- **Financial statement version**  
  Object structuring **general ledger accounts** to produce **balance sheet** and **P&L reports** for local legal and internal reporting.

- **Foreign currency valuation**  
  Process to valuate open items and account balances using the currency translation rate on the key date.

- **Goods receipt/invoice receipt account**  
  Account with balance representing mismatches between goods receipt amounts and invoiced amounts. Cleared at period end and reversed at the beginning of the next period.

- **Individual value adjustment**  
  Either a post to a special general ledger or flat-rate individual value adjustment for unsecured or overdue receivables shown in separate balance sheet sections.

- **Intercompany matching and reconciliation (ICMR)**  
  Process to ensure items and balances among affiliate companies are consistent for involved company codes.

- **Physical inventory**  
  Process of counting actual physical stock quantities at warehouses.

- **Recurring entry**  
  Journal entry repeated unchanged at regular intervals defined in the header section.

- **Reporting characteristics**  
  Criteria by which data is selected and displayed (e.g., organizational units, master data, year, period).

- **Reporting key figures**  
  Include stored values, quantities, and values calculated based on fixed formulas.

- **SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing cockpit task list**  
  Defines specific tasks executed during period end; execution monitored and analyzed within the cockpit.

- **SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing cockpit task template**  
  Holds generic closing tasks to execute closing on various organizational unit levels.

- **Stock valuation**  
  Updates valuation of materials in warehouses based on latest prices maintained in material master records.

- **Valuation area**  
  Bridges the valuation method and accounting principle; allows defining one to three currency types per valuation area; used when posting foreign currency and other valuations.

- **Valuation method**  
  Customizing object controlling definitions for the valuation procedure (always evaluate, lowest-value principle, strict-lowest-value principle), document posting parameters, and exchange rate type determination.

---

## 5.12 Practice Question Answers and Explanations

1. **Correct answer: B**  
Manually defining the **item keys** allows you to enter your own explanatory texts for these.  

2. **Correct answer: A**  
True. You don’t need to assign a specific **chart of accounts** to a **financial statement version**; you must assign a chart of accounts for accounts you define on the item level.  

3. **Correct answers: A, B, D**  
The complete list of **default items** includes the following:  
- Assets  
- Liabilities and equity  
- P&L result  
- Net result: loss  
- Net result: profit  
- Financial statement notes  
- Not assigned  

4. **Correct answer: B**  
False. You can only assign accounts to the **lowest level** within a hierarchy node.  

5. **Correct answers: B, D**  
The full list of checks is as follows:  
- Accounts assigned to one side only  
- Nonassigned accounts  
- Incorrectly assigned accounts  
The system doesn’t need to check for duplicate keys because you can’t create duplicate keys; you get an error before being able to save. Noted items don’t go to the **financial statement notes**, and they don’t show up at all on the financial statement.  

6. **Correct answers: A, D, E**  
Even if you don’t know the answer for the specifics of the app, you can guess it based on your knowledge of which objects have hierarchies in **SAP S/4HANA**. The **internal orders** and the **segments** don’t have any hierarchy structure in the system, so they can be excluded as wrong answers.  

7. **Correct answer: A**  
Around **130 possible line-item fields** are available to use for analysis in the standard system.  

8. **Correct answer: C**  
There are three intervals: one for normal periods, one for valuations, and one for controlling postings.  

9. **Correct answers: A, C**  
You define the **open periods per controlling area** in the advanced period definition of controlling. In financial accounting, you use the **posting period variant** to manage periods for the company codes assigned to it.  

10. **Correct answer: C**  
You can have up to **four special/valuation periods** in the fiscal year variant, and all can be open at the same time.  

11. **Correct answer: C**  
You perform **carryforward separately for each ledger**. This definition includes the extension ledgers assigned to a company code.  

12. **Correct answers: A, C, D**  
The full list of available checks includes the following:  
- Check gaps in **journal entry numbering**  
- Display **journal entry changes**  
- Check **multireferenced invoices**  
- Display **update terminations**  

13. **Correct answer: B**  
The fact that you preemptively assign a **reversal reason** and the date for reversal in the document header is what makes this posting unique.  

14. **Correct answer: B**  
False. **Recurring entries** are posted in the same way, meaning you can’t use different accounts, amounts, or anything.  

15. **Correct answers: A, D**  
You can select between **full amounts**, for which the system inverts the posted amount and reposts the complete amount, and **delta posting**, in which the system only posts the difference calculated for the period. You can never post to a **closed period**, and **foreign currencies** will be updated according to the ledger configurations, not the accrual management configuration.  

16. **Correct answer: B**  
The creation of the **accrual object** is automated; specifically, an additional accrual object is created for each (relevant) **purchase order**. You must schedule or start the accrual run for both purchase order and manual accruals. Purchase order accruals have no opening posting; only periodic postings are required. The **accrual amount** is broken down automatically irrespective of the type of accrual.  

17. **Correct answer: D**  
You assign the **valuation procedure** to the **valuation method**. After defining the valuation method, you assign it to the **valuation area**. You assign the valuation area to the **accounting principle**.  

18. **Correct answer: B**  
The valuation currently stands at **98**, having a –2 amount from the initial valuation. Because the **delta logic** is enabled, the entry isn’t reversed. When –1 is posted, this is on top of the –2 already posted; therefore, in total, it’s **100 – 3 = 97**.  

19. **Correct answer: B**  
False. **Simulation runs** are executed not for **standard ledgers** but for **extension ledgers**. The extension ledger then must be defined as a **simulation extension ledger**.  

20. **Correct answer: C**  
Only **customers** can be included in these valuations.  

21. **Correct answers: A, B, C**  
Regrouping has nothing to do with **dunning**, nor with **balance confirmations**.  

22. **Correct answer: A**  
**Raw materials** are usually brought in, so the **MAP valuation** is generally the best fit for these materials.  

23. **Correct answer: C**  
The **notes task type** is essentially for setting reminders and providing information, so there is no posting triggered automatically by the system for this kind of task.  

24. **Correct answer: B**  
False. You can assign multiple tasks as prerequisites, including an entire **task folder**.  


## 5.13 Test Takeaway

You now understand how to create and manage **financial statement versions** in the **SAP S/4HANA system**, and how to use the financial statement version to **export financial statements** and **structure other reports**. You know how to define **open posting periods** and perform **balance carryforward activities**. You also understand the **auditing reports** available for financial accounting.

You can post **accruals and deferrals** manually and with **recurring entries**. You can perform the closing activities for **accounts payable/receivable**, such as sending account balances, performing **foreign currency valuation**, making **individual value adjustments**, and regrouping payables and receivables from **customers and suppliers**.

You understand the closing process in **materials management** and how it concerns financial accounting. You have a high-level understanding of the features available and process steps to use the **SAP S/4HANA Financial Closing cockpit** and can perform a basic **period-end intercompany reconciliation**.  


## 5.14 Summary

The **financial close process** includes a diverse set of tasks that need to be executed in multiple different modules of **financial accounting**. There are additional considerations to be made due to the tight integration with **controlling**, **materials management**, and other functionalities.

**SAP S/4HANA** offers speedy transaction processing, less need for reconciliation activities, and detailed reporting to cover the requirements for every business.

In the next and final chapter, we’ll go over some other **accounting topics**, which we’ll call **cross topics** for lack of a different label for them in the book’s structure. You’ll refresh your knowledge on **bank account management**, **document parking**, **validations and substitutions**, **archiving**, and **data aging**.  


## Chapter 6  
### Organizational Assignments and Process Integration  

### Techniques You’ll Master  
- Manage **banks and house banks**  
- Maintain **bank accounts**  
- Use **document parking** and **document parking workflow**  
- Configure and perform **journal entry verification**  
- Create **substitutions and validations**  
- Configure and perform **data archiving**  
- Activate, configure, and run **data aging**  


### Introduction

The purpose of this chapter is to analyze concepts that don’t fit in the general ledger, accounts payable/accounts receivable, asset accounting, or financial closing subjects and don’t affect the flow of understanding required for the concepts analyzed up to now.

The topics reviewed include **bank account management**, **document parking**, **document validations and substitutions**, **data archiving**, and **data aging**.  


### Real-World Scenario

When working on a project for a customer, you’ll find processes and tools that are used across **SAP ERP Financials modules**. In larger projects, you might have a cash management consultant to set up all the bank accounts, but this won’t always be the case because **SAP Cash Management** isn’t a de facto product that customers purchase and configure.

An understanding of how the basic **bank and bank account management** works in an **SAP S/4HANA system** is required. Cash management is also becoming more commonplace in SAP S/4HANA systems, so getting a start in your understanding of it, even a very basic one, is useful.

**Document parking** is a tool that allows users to save a document without posting. It’s also commonly used by customers as a basis for a simple workflow for document posting to comply with the **four-eyes principle** that many require for certain postings.

Being able to create and manage your own **validations and substitutions** is also an extremely useful skill. With **validations**, you can ensure a user is aware of a wrong entry because the user will be confronted with a warning or an error message for combinations of data that aren’t allowed. With **substitutions**, you can make data entry simpler and ensure the correct data is entered as well because the substitution value is derived by preset rules and can’t be changed by the user.

Finally, understanding how to configure **data archiving** and **data aging** will also help with your understanding of some of the more administrative tasks in the system. Many customers who want to move to SAP S/4HANA by updating their own system start that journey with a large-scale **data archiving project**.

Archiving as much data as possible before the system conversion speeds and simplifies the transition to **SAP S/4HANA**. The knowledge you gain here can be reused in **SAP ERP systems** because the processes are the same.

On the other hand, **data aging** is useful only for an SAP S/4HANA system because it decreases the **memory footprint of financial accounting documents**.

## 6.1 Objectives of This Portion of the Test

The purpose of this portion of the **certification exam** is to test your general knowledge of the **closing activities for financial accounting**. The exam expects you to have a good understanding of the following topics:

- **Managing banks, house banks, and bank accounts**
- **Posting, editing, and completing parked documents**
- **Configuring the parked document release scenario in SAP Business Workflow**
- **Configuring and using general journal entry verification**
- **Managing validations, substitutions, rules, and sets**
- **Executing data archiving for general ledger accounts**
- **Performing data aging for journal entries in financial accounting**

**Note:**  
The **organizational assignments** and **process integration** topics make up **15% of the total exam**.

---

## 6.2 Bank Account Management

**Bank account management** in **SAP S/4HANA** concerns **centralized bank account management**. These processes control the lifecycle of **banks and bank accounts**, such as opening, changing, reviewing, and closing bank accounts.

In this section, you’ll learn how to manage the **bank directory**, **bank accounts**, and **house banks**.

### 6.2.1 Bank Directory

The **bank directory** is a list with the details of all the **banks** you and your business partners do business with. This directory is maintained via the **Manage Banks app** (Figure 6.2), which provides an overview of all banks in the system.

You can:

- Add new banks
- Display and change existing banks

Banks, at least for the country where the **company code** is located, are commonly created by uploading a file to SAP S/4HANA using:

- **SAP GUI Transaction BAUP** (Country-Specific Transfer of Bank Data)
- **Transaction BIC2** (Takeover BIC Data)

To create a bank manually, you need the following details:

- **Bank Country**  
  This field is required. A bank can have subsidiaries in many countries.

- **Bank Key**  
  Required field. Must be unique per country and is usually provided by the country’s central bank.

- **Bank Name**  
  Required field. The name registered at the central bank.

- **SWIFT/BIC**  
  Use when available.

- **Bank Group**  
  Used, for example, in automatic payment bank selections.

- **BP Grouping/BP Number**  
  Used to create the bank as a business partner. The bank is given general, bank, and financial services roles by default.

- **Address**  
  Includes Region, Street, City, and Bank Branch fields. More detailed data can be maintained after saving.

- **Risk Information**  
  A credit rating maintained in the **Rating** field is used to assess bank risk.

**Note:**  
The **SWIFT/BIC code** is an **ISO code** identification for banks worldwide. It is used for **money transfers** and **message exchanges** between banks.

### 6.2.2 House Bank

**House banks** are the banks your company does business with, meaning the company has its own bank accounts at the bank to make and receive payments.

You maintain the following fields for a house bank:

- **Company Code**  
  The company code the house bank belongs to (a bank can be house bank for multiple company codes).

- **House Bank Key**  
  A five-digit unique identifier within each company code.

You can also maintain details for:

- Communications
- Data Medium Exchange (DME)
- Bank charges
- Electronic Data Interchange (EDI)

### 6.2.3 Bank Account Creation

You use the **Manage Bank Accounts app** to create new bank accounts and maintain existing bank accounts.

To create a new bank account, enter the following details:

- **Opening Date**  
  The date from which the bank account can be used for transactions.

- **Company Code**  
  The responsible company code.

- **Account Holder**  
  The owner of the bank account (person or legal entity).

- **Bank Country**  
  The country where the bank is located.

- **Bank Key**  
  The identification key of the bank. The SWIFT/BIC key and Bank Number will be displayed if maintained.

- **Currency**  
  The account currency key.

- **IBAN (International Bank Account Number)**  
  Standard numbering to identify international banks. The system proposes this based on bank key and bank account, but validate it against the bank's version.

- **Account Number**  
  The bank account number as provided by the bank.

- **Description**  
  A text field for identifying the bank account. Can be maintained in multiple languages.

- **Account Type**  
  Defines the purpose of the account (e.g., current, deposit, loan, investment, checking).

More fields are available such as contact details and data for bank statements. You can also enter a **Profit Center** and **Segment** in the **Additional Data** tab.

After saving the bank account as **Active**, additional details can be entered:

- **Payment Signatories** responsible for approving payments
- **Overdraft Limits** as agreed with the bank
- **Connectivity Path**

On the **Connectivity Path** tab, you link the bank account to the corresponding **house bank account**.  

- Enter an identification code for the house bank (up to five digits) in the **House Bank Acct ID** field.

Each house bank account must have a **main bank general ledger (G/L) account** assigned. The same G/L account can be shared by multiple house bank accounts.

The bank general ledger account uses a special type of **balance sheet account** called a **reconciliation account for bank accounts**, represented as **Cash Account** in the G/L Account Type field.

The main bank account and subaccounts should be of the **same type** to minimize the number of general ledger accounts required.

---

## 6.3 Document Parking

With **document parking**, you can post **temporary, incomplete documents** in SAP S/4HANA. You can:

- Add and change information
- Perform additional checks
- Post the complete document after verification

### 6.3.1 Overview of Document Parking

SAP S/4HANA offers two basic options for saving an incomplete document:

- **Holding a document**  
  Used for short interruptions when posting multiline documents. Held documents:

  - Keep entered data to avoid loss from browser timeout or power/network failure
  - Can only be retrieved by the user who created them
  - Generate no document number
  - Cannot be evaluated in reports
  - No standard workflow uses held documents functionality

- **Parking a document**  
  Used to store incomplete documents in the system. The system checks entries such as tax code, general ledger account, and cost center are valid but not extensive checks like tolerance limits.

  Key points for parked documents:

  - Receive a **document number** which does **not change** when finalized
  - **Substitution** is done only when converting to a complete journal entry
  - Can park **cross-company code documents** — only the originating company code’s posting receives a document number; final posting generates all documents
  - Can be used for business evaluations, e.g., advance tax returns and payment requests
  - Deleting a parked document loses the document number permanently and creates audit trail gaps

### 6.3.2 Document Parking Workflow Customizing

**SAP Business Workflow** in SAP S/4HANA automates communication and coordination between system components.

Many **standard workflows** are delivered with SAP S/4HANA. Example:

- **Single-Level Release for Document Parking (WS10000052)**  
  A subworkflow within the workflow framework for document parking (**WS10000051**).

The workflow:

- Begins with a **triggering event** (e.g., creating a master record, posting a document, parking a journal entry)
- The **workflow manager** assigns a **work item** (task) to the **organizational object** (defines permitted users)
- When a user accepts or rejects the work item, the workflow manager advances to the next step

The first step in customizing the document parking workflow is defining the **workflow variant**.

---

**© 2024 by Rheinwerk Publishing Inc., Boston (MA)**

## Workflow Variant Definition and Assignment

Here, you select **Posting Release** to use that feature, select the amount from which a release is triggered (**Release From**), and choose the **Subworkflow scenario**.

The **workflow variant** is assigned to one or more **company codes**, as shown in Figure 6.11. This assignment also defines the currency of the minimum amount previously set in the variant.

You can define **release groups** if you want to assign varying release procedures for your **business partners**. There are no underlying settings initially; you just assign a key and description to define the groups.

As shown in Figure 6.13, you assign the release group in the **master record** of the business partner. After selecting the Customer or Vendor role for **financial accounting**, you maintain the release group in the company code settings under the **Account Management** area.

The **release approval path** is the object for which you define who processes the release approval. You create the release approval path object by defining a key and description.

The release approval path is determined by the workflow variant together with the **document type** and **release group**, as shown in the Release Approval Path Allocation Customizing screen.

You can assign different **subworkflows** in accordance with the release approval path and the amount. This allows you to define more release levels or different approvers for larger posting amounts.

In the final Customizing step, you define who is responsible for performing the release approval per **workflow variant**, release approval path, release level, and amount. For each combination, you assign the relevant **organizational object**. The system identifies the users responsible for releasing the parked document based on these assignments.

---

## 6.3.3 Document Parking with Workflow

Figure 6.19 shows a document posting of a parked document. In the **Park General Journal Entries app**, the user default action is to save the parked document.

In other apps, such as the **Post Incoming Invoices app**, the option to park documents is in the top menu bar, and the default option is to post the document.

After saving, you can retrieve the parked document for editing. Not all fields can be changed after parking since a **document number** is assigned. The following fields cannot be changed:

- **Company Code**  
- **Currency**  
- **Ledger Group**  
- **Document Type**  
- **Document Number**  

There are no limitations for changing the **line items** of the document; you can remove lines completely and add new ones as needed. The system keeps a **log of changes** made to parked documents.

After verifying the document, you can post it. The system creates a **journal entry** with the same number. The document undergoes normal posting checks and substitution will take place. The **change history** is retained and logged in the journal entry.

The user posting the document is assigned as the user who entered the document, irrespective of the user who originally parked it.

If a **workflow variant** is assigned and the parked document is relevant for workflow, you can see the relevant **approval path** and **release level** in the **Workflow tab** of the parked document.

In the **Workflow Control** section, you can determine whether the document release is required (**Release Req.**), marked as complete (**Doc. Complete**), or completed successfully (**Released**).

In the top bar, a processor can **release** or **reject** the document. If rejected, it can be changed and sent back with a note explaining the rejection.

Workflow items needing processing are delivered to the **inbox** of relevant users. A user can forward the work item to another user for processing.

After releasing an item, it moves to the **processed workflows folder** in the inbox, where it can be retrieved.

You can check the **workflow log** at any time, as it keeps a detailed record of all steps and processors. There are different views, such as **Workflow Agents** (actions per processor) and **Workflow Objects**.

---

## 6.4 Journal Entry Verification

An additional, simpler verification process for reviewing and approving **general journal entries** is available in **SAP S/4HANA** from version 1709 and is accessible only via **SAP Fiori**.

You use three apps to manage this process: one for the **requester** to submit entries and two for the **reviewer** to manage pending and submitted entries.

SAP delivers a predefined, **single-step approval workflow** for general ledger journal entry verification, which can be adjusted to specific requirements.

---

### 6.4.1 Verification Process

A **requester** creates and submits a journal entry with the **Verify General Journal Entries – For Requester app**. This app allows creating manual entries or uploading from Microsoft Excel.

The system checks the journal entry against preconfigured criteria (e.g., amount) and assigns workflow processors if applicable.

The requester can view the **status** of submitted journal entries.

The **request processor** uses the **Verify Journal Entries – For Processor app** to review entries and select one action:

- **OK**: The journal entry will be posted if complete and correct.  
- **Reject**: The requester must edit and resubmit.  
- **Suspend**: The document is on hold for later processing.

The processor uses two apps: an **inbox** and an **outbox**, to process entries based on status.

---

### 6.4.2 Workflow Configuration

Two configuration apps are used to set up the verification workflow:

- **Manage Workflows for General Journal Entry Verification**: Activates workflows and sets prerequisites.  
- **Define Responsibilities**: Assigns users or user groups to workflows.

In the **Manage Workflows** app, you define:

- Description  
- Validity period  
- Preconditions for workflow application, based on:  
  - **Account group**  
  - **Threshold amount** (in company code currency)  
  - **Cost center**  
  - **Source company code**

You also configure **step sequence settings** for verification and posting steps, assigning approver rules and exception handling.

In the **Define Responsibilities** app, you set:

- **Priority** (01 to 99)  
- Amount ranges and company codes for responsibility validity  
- Assign users or user groups as **recipients** and **processors** for the verification workflow.

---

> **Tip**  
> The SAP Training and Adoption course materials for SAP S/4HANA 2020 do not cover journal entry verification, but this topic may be included in future courses and certifications.  
> For full configuration and usage guides, visit the SAP Help Portal: [http://s-prs.co/485603](http://s-prs.co/485603).

---

## 6.5 Validations and Substitutions

In **SAP S/4HANA**, you use **validations** to perform checks on user-entered data. This helps prevent erroneous postings by creating standard checks for entered data.

## 6.5 Validations and Substitutions

**Substitutions** are meant to either fill **fields** left blank or change entries in fields filled with values different from those defined in the substitution rules. In this chapter, we analyze how to define **validation** and **substitution rules**, and how to maintain sets and rules used in their definitions.

---

### 6.5.1 Overview of Validations and Substitutions

**Validations** and **substitutions** can be defined for multiple application areas (see Figure 6.34). The most relevant areas for a **financial accounting consultant** are:

- **Financial Accounting**
- **Asset Accounting**
- **Cost Accounting**

The focus here and in the certification is on **financial accounting**.

Validations and substitutions are valid for specific **callup points** (shown in Figures 6.34 and 6.35). Important callup points to remember are:

- **Document header**  
  Fields checked or substituted belong to the **document header** (table BKPF) and **system fields** (SYST), such as the system date. The logic is based on fields known from the completed header section.
  
- **Line Item**  
  Validation or substitution occurs at the line item level. You can evaluate fields from the header, system fields, and other line-item fields (table BSEG).
  
- **Complete document**  
  Used to check or substitute fields in both header and line item. Useful when line items must be entered to check or change header details, or to handle automatically generated line items (e.g., tax items) or multiple line items together (e.g., total posted amount).

To use a validation or substitution, assign it to the **company code** in **Customizing** (see Figure 6.35). 

You can assign a single validation/substitution per company code and callup point. For each validation/substitution, define the **activation level**:

- **0: Inactive**  
  The system performs no validation/substitution; equivalent to not having the line in the maintenance table.
  
- **1: Active**  
  The system performs the validation/substitution for each journal entry.
  
- **2: Active, no batch input**  
  The system performs validation/substitution for manual journal entries only; not for batch processes like data migration.

When defining validations/substitutions, multiple steps can be defined. The system processes each step sequentially at the callup point.

- For **validations**, the system raises the **first message** found.
- For **substitutions**, all changes are performed without user intervention.

**Note:**  
If the first validation message is a **warning** and the user ignores it, the system continues through subsequent steps and messages. The system does not display all validation problems in a single output; each must be addressed sequentially.

---

#### Example Validation Step (Figure 6.36)

A validation step refers to a specific **validation rule** (e.g., **OC-BUK**) made up of:

- **Prerequisite**  
  Defines whether the validation is executed. Example: Validation runs if the user making the journal entry is **SCHMIDTK** or **MUELLERP**.
  
- **Check**  
  The validation condition. The step activates if this check is **not fulfilled**. Example: Validate that the document type is different from **SA**. If document type ≠ SA, no message is generated.
  
- **Message**  
  If the check fails, the system generates an **error message** (Z1 021), which reads: "Do not use document type SA."

This validation ensures the two specified users cannot post with document type **SA**.

---

### 6.5.2 Substitution Definition

Substitutions use a **rule** to change the value of a field, regardless of whether it is already filled or empty. A substitution is stronger than manual entry or a default value—it will always be performed if the **prerequisite** is met.

Substitutions can fill fields not visible on the screen; the system writes values directly to Document Header or Line Item fields as defined.

**Warning:**  
Substitutions can contradict validations or normal journal entry checks, potentially causing errors. Solutions include:

- Change the posting to allow the value
- Change the validation or system check message
- Change the substitution step

---

#### Example Substitution Step (Figure 6.37)

- When the document type is **SA**, fill the **document reference field** with the **system date**.

To define such a step:

1. Create a new step within the substitution assigned to the company code at the **Document Header callup point**.
2. Select the field(s) to substitute (popup screen, Figure 6.38).
3. Select the substitution method (Figure 6.39):

   - **Constant value:** Enter a fixed value.
   - **Exit:** Use user exit for custom ABAP code.
   - **Field - Field assignment:** Use another field's value (no combination of field values allowed).

---

#### Building Prerequisites (Figure 6.40)

The **formula builder**:

- Guides you in writing syntactically correct prerequisite code.
- Allows field selection valid for the callup point.
- Has a list of operators (equal to, greater than, different from).
- Operands include:
  
  - **Constant:** Fixed value  
  - **FldComp. (field comparison):** Specify part of a table field (e.g., first 3 chars of general ledger account)  
  - **Comments:** For information/maintenance  
  - **Set directory:** Group of values for a field (e.g., set of G/L accounts starting with 123)

When entering constants, if the field has a list of valid values, you must select from them (Figure 6.41).

---

#### Assigning Substitution Values

- For field-to-field substitution, select the reference field from which the value is copied (Figure 6.42).
- The system updates the target field with the reference field's value when the prerequisite is met (Figure 6.43).

---

### 6.5.3 Validation Definition

Validation steps include an extra **check** stage compared to substitutions and output **messages** instead of changing field values.

---

#### Example Validation Setup (Figure 6.44)

If the **general ledger account** and **cost centers** belong to specific sets, the system checks that the **internal order** field is filled.

- If internal order is empty, an **error message** is issued.

Prerequisites and checks are built using the same **formula editor** tool as substitutions.

You select the **message class** where validation messages originate. In each step:

- Assign an existing message or create a new one.
- Message types include:

  - **Cancel:** Forces exit from journal entry screen.
  - **Error:** Forces user to correct field values.
  - **Warning:** User can skip, but not recommended.
  - **Information:** Informs user of details.

---

#### Message Variables and Workflow

You can assign up to **four field variables** for message texts to provide detailed explanations.

Example:

- Message:  
  *"With the combination G/L Account & and Cost Center &, you must enter an internal order."*
  
- Message variables might be:  
  - **BSEG-SAKNR** (general ledger account)  
  - **BSEG-KOSTL** (cost center)  
  
The system outputs user-entered values for these fields in messages.

The final option in message assignment is the **Trigger Workflow** indicator.

## Chapter 6 Organizational Assignments and Process Integration

---

### 6.5.4 Sets Definition

**Sets** are used to group together values for specific dimensions. To define a set, you enter a **name (Set Name)** and reference a specific system table (e.g., **Table ACDOCA**), as shown in Figure 6.47. Then you select a **Set type**. You can also reference an existing set (**Reference Set**) to speed up the set definition.

In the **Basic Set**, you define value ranges for a specific field (Figure 6.48). This makes it easier to include ranges of data in validations and substitutions.

You can also combine sets of different characteristics in **multisets** for cross-characteristic validations (Figure 6.49).

---

### 6.5.5 Rules Definition

You can think of a **rule** as a **validation/substitution function module**. It’s a piece of code logic that you can embed into validation/substitution prerequisites and validation checks. Instead of writing the logic in the validation, you create a **rule** with the same exact logic.

Advantages of using rules:
- Assign the same rule to multiple steps instead of rewriting it every time.
- Keep prerequisites/checks cleaner when dealing with complex logic.

On its own, a rule doesn’t do anything; it must be embedded in a **prerequisite** or **check** to be useful (Figure 6.50).

---

## 6.6 Data Archiving

With **data archiving** in an **SAP S/4HANA system**, you can remove application data from the database that no longer needs to be actively accessed for day-to-day activities. The data isn’t deleted; instead, it is transferred to **external storage media** for later access and analysis.

### Reasons to Archive Data
- Saves memory space and reduces related performance problems
- Keeps the database more manageable
- Ensures cost efficiency
- Enables faster downtime cycles for the system
- Allows access and reuse of archived data later

In Figure 6.51, you assign a **life** to the archiving object to avoid archiving data still in use. Financial accounting consultants advise and work with system administrators to configure archiving needs and the life of financial accounting archive objects.

When archiving, the system:
- Writes relevant data to an archive file
- Stores the archive file as configured
- Deletes archived data from the active database

---

### 6.6.1 General Customizing for Data Archiving

Data archiving configuration and execution are done by a **system administrator**.

Key configuration steps:
- **Storage locations:** Configure storage locations for archived files (Figure 6.52).
- **Cross-object Customizing:** Mostly admin configurations to ensure smooth archiving workflows. The **Data Archiving Monitor** tracks all archiving jobs and is usually active (Figure 6.53).

---

### 6.6.2 Object-Specific Customizing for Data Archiving

Using the **general ledger account** as an example, additional archiving objects for financial accounting are shown in Figure 6.54.

Settings for an accounting object include (Figure 6.55):
- **Logical File Name:** Maintain a logical file name.
- **Maximum Size in MB:** Define maximum archive file size.
- **Test Mode Variant/Live Mode Variant:** Create variants for test and production runs.
- **Start Automatically:** Option to execute deletion automatically after archive file creation.

---

### 6.6.3 Performing Data Archiving: General Ledger Account Example

To archive a **general ledger account**:
- Enter the **Life (number of days)** to keep a general ledger account per company code, account type, and account range (Figure 6.56).

Before executing archiving:
- Set the **Marked for Deletion** checkbox in both the **chart of accounts** and the **company code** (Figure 6.57). Blocking the account is recommended though not mandatory.

Use the **archive administration tool** (Figure 6.58) to process data archiving and create the archive file by following these steps:

1. **Create an archiving variant** (Figure 6.59): Define data to be archived, such as company code or chart of accounts data. Variants can be for **test runs** or **productive runs**. Define data logging for the run.
2. Specify the **execution user** with required authorizations.
3. Specify the **Start Date and Time**.
4. Define the **Spool Parameters** for log printout.

The system outputs job logs as defined (Figure 6.60). Logs can be selected for detailed viewing.

Figure 6.61 shows detailed archiving output confirming the general ledger account archived for the company code.

After archiving, the general ledger account is no longer defined for the company code (Figure 6.62). Deletion from the chart of accounts requires a separate run.

---

## 6.7 Data Aging

**Data aging** transfers data from the **in-memory** section of the database to traditional disk drives.

Though **SAP HANA** is an in-memory database, storing all data in memory is cost-prohibitive and not always viable due to hardware limits.

With **data aging**, data no longer needed for daily real-time processing can be moved to **traditional disk drives** (e.g., magnetic disks, tapes, SSDs).

Though data aging is primarily a **database function**, it is activated at the system level and configured per application data.

### Data Aging for Financial Accounting Documents

You define a **minimum life** per **account type** and **document type** determining how long documents remain in the **hot (current)** data layer.

When data aging runs:
- Documents beyond their configured life are moved to the **historic (cold) partition** of the database (Figure 6.63).

Data moved to the **cold partition** remains available for reporting but retrieving it may incur slower access speeds.

---

### 6.7.1 Data Aging Customizing

Configuration steps to enable **data aging**:

- Activate data aging in the **SAP HANA database** and **SAP S/4HANA system**.
- Enable the **DAAG_DATA_AGING** business function in the **business function switch framework** (Figure 6.64). This function is reversible.
- Assign appropriate user authorizations (**S_DAAG** and **S_DAGPTM**).
  
Two standard roles:
- **SAP_DAAG_ADMIN:** For system administrators.
- **SAP_DAAG_EXPERT:** For users responsible for scheduling aging runs.

For financial accounting, activate the **FI_DOCUMENT** data aging object (Figure 6.65).

Customize the document life per **Company Code** and **Account Type** (Figure 6.66). You can use an asterisk ("*") for settings valid across all company codes. The **Account Life** is set in days (up to four digits allowed).

## Data Aging Account Type Lives

You also configure the **document life** by **company code** and **document type**. For areas requiring more frequent access to **historic data**, a longer life is set. Here you can specify life in **days** and **years** (see Figure 6.67).

### Data Aging Requirements

To use **data aging**, you must:

- Activate **table partitioning**
- Set up at least **two partitions** to separate current and historic data

This is an **administrative task** shown in Figure 6.68.

### Data Aging Group Definition

- Define a **data aging group**
- Add multiple **objects** to run in a single data aging run
- Assign a **sequence number** and the **object** (e.g., **FI_DOCUMENT** as in Figure 6.69)

---

## 6.7.2 Data Aging Run

Once configured, you can perform the first **data aging run**:

- In the application, select **schedule a new run**
- Define **User Name** and **Group** (see Figure 6.70)
- Schedule **Start Date** and printing details (**Spool Parameters**)
- Monitor success by refreshing the view and reviewing the **log**

### Additional Monitoring

- Special **SAP Fiori dashboards** exist for monitoring data aging groups and objects
- Without **SAP ILM**, use the **data browser** to check entries in the **Universal Journal table (ACDOCA)**
- The **Data Filter Value for Data Aging** field uses the **posting date** as a timestamp
- Lines with this field filled are **aged** and moved to the **historic partition** (Figure 6.71)

---

## 6.8 Important Terminology

This section defines key terminology used in the chapter:

- **Application area**: Basis for validation and substitution creation; maps to SAP S/4HANA components (e.g., **financial accounting**, **controlling**).
- **Archiving object**: Specifies data to archive and how; preconfigured due to process sensitivity.
- **Archive variant**: Parameters for running the archiving, including test vs. productive runs and log types.
- **Bank directory**: List of all banks in the SAP S/4HANA client; banks must be here to assign to business partners.
- **Bank group**: Groups banks for payment process selection of the **house bank**.
- **Callup point**: Timing and area of validation/substitution evaluation (e.g., **Document Header**, **Line Item**).
- **Current partition**: In-memory partition of SAP HANA tables; also called **hot data storage**.
- **Data aging**: Transfers data from in-memory to slower disk storage to free memory for active data.
- **Data archiving**: Removes old data from active DB, transfers to external media for future retrieval.
- **Formula editor**: Tool for creating Boolean logic strings used in validations and substitutions.
- **Held document**: Incomplete journal entry saved by user without assigned number.
- **Historical partition**: Slower disk-based partition of SAP HANA tables; also called **cold data storage**.
- **House bank**: Bank defined as a business partner connected with bank accounts.
- **Organizational object**: Used for organizational plan creation and workflow processing; types include
  - Organizational unit
  - Position
  - Job
  - Work center
  - Task
- **Parked document**: Incomplete document with a system-assigned number; appears in some reports and processes.
- **Release approval path**: Defines which HR organizational unit processes workflow items by company code, document type, amount, and release group.
- **Release group**: Business partner grouping to assign different release approval paths.
- **Rules**: Common logic strings used in validation and substitution steps for prerequisites and checks.
- **SAP Business Workflow**: Enables design and execution of workflows in SAP S/4HANA.
- **Sets**: Flexible groupings of characteristic values and key figures, assignable in validation/substitution steps.
- **Substitutions**: Rules to modify entered or blank field values during transactions.
- **Subworkflow**: Defines detail such as number of release levels in workflows; multiple subworkflows possible.
- **Validations**: Custom checks for values/combinations during business transactions.
- **Workflow**: Tool for automating multi-step business processes and defining workflow framework.
- **Workflow variant**: Assigned at company code level; defines activation of workflow for document parking.

---

## 6.9 Practice Questions

These practice questions support self-assessment of chapter topics, resembling certification exam style.

1. **When adding a bank to the bank directory, which field is required?**  
   - A. Company code  
   - B. Opening date  
   - C. Currency  
   - D. Country  

2. **On which level do you maintain the bank directory?**  
   - A. Bank area  
   - B. Company code  
   - C. Client  
   - D. Profit center  

3. **What is defined in the bank account connectivity path settings?**  
   - A. Payment approvers for workflows  
   - B. Business partner assigned to the bank  
   - C. House bank account ID details  
   - D. Relevant profit center and segment  

4. **When creating a bank as a business partner, what roles are assigned by default?** (Three correct answers)  
   - A. Customer  
   - B. Supplier  
   - C. General  
   - D. Financial Services  
   - E. Bank  

5. **What are the differences between holding and parking documents?** (Two correct answers)  
   - A. Held document has no document number assigned  
   - B. Held document can be incomplete  
   - C. Parked document can trigger workflow processes  
   - D. Parked document is considered for financial statements  

6. **On which level is the document parking workflow variant assigned?**  
   - A. Company  
   - B. Company code  
   - C. Business partner  
   - D. Profit center  

7. **How can you differentiate document parking workflow on the business partner level?**  
   - A. Assign different workflow release groups  
   - B. Assign different payment methods  
   - C. Assign different business partner groupings  
   - D. Assign different responsible organization units  

8. **True or False: Subworkflows define the number of release levels in the document parking workflow process.**  
   - A. True  
   - B. False  

9. **What options does a processor have for a general journal entry submitted for verification?** (Three correct answers)  
   - A. Park  
   - B. Approve  
   - C. Delete  
   - D. Reject  
   - E. Suspend  

10. **Which values can be prerequisites for triggering the general journal entry verification workflow?** (Three correct answers)  
    - A. Account group  
    - B. Target company code  
    - C. Cost center  
    - D. Source company code  
    - E. Profit center  

11. **Why choose the document parking workflow for journal entry verification over general verification?**  
    - A. You do not use SAP Fiori  
    - B. You need to define two-level verification  
    - C. You’re running SAP S/4HANA 1610  
    - D. You don’t know how to configure the new functionality  

12. **What are the basic definitions for validations?** (Three correct answers)  
    - A. Prerequisite  
    - B. Check  
    - C. Rule  
    - D. Set  
    - E. Message  

13. **At which levels can validations and substitutions for financial accounting be defined?** (Three correct answers)  
    - A. Line item  
    - B. System data  
    - C. Universal Journal  
    - D. Complete document  
    - E. Header  

14. **True or False: A single substitution step can substitute multiple fields in a document.**  
    - A. True  
    - B. False  

15. **True or False: Multisets can be created only if they combine data from basic sets grouping the same characteristic.**  
    - A. True  
    - B. False  

16. **What is the main motivation for creating rules for substitutions and validations?**  
    - A. Simpler definition tools  
    - B. Reuse in multiple steps  
    - C. Not bound by Boolean logic  
    - D. Additional fields available  

17. **What are the steps in Customizing data archiving?** (Three correct answers)  
    - A. Define archiving storage locations  
    - B. Perform cross-object Customizing  
    - C. Define table partitions  
    - D. Activate data aging objects  
    - E. Perform object-specific Customizing  

18. **What is a reason for performing data archiving?**  
    - A. To have fewer downtime cycles  
    - B. To control hardware requirements  
    - C. To protect data from being lost  
    - D. To back up data on a separate drive  

19. **True or False: Deleting a general ledger account for a company code allows removing it from the chart of accounts.**  
    - A. True  
    - B. False  

20. **True or False: Data aging is executed separately for each data aging object.**  
    - A. True  
    - B. False  

21. **Which is a difference between data aging and data archiving?**  
    - A. Data aging allows retrieval of aged data for analysis  
    - B. Data aging frees up memory space  
    - C. Data archiving removes data from the database  
    - D. Data archiving has advanced logging capabilities  

22. **On which levels can you maintain useful life for documents of a company code in the context of data aging?**  

## 6.10 Practice Question Answers and Explanations

1. **Correct answer: D**  
You must define the **country**, **bank code**, and **bank name** when defining a new bank. The details for **company code** are maintained on the **house bank** level and **bank account** level. The **opening date** and **currency** are maintained per bank account.

2. **Correct answer: C**  
**Banks** are defined on the **client level** and are assigned to a **country**. Because many **company codes**, **customers**, and **suppliers** may use the same banks, it makes sense they are defined at the highest level.

3. **Correct answer: C**  
The **connectivity path** is where you define the connection between a **bank account** and the **house bank**. The **business partner** is defined in the bank details, **payment approvers** in the bank account signatory details, and the **profit center** and **segment** in the account additional details.

4. **Correct answers: C, D, E**  
The correct answers are the **bank role**, the **financial services role**, and the **general role**. The **general role** is always assigned; you can't create a business partner without it. No **customer** or **supplier reconciliation account** is assigned when creating a bank, so these roles don't appear in the business partner master record.

5. **Correct answers: A, C**  
**Held documents** don’t receive a document number (though the user assigns an identifier). Only **document parking** is integrated with **SAP Business Workflow**. Both **parked** and **held documents** can be saved incomplete and are not included in financial statements.

6. **Correct answer: B**  
You assign the **workflow variant** to each **company code**. You can view this in the global settings for the company code (Transaction **OBY6** in **SAP Easy Access**).

7. **Correct answer: A**  
You assign the **workflow release group** in the company code details of the **business partner roles** for **financial accounting customers** and **suppliers** to control release strategy separately.

8. **Correct answer: A**  
True. The **subworkflow** defines special workflow characteristics such as the number of **release levels**. It can differentiate approvers based on different amounts.

9. **Correct answers: B, D, E**  
As a processor, you can **approve** or **reject** the document entry. **Suspend** means putting a journal entry "in waiting." **Delete** is rare in **SAP S/4HANA** documents. **Park** is similar to suspend but not the correct term here.

10. **Correct answers: A, C, D**  
Correct answers are **account group**, **source company code**, and **cost center**. The **threshold value** is also used. The **profit center** acts as a distractor since it mirrors the cost center; **target company code** is less effective as a distractor.

11. **Correct answer: A**  
The **general journal entry verification** requires **SAP Fiori**. Delivered workflow is single-step, but custom two-level verification processes can be created.

12. **Correct answers: A, B, E**  
A **prerequisite** must be fulfilled for the system to perform checks if the validation is true. The defined **message** is raised if the check fails. **Rules** and **sets** define prerequisites and checks.

13. **Correct answers: A, D, E**  
Each **validation** and **substitution** is defined for a specific **callup point**. The same validation/substitution cannot be used for two different callup points. For financial accounting, these are at the **Document Header**, **Line Item**, or **Complete Document** level.

14. **Correct answer: A**  
True. A single step can fulfill multiple **substitution prerequisites**, enabling multiple field changes without direct field dependency assignments.

15. **Correct answer: B**  
False. **Multisets** combine any basic sets regardless of characteristics. The statement describes a **single set**, which combines basic sets for the same attribute.

16. **Correct answer: B**  
You can reuse **rules** in multiple validation/substitution steps to save time. The tools, fields, and logic are the same as those used for prerequisites and checks.

17. **Correct answers: A, B, E**  
**Customizing steps sequence**:  
- Define **archiving storage locations**  
- Perform **cross-object Customizing**  
- Customize **object-specific settings**  
**Table partitioning** and **aging object activation** are part of data aging activation.

18. **Correct answer: B**  
Data archiving helps maintain stable **hardware requirements** by keeping the database size constant. It shortens downtime cycles but does not reduce the number of downtimes. Data is never lost, and archiving is not data backup.

19. **Correct answer: B**  
False. Deleting a **general ledger account** requires deletion from all **company codes** first. Deletion in **SAP S/4HANA** follows many dependency and consistency checks.

20. **Correct answer: B**  
False. You create **object groups** combining multiple aging objects for sequential processing, which simplifies and improves aging run administration.

21. **Correct answer: C**  
**Archiving** physically removes data from the database, whereas **data aging** moves data to a historical partition. Both preserve data retrieval and reduce memory usage, offering logs to check processing results.

22. **Correct answers: A, B**  
**Aging Customizing** controls useful life per **company code** and **account type**, allowing different retention periods for various document types (e.g., general ledger vs asset accounting).

---

## 6.11 Test Takeaway

You now understand how to create and manage **banks**, **house banks**, and **bank accounts** in the **SAP S/4HANA** system. You can use **document parking**, configure and use the **workflow** for parked document approval and finalization.

You can configure and use the **general journal entry verification** applications and workflow. You can control document posting with **validations** and **substitutions**, using **sets** and **rules** in control definitions.

Collaboration with an administrator for **archiving configuration** and participation in data archiving projects is possible. Configuration of **data aging** for documents posted to the **Universal Journal** frees memory space for real-time analysis of critical data.

---

## 6.12 Summary

This chapter covered cross topics in **financial accounting** beyond **bank account management**, including **SAP Cash Management**, **document parking**, **general journal entry verification**, **validation and substitution**, **archiving**, and **data aging**.

These topics are essential knowledge for a **financial accounting consultant** regardless of specific project focus. This concludes the final chapter and completes the diverse knowledge required to pass the **financial accounting certification exam** in **SAP S/4HANA**.

Mastering this material and confidently answering practice questions will lead to success in certification. This book aims to serve as a clear reference beyond certification attainment.

## The Author

**Stefanos Pougkas** is the **certification exam owner** for the **1909** and **2020 exams** and has led the design and writing of questions for these exams.

At **SAP Training and Adoption**, Stefanos is part of the **learning architect team** for digital core applications, responsible for the **financials curriculum**. He is a **subject matter expert** for financials courses and lead moderator in the global **SAP Financials Learning Room**.

---
